ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS
I am grateful to all my lovely clients who, over the last three decades, honored me with their
brave vulnerability and authenticity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 21 (Number of characters: 161):
Their stories verified to me that there is an epidemic of poor
parenting, and their inspiring work proved to me that the effects of it could be largely overcome.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 22 (Number of characters: 224):
I am also grateful to the readers of my first book and to my website respondents whose
generous feedback greatly alleviated my performance anxiety about writing another book and
putting my words out there for public viewing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 23 (Number of characters: 143):
Their overwhelmingly positive support
ameliorates the fear that my words will be used as weapons against me as they so often were in
childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 24 (Number of characters: 89):
I am grateful to my good friend Bill O’Brien who gave me invaluable editorial assistance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 25 (Number of characters: 152):
I am grateful to all those writers listed in the Bibliography, and those unlisted, whose ideas
have fertilized my mind and helped me to write this book.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 26 (Number of characters: 162):

commiseration. We have aided each other greatly in our journeys of recovery.

chunk 33 (Number of characters: 124):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 34 (Number of characters: 84):
Forty years ago, I was riding on a train in India travelling from Delhi to Calcutta.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 35 (Number of characters: 64):
I was at
the end of a failed, yearlong spiritual quest in India.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 36 (Number of characters: 96):
Instead of enlightenment, my salvation
fantasy had only netted me despair and amoebic dysentery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 37 (Number of characters: 86):
The latter cost me thirty pounds of
flesh, and left me looking like an emaciated monk.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 38 (Number of characters: 118):
Even worse was the absolute loss of the hope that had been inflamed by reading Walt
Whitman’s “Song of the Open Road.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 39 (Number of characters: 119):
This hope had supported me through five years of world
travel after I was unceremoniously kicked out of my family home.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 40 (Number of characters: 23):
But, back to the train.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 41 (Number of characters: 139):
I was sitting in my cramped second class seat with the untouchables,
chickens and goats, reading an English version of an Indian newspaper.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 42 (Number of characters: 153):
The paper informed me
that my destination, Calcutta, was now inundated with 100,000 refugees from Bangladesh who
had just fled their flood–swamped homes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 43 (Number of characters: 155):
They were all apparently sleeping on the downtown
streets in the recesses beneath the protruding second floors of all the buildings that lined the
streets.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 44 (Number of characters: 127):
I came in late at night and sure enough, sleeping bodies wrapped in sheets, shoulder to
shoulder, lined the streets everywhere.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 45 (Number of characters: 85):
I checked into a twenty cents-a-night hotel that a fellow
traveler had told me about.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 46 (Number of characters: 74):
I slept unevenly, dreading the sight that I would behold the next
morning.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 47 (Number of characters: 93):
How would I handle viewing masses of desperate people, especially when I had
nothing to give?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 48 (Number of characters: 107):
I doubted that I even had enough money to make it to Australia where I could
hopefully replenish my wallet.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 49 (Number of characters: 121):
When I finally nudged myself down the stairs late the next morning, I was aghast at the
transformed scene on the streets.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 50 (Number of characters: 79):
Sheets had been spread out like picnic blankets and each hosted
happy families.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 51 (Number of characters: 54):
Little portable stoves produced meals and cups of tea.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 52 (Number of characters: 80):
People bantered with
incredible vitality and enthusiasm, and children...children

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 53 (Number of characters: 195):
[this was the part that emblazoned on
my memory] crawled all over their parents, especially their fathers in affectionate playful
gymnastics that their fathers seemed to love as much as they did.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 54 (Number of characters: 137):
I was flooded with a mélange of feelings unlike anything I’d ever experienced before - a
strange cocktail of relief, delight and anxiety.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 55 (Number of characters: 138):
The anxiety I wouldn’t understand until ten years

later when I realized that envy had been percolating below the surface of my awareness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 56 (Number of characters: 116):
I was deeply envious of this gorgeous buffet of familial love that I had never experienced or
even witnessed before.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 57 (Number of characters: 183):
The family sitcoms – even the syrupy sweet ones - that I had watched
growing up came nowhere near creating such an authentic, tactile representation of healthy
bonding and attachment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 58 (Number of characters: 265):
When I realized what this was years later as an anthropology and social work student, I
positively flashed back to other non-industrial countries where I had seen similar scenes on a less
grand level: Morocco, Thailand, Bali, and an Aboriginal reserve in Australia.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 59 (Number of characters: 128):
These memories also viscerally informed me about the kind of relational love I had never
seen in my own or my friends’ families.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 60 (Number of characters: 362):
As I digested this experience over the years and used it
to overcome my denial about what I had missed out on as a child, I began the decades long quest
that has lead me to write this book as well as The Tao of Fully Feeling, which precedes it. The
Tao of Fully Feeling is a companion to this book and elaborates many of the foundational
principles of this book.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 61 (Number of characters: 132):
This book then is my hopeful effort to create a map that you can follow to heal the wounds
that come from not enough childhood love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 62 (Number of characters: 247):
If I am a bit repetitive at times about issues like
shrinking the critic and grieving the losses of childhood, it is my attempt to find different ways to
emphasize the great importance of engaging these themes of recovery work over and over again.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 63 (Number of characters: 124):
If you find yourself lost and not sure of how to get back onto the map, these themes will always
be key portals for reentry.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 64 (Number of characters: 115):
I sometimes recommend that readers view the table of contents and start with whatever headings
most strike a chord.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 65 (Number of characters: 784):
Although the book is laid out in a somewhat linear fashion, everyone’s
journey of recovering is different, and journeys can be initiated in a variety of ways. Journeys of recovering may begin when a death or great loss brings up an emotional storm
that opens up a hidden reservoir of childhood pain; or when a friend shares something about his
or her recovery process that strikes a chord; or when a book or TV show triggers a more serious
consideration of what really happened in childhood; or when something gets “opened up” in
couple’s therapy; or when a healing crisis in the form of panic attacks or a nervous breakdown
requires some outside help; or when the self-medicating strategies developed to soothe
depression and anxiety get out of control and also require outside help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 66 (Number of characters: 252):
I hope that readers will be able to use this book as a textbook for recovering, and that
certain sections will call you back or forward to them repeatedly, as over time and with effective
work, certain themes continue to take on ever deepening meaning.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 67 (Number of characters: 219):
In this vein, you will find that the Table of Contents is quite comprehensive, and sometimes
the best way to use this book is to browse through it and then read the sections and chapters that
most capture your interest.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 68 (Number of characters: 65):
Moreover, this is not a one size fits all formula for recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 69 (Number of characters: 143):
Depending on the specific
pattern of your childhood trauma, some of the advice contained herein may be less relevant or
even irrelevant to you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 70 (Number of characters: 75):
Please then focus on the material that seems applicable and helpful to
you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 71 (Number of characters: 272):
I also hope this map will guide you to heal in a way that helps you become an unflinching source
of kindness and self-compassion for yourself, and that out of that journey you will find at least
one other human being who will reciprocally love you well enough in that way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 72 (Number of characters: 66):
Finally I have illustrated this work with many real life examples.

chunk 74 (Number of characters: 167):
PART 1
AN OVERVIEW OF RECOVERING

THE JOURNEY OF RECOVERING FROM CPTSD
I wrote this book from the perspective of someone who has Complex Post-Traumatic Stress
Disorder

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 75 (Number of characters: 78):
[Cptsd], and who has experienced a great reduction of symptoms over the years.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 76 (Number of characters: 141):
I also
wrote it from the viewpoint of someone who has discovered many silver linings in the long,
windy, bumpy road of recovering from Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 77 (Number of characters: 94):
I have also seen this type of recovering in a
number of my friends and many long term clients.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 78 (Number of characters: 33):
First, the good news about Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 79 (Number of characters: 99):
It is a learned set of responses, and a failure to complete
numerous important developmental tasks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 80 (Number of characters: 63):
This means that it is environmentally, not genetically,
caused.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 81 (Number of characters: 109):
In other words, unlike most of the diagnoses it is confused with, it is neither inborn nor
characterological.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 82 (Number of characters: 23):
As such, it is learned.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 83 (Number of characters: 32):
It is not inscribed in your DNA.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 84 (Number of characters: 34):
It is a disorder caused
by nurture

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 85 (Number of characters: 38):
[or rather the lack of it] not nature.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 86 (Number of characters: 85):
This is especially good news because what is learned can be unlearned and vice versa.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 87 (Number of characters: 81):
What
was not provided by your parents can now be provided by yourself and others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 88 (Number of characters: 80):
Recovery from Cptsd typically has important self-help and relational components.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 89 (Number of characters: 132):
The
relational piece can come from authors, friends, partners, teachers, therapists, therapeutic groups
or any combination of these.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 90 (Number of characters: 45):
I like to call this reparenting by committee.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 91 (Number of characters: 245):
I must emphasize, however, that some survivors of Cptsdengendering families were so
thoroughly betrayed by their parents, that it may be a long time, if ever, before they can trust
another human being enough to engage in relational healing work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 92 (Number of characters: 110):
When this is the case, pets,
books and online therapeutic websites can provide significant relational healing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 93 (Number of characters: 61):
This book describes a multimodal treatment approach to Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 94 (Number of characters: 139):
It is oriented toward the most
prevalent kind of Cptsd, the kind that comes from growing up in a severely abusive and/or
neglectful family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 95 (Number of characters: 282):
In this vein, the book describes a journey of healing the damage that occurs

when you suffer traumatizing abuse and abandonment. Traumatizing abuse and abandonment
can occur on verbal, emotional, spiritual, and/or physical levels. Moreover, sexual abuse is
especially traumatizing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 96 (Number of characters: 60):
I believe that we have an epidemic of traumatizing families.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 97 (Number of characters: 244):
Current estimates posit that one
in three girls and one in five boys are sexually abused before they enter adulthood, and recent
statistics from The Kim Foundation report that 26% of Americans over 18 have been diagnosed
with a mental disorder.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 98 (Number of characters: 100):
When abuse or neglect is severe enough, any one category of it can cause the child to
develop Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 99 (Number of characters: 110):
This is true even in the case of emotional neglect if both parents collude in it, as
we will see in chapter 5.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 100 (Number of characters: 90):
When abuse and neglect is multidimensional, the severity of the Cptsd
worsens accordingly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 101 (Number of characters: 89):
Definition Of Complex PTSD
Cptsd is a more severe form of Post-traumatic stress disorder.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 102 (Number of characters: 589):
It is delineated from this better
known trauma syndrome by five of its most common and troublesome features: emotional
flashbacks, toxic shame, self-abandonment, a vicious inner critic and social anxiety. Emotional flashbacks are perhaps the most noticeable and characteristic feature of Cptsd. Survivors of traumatizing abandonment are extremely susceptibility to painful emotional
flashbacks, which unlike ptsd do not typically have a visual component. Emotional flashbacks are sudden and often prolonged regressions to the overwhelming
feeling-states of being an abused/abandoned child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 103 (Number of characters: 98):
These feeling states can include
overwhelming fear, shame, alienation, rage, grief and depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 104 (Number of characters: 71):
They also include unnecessary
triggering of our fight/flight instincts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 105 (Number of characters: 163):
It is important to state here that emotional flashbacks, like most things in life, are not all-or-
none. Flashbacks can range in intensity from subtle to horrific.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 106 (Number of characters: 131):
They can also vary in duration
ranging from moments to weeks on end where they devolve into what many therapists call a
regression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 107 (Number of characters: 135):
Finally, a more clinical and extensive definition of Cptsd can be found on p. 121 of Judith
Herman’s seminal book, Trauma and Recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 108 (Number of characters: 192):
An Example Of An Emotional Flashback
As I write this I recall the first emotional flashback I was ever able to identify, although I did not
identify it until about ten years after it occurred.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 109 (Number of characters: 69):
At the time of the event, I was living with my
first serious partner.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 110 (Number of characters: 143):
The honeymoon phase of our relationship came to a screeching halt when
she unexpectedly started yelling at me for something I no longer recall.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 111 (Number of characters: 55):
What I do most vividly recall was how the yelling felt.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 112 (Number of characters: 31):
It felt like a fierce hot wind.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 113 (Number of characters: 111):
I felt
like I was being blown away – like my insides were being blown out, as a flame on a candle is
blown out.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 114 (Number of characters: 121):
Later, when I first heard about auras, I flashed back to this and felt like my aura had been
completely stripped from me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 115 (Number of characters: 136):
At the time itself, I also felt completely disoriented, unable to speak, respond or even think. I felt terrified, shaky and very little.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 116 (Number of characters: 124):
Somehow, I finally managed to totter to the door and get out

of the house where I eventually slowly pulled myself together.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 117 (Number of characters: 135):
As I said earlier, it took me ten years to figure out that this confusing and disturbing
phenomenon was an intense emotional flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 118 (Number of characters: 77):
Some years later, I came to understand the
nature of this type of regression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 119 (Number of characters: 167):
I realized it was a flashback to the hundreds of times my
mother, in full homicidal visage, blasted me with her rage into terror, shame, dissociation and
helplessness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 120 (Number of characters: 330):
Emotional flashbacks are also accompanied by intense arousals of the fight/flight instinct, along
with hyperarousal of the sympathetic nervous system, the half of the nervous system that
controls arousal and activation. When fear is the dominant emotion in a flashback the person
feels extremely anxious, panicky or even suicidal.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 121 (Number of characters: 305):
When despair predominates, a sense of
profound numbness, paralysis and desperation to hide may occur. A sense of feeling small, young, fragile, powerless and helpless is also commonly
experienced in an emotional flashback, and all symptoms are typically overlaid with humiliating
and crushing toxic shame.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 122 (Number of characters: 261):
Toxic Shame: The Veneer Of An Emotional Flashback
Toxic shame, explored enlighteningly by John Bradshaw in Healing The Shame That Binds,
obliterates a Cptsd survivor’s self-esteem with an overwhelming sense that he is loathsome, ugly,
stupid, or fatally flawed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 123 (Number of characters: 146):
Overwhelming self-disdain is typically a flashback to the way he felt
when suffering the contempt and visual skewering of his traumatizing parent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 124 (Number of characters: 75):
Toxic shame can
also be created by constant parental neglect and rejection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 125 (Number of characters: 158):
Early in my career I worked with David, a handsome, intelligent man who was a
professional actor. One day David came to see me after an unsuccessful audition.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 126 (Number of characters: 94):
Beside himself,
he burst out: “I never let on to anyone, but I know that I’m really very ugly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 127 (Number of characters: 79):
It is so stupid that
I’m trying to be an actor when I’m so painful to look at.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 128 (Number of characters: 160):
I will never forget how shocked and
disbelieving I felt at first, that such a handsome person could feel ugly, but further exploration
brought me understanding.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 129 (Number of characters: 72):
David’s childhood was characterized by broad spectrum abuse and neglect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 130 (Number of characters: 244):
He was the last
and unwanted child of a large family, and his alcoholic father repeatedly attacked and looked at
him with disgust. To make matters worse, his family imitated his father and frequently
humiliated him with heavy doses of contempt.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 131 (Number of characters: 103):
His older brother’s favorite gibe, accompanied by
a nauseated grimace, was “I can’t stand sight of you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 132 (Number of characters: 27):
You make me want to vomit!”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 133 (Number of characters: 67):
Toxic shame can obliterate your self-esteem in the blink of an eye.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 134 (Number of characters: 150):
In an emotional flashback
you can regress instantly into feeling and thinking that you are as worthless and contemptible as
your family perceived you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 135 (Number of characters: 414):
When you are stranded in a flashback, toxic shame devolves into the
intensely painful alienation of the abandonment mélange - a roiling morass of shame, fear and
depression. The abandonment mélange is the fear and toxic shame that surrounds and interacts with the
abandonment depression. The abandonment depression itself is the deadened feeling of
helplessness and hopelessness that afflicts traumatized children.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 136 (Number of characters: 62):
Toxic shame also inhibits us from seeking comfort and support.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 137 (Number of characters: 165):
In a reenactment of the
childhood abandonment we are flashing back to, we often isolate ourselves and helplessly
surrender to an overwhelming feeling of humiliation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 138 (Number of characters: 117):
If you are stuck viewing yourself as worthless, defective, or despicable, you are probably in
an emotional flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 139 (Number of characters: 87):
This is typically also true when you are lost in self-hate and virulent
self-criticism.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 140 (Number of characters: 280):
Immediate help for managing emotional flashbacks can be found at the beginning
of chapter 8 which lists 13 practical steps for resolving flashbacks. Numerous clients and respondents to my website tell me that the concept of emotional flashback
brings them a great sense of relief.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 141 (Number of characters: 93):
They report that for the first time they are able to make some
sense of their troubled lives.

--------------------------------------------------

Suicidal Ideation

Suicidal Ideation
Suicidal ideation is a common phenomenon in Cptsd, particularly during intense or prolonged
flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 151 (Number of characters: 304):
Suicidal ideation is depressed thinking or fantasizing about wanting to die. It can
range from active suicidality to passive suicidality. Passive suicidality is far more common with the Cptsd survivors who I have known, and it
ranges from wishing you were dead to fantasizing about ways to end your life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 152 (Number of characters: 153):
When lost in
suicidal ideation, the survivor may even pray to be delivered from this life, or fantasize about
being taken by some calamitous act of fate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 153 (Number of characters: 110):
He may even think or obsess - without being serious
- of stepping in front of a car or jumping off a building.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 154 (Number of characters: 75):
Fantasy typically ends, however, without a serious intent to kill yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 155 (Number of characters: 429):
This is as opposed
to active suicidality where the person is actively proceeding in the direction of taking her life. I am discussing passive suicidality because it does not merit the same kind of alarm as
active suicidality. Passive suicidality is typically a flashback to early childhood when our
abandonment was so profound, that it was natural for us to wish that God or somebody or
something would just put an end to it all.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 156 (Number of characters: 183):
When the survivor catches himself in a suicidal reverie, he will benefit from seeing it both
as an emblem of how much pain he is in, and as a sign of a particularly intense flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 157 (Number of characters: 76):
This
then can direct him to use the flashback management steps in chapter 8.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 158 (Number of characters: 298):
If however, flashback management does not help, and suicidality becomes increasingly
active, 
please 
call 
the 
national 
suicide 
hot-line [1-800-273-8255] 
or 
visit
www.suicidepreventionlifeline.org, because this is a flashback that you may need help
managing, and you will get good help there.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 159 (Number of characters: 166):
Skilled therapists and caregivers learn to discriminate between active and passive suicidal
ideation, and do not panic and catastrophize when encountering the latter.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 160 (Number of characters: 428):
Instead, the counselor
invites the survivor to explore his suicidal thoughts and feelings knowing that in most cases,
verbal ventilation of the flashback pain underneath it will deconstruct the suicidality. In the much less common scenario of active suicidality, encouraging verbal ventilation will
also help the therapist or helper discern if there is indeed a real risk and if action needs to be
taken to protect the survivor.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 161 (Number of characters: 143):
What You May Have Been Misdiagnosed With
I once heard renowned traumatologist, John Briere, quip that if Cptsd were ever given its due,
the DSM

--------------------------------------------------

professionals would shrink from its dictionary like size to the size of a thin pamphlet.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 163 (Number of characters: 101):
In other
words, the role of traumatized childhoods in most adult psychological disorders is enormous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 164 (Number of characters: 100):

disorders.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 165 (Number of characters: 142):
Moreover, many are also unfairly and inaccurately labeled with bipolar, narcissistic,
codependent, autistic spectrum and borderline disorders.

sometimes co-occur with these disorders.]

[Attention Deficit Hyperactive

[see the 4F’s below].

of ADD

[Attention Deficit Disorder] and some depressive and dissociative disorders which

chunk 172 (Number of characters: 136):

and correlative with the disorders above.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 173 (Number of characters: 137):
The key point is that these labels are incomplete and
unnecessarily shaming descriptions of what the survivor is actually afflicted with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 174 (Number of characters: 89):
Reducing Cptsd to “panic disorder” is like calling food allergies chronically itchy eyes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 175 (Number of characters: 286):
Over-focusing treatment on the symptoms of panic in the former case and eye health in the latter
does little to get at root causes. Feelings of panic or itchiness in the eyes can be masked with
medication, but all the associated problems that cause these symptoms will remain untreated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 176 (Number of characters: 228):
Moreover, most of the diagnoses mentioned above are typically treated as innate
characterological defects rather than as learned maladaptations to stress – adaptations that
survivors were forced to learn as traumatized children.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 177 (Number of characters: 179):
And, most importantly, because these
adaptations were learned, they can often be extinguished or significantly diminished, and
replaced with more functional adaptations to stress.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 178 (Number of characters: 141):
In this vein, I believe that many substance and process addictions also begin as misguided,
maladaptations to parental abuse and abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 179 (Number of characters: 411):
They are early adaptations that are attempts
to soothe and distract from the mental, emotional and physical pain of Cptsd. Origins Of Cptsd
How do traumatically abused and/or abandoned children develop Cptsd? While the origin of Cptsd is most often associated with extended periods of physical and/or
sexual abuse in childhood, my observations convince me that ongoing verbal and emotional
abuse also causes it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 180 (Number of characters: 116):
Many dysfunctional parents react contemptuously to a baby or toddler’s plaintive call for
connection and attachment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 181 (Number of characters: 201):
Contempt is extremely traumatizing to a child, and at best, extremely
noxious to an adult. Contempt is a toxic cocktail of verbal and emotional abuse, a deadly amalgam of
denigration, rage and disgust.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 182 (Number of characters: 148):
Rage creates fear, and disgust creates shame in the child in a way
that soon teaches her to refrain from crying out, from ever asking for attention.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 183 (Number of characters: 205):
Before long, the
child gives up on seeking any kind of help or connection at all. The child’s bid for bonding and
acceptance is thwarted, and she is left to suffer in the frightened despair of abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 184 (Number of characters: 104):
Particularly abusive parents deepen the abandonment trauma by linking corporal
punishment with contempt.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 185 (Number of characters: 102):
Slaveholders and prison guards typically use contempt and scorn to
destroy their victims’ self-esteem.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 186 (Number of characters: 169):
Slaves, prisoners, and children, who are made to feel
worthless and powerless devolve into learned helplessness and can be controlled with far less
energy and attention.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 187 (Number of characters: 148):
Cult leaders also use contempt to shrink their followers into absolute
submission after luring them in with brief phases of fake unconditional love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 188 (Number of characters: 65):
Furthermore, Cptsd can also be caused by emotional neglect alone.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 189 (Number of characters: 50):
This key theme is explored at
length in chapter 5.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 190 (Number of characters: 180):
If you notice that you are berating yourself because your trauma seems
insignificant compared to others, please skip ahead to this chapter and resume reading here upon

completion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 191 (Number of characters: 96):
Emotional neglect also typically underlies most traumatizations that are more glaringly
evident.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 192 (Number of characters: 270):
Parents who routinely ignore or turn their backs on a child’s calls for attention,
connection or help, abandon their child to unmanageable amounts of fear, and the child
eventually gives up and succumbs to depressed, death-like feelings of helplessness and
hopelessness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 193 (Number of characters: 110):
These types of rejection simultaneously magnify the child’s fear, and eventually add a
coating of shame to it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 194 (Number of characters: 226):
Over time this fear and shame begets a toxic inner critic that holds the
child, and later the adult, totally responsible for his parents’ abandonment, until he becomes his
own worst enemy and descends into the bowels of Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 195 (Number of characters: 164):
More About Trauma
Trauma occurs when attack or abandonment triggers a fight/flight response so intensely that the
person cannot turn it off once the threat is over.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 196 (Number of characters: 176):
He becomes stuck in an adrenalized state. His
sympathetic nervous system is locked “on” and he cannot toggle into the relaxation function of
the parasympathetic nervous system.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 197 (Number of characters: 93):
One common instance of this occurs when a child is attacked and hurt by a bully after
school.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 198 (Number of characters: 201):
He may remain in a hypervigilant, fearful state until someone takes action to insure him
that he will not be revictimized, and until someone helps him release the hyperactivation in his
nervous system.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 199 (Number of characters: 173):
If the child has learned through experience that he can come to at least one of his parents
when he is hurting, frightened or needing help, he will tell mom or dad about it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 200 (Number of characters: 188):
With them, he
will grieve the temporary death of his sense of safety in the world by verbally ventilating, crying
and angering about it [chapter 11 expands on these processes of grieving].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 201 (Number of characters: 156):
Moreover, his parent will report the bully and take steps to assure that it will not happen
again, and the child will typically be released from the trauma.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 202 (Number of characters: 91):
He will naturally relax back into
the safety of parasympathetic nervous system functioning.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 203 (Number of characters: 103):
“Simple”, one incident traumas can often be resolved relatively easily if Cptsd is not
already present.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 204 (Number of characters: 265):
If however the bullying happens on numerous occasions and the child does not seek help, or
if the child lives in an environment so dangerous that the parent is powerless to ensure a
modicum of safety, it may take more than parental comforting to release the trauma.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 205 (Number of characters: 212):
If the
trauma is not too continuous over too long a time, a short course of therapy may be all that is
needed to resolve the trauma, provided of course the danger in the environment can effectively
be remediated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 206 (Number of characters: 168):
When the trauma however is repetitive and ongoing and no help is available, the child may
become so frozen in trauma that the symptoms of “simple” ptsd begin to set in.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 207 (Number of characters: 113):
This can also
occur during the prolonged trauma of combat or entrapment in a cult or domestic violence
situation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 208 (Number of characters: 197):
If however, a person is also afflicted by ongoing family abuse or profound emotional
abandonment, the trauma will manifest as a particularly severe emotional flashback because he
already has Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 209 (Number of characters: 58):
This is particularly true when his parent is also a bully.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 210 (Number of characters: 13):
The Four F’s:

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 211 (Number of characters: 245):
Fight, Flight, Freeze And Fawn
Earlier, I mentioned the fight/flight response that is an innate automatic response to danger in all
human beings. A more complete and accurate description of this instinct is the
fight/flight/freeze/fawn response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 212 (Number of characters: 109):
The complex nervous system wiring of this response allows a
person in danger to react in four different ways.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 213 (Number of characters: 100):
A fight response is triggered when a person suddenly responds aggressively to something
threatening.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 214 (Number of characters: 137):
A flight response is triggered when a person responds to a perceived threat by
fleeing, or symbolically, by launching into hyperactivity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 215 (Number of characters: 181):
A freeze response is triggered when a
person, realizing resistance is futile, gives up, numbs out into dissociation and/or collapses as if
accepting the inevitability of being hurt.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 216 (Number of characters: 144):
A fawn response is triggered when a person responds to
threat by trying to be pleasing or helpful in order to appease and forestall an attacker.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 217 (Number of characters: 75):
This
fourfold response potential will heretofore be referred to as the 4Fs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 218 (Number of characters: 305):
Traumatized children often over-gravitate to one of these response patterns to survive, and
as time passes these four modes become elaborated into entrenched defensive structures that are
similar to narcissistic [fight], obsessive/compulsive [flight], dissociative [freeze] or codependent
[fawn] defenses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 219 (Number of characters: 133):
These structures help children survive their horrific childhoods, but leave them very limited
and narrow in how they respond to life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 220 (Number of characters: 138):
Even worse, they remain locked in these patterns in
adulthood when they no longer need to rely so heavily on one primary response pattern.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 221 (Number of characters: 183):
It is important to understand that variances in the childhood abuse/neglect patterns, birth
order, and genetic predispositions result in people polarizing to their particular 4F type.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 222 (Number of characters: 116):
In the next section we will explore examples of how children are driven into these defenses
by traumatizing parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 223 (Number of characters: 275):
The four children in the vignette below match the four basic types of
trauma survivors:
Bob=Fight - Narcissistic
Carol=Flight - Obsessive/Compulsive
Maude=Freeze - Dissociative
Sean=Fawn - Codependent
The 4F’s In A Cptsd-Inducing Family
Carol was the scapegoat of her family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 224 (Number of characters: 110):
Narcissistic and borderline parents typically choose at
least one child to be the designated family scapegoat.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 225 (Number of characters: 345):
Scapegoating is the process by which a bully offloads and externalizes his pain, stress, and
frustration by attacking a less powerful person. Typically scapegoating brings the bully some
momentary relief. It does not however effectively metabolize or release his pain, and
scapegoating soon resumes as the bully’s internal discomfort resurfaces.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 226 (Number of characters: 246):
Wilhelm Reich, in his brilliant book The Psychology of Fascism, explains how scapegoating
occurs on a continuum that stretches from the persecution of the targeted child by a bullying
parent to the horrific scapegoating of the Jews by the Nazi’s.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 227 (Number of characters: 147):
In especially dysfunctional families
like Carol’s, the scapegoating parent often organizes the rest of the family to also gang up on the
scapegoat.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 228 (Number of characters: 232):
Carol discovered a great deal about her early childhood from watching home videos. Her
parents were so narcissistically oblivious, that they unabashedly recorded many incidents of
Carol being verbally and emotionally abused by them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 229 (Number of characters: 112):
This was usually in the background of
recordings of the performances of their favorite child, her older brother.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 230 (Number of characters: 82):
Severely narcissistic
parents are rarely embarrassed by their aggressive behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 231 (Number of characters: 140):
They feel entitled to punish a child
for anything that displeases them, no matter how unreasonable it might appear to an impartial
observer.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 232 (Number of characters: 115):
Carols’ parents started in on her early by disdainfully blaming her for soiling her diaper
before she was even one.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 233 (Number of characters: 201):
By the time she was three, she had been so frequently punished for
making noise while talking and playfully exploring her house, that her constant state of fear
generated an ADHD-like condition in her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 234 (Number of characters: 210):
Carol’s large backyard was her refuge where she would play with great gusto - climbing,
running, cavorting, and building and ransacking villages that she made with her toys and leaves,
grass, sticks and stones.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 235 (Number of characters: 192):
She would busy herself from breakfast until supper, often forgetting to
come in for lunch, which she thought in retrospect made life even easier for her mother, who
never called her in to eat.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 236 (Number of characters: 120):
One family video from this time was the straw that broke the camel’s back of Carol’s denial
that her family was abusive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 237 (Number of characters: 187):
It showed her playing a game whereby she would repetitively smack

touching various knick-knacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 238 (Number of characters: 127):
There was a considerable amount of footage that showed her
parents and siblings roaring with mocking delight in the background.

chunk 239 (Number of characters: 110):
When contempt replaces the milk of human kindness at an early age, the child feels
humiliated and overwhelmed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 240 (Number of characters: 155):
Too helpless to protest or even understand the unfairness of being

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 241 (Number of characters: 75):
Frequently she comes to believe that she deserves her parents’ persecution.

chunk 254 (Number of characters: 282):
I believe there is an epidemic of sibling abuse that afflicts many dysfunctional families. Siblings in such families can traumatize the victim-scapegoat as severely as the parents. In
families with checked out, disinterested parents, they can in fact be the chief sources of trauma.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 255 (Number of characters: 167):
This is especially true in our culture where emotional neglect of children is rampant and where

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 256 (Number of characters: 150):
But how does a child who

has half the strength of his older sibling work it out, and stop him from tormenting her without

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 259 (Number of characters: 150):

chunk 260 (Number of characters: 156):

chunk 262 (Number of characters: 470):
As an adolescent, her trauma was painfully reinforced by her

seemingly escaped from the family. Carol remained symbolically enthralled to the family by
getting ensnared with narcissistic people who were just as abusive and neglectful as her parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 263 (Number of characters: 142):
This well known psychological phenomenon is called repetition compulsion or reenactment, and
trauma survivors are extremely susceptible to it.

chunk 275 (Number of characters: 230):
Poor Parenting Creates Pathological Sibling Rivalry
Like many children in Cptsd-engendering families, Maude could not turn to her siblings for
comfort because her parents unconsciously practiced the “divide and conquer” principle.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 276 (Number of characters: 89):
Her
parents modeled and encouraged sarcasm and constant fault finding among the children.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 277 (Number of characters: 73):
Moreover, interactions of cooperation or warmth were routinely ridiculed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 278 (Number of characters: 290):
Sibling rivalry is further reinforced in dysfunctional families by the fact that all the children
are subsisting on minimal nurturance, and are therefore without resources to give to each other. Moreover, competition for the little their parents have to give creates even fiercer rivalries.

chunk 280 (Number of characters: 212):

--------------------------------------------------

Chapters 6 and 7 explore each of the 4F’s and their corresponding defensive structures in
greater detail.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 294 (Number of characters: 210):
These chapters will also help you determine your key 4F defense, and help you
address issues that are more specific to your type of Cptsd.

LEVELS OF RECOVERING
Healing from Complex PTSD is, above all, complex.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 295 (Number of characters: 129):
This is important to emphasize because
there are numerous one dimensional approaches to trauma that bill themselves as cure-alls.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 296 (Number of characters: 121):
In my
opinion, however, singular approaches are unable to address all the levels of wounding that
combine to cause Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 297 (Number of characters: 126):
Moreover, working with simplistic approaches can leave you stranded in toxic shame when
you do not achieve the touted results.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 298 (Number of characters: 163):
I was motivated to write this book in large part because of
the many times I sank into new levels of self-contempt when the latest panacea therapy did not
cure me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 299 (Number of characters: 96):
I will use the word “key” repeatedly to describe the various tasks upon which recovering
hinges.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 300 (Number of characters: 140):
This book offers a keychain of perspectives and techniques to unlock yourself from being
what Alice Miller called a “Prisoner of Childhood.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 301 (Number of characters: 130):
Abusive and abandoning parents can injure and abandon us on many levels: cognitive,
emotional, spiritual, physical and relational.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 302 (Number of characters: 165):
To recover, you need to learn how to support
yourself – to meet your unmet developmental needs on each level that is relevant to your
experience of childhood trauma.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 306 (Number of characters: 127):
Key Developmental Arrests In Cptsd
What follows is a list of some of the most common developmental arrests that occur in Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 307 (Number of characters: 105):
You may find that you experience a diminishment or absence of these key features of healthy

human being.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 308 (Number of characters: 85):
Typically, survivors will vary on which and how many of these arrests relate to
them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 309 (Number of characters: 156):
Factors affecting this are your 4F type, your childhood abuse/ neglect pattern, your innate
nature and any recovery work that you have already accomplished.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 310 (Number of characters: 406):
Self-acceptance
Clear sense of identity
Self-Compassion
Self-Protection
Capacity to draw comfort from relationship
Ability to relax
Capacity for full self-expression
Willpower & Motivation
Peace of mind
Self-care
Belief that life is a gift
Self-esteem
Self-confidence
My efforts to nurture myself in these arrested areas of development were limited and spoiled in
early recovery by a feeling of resentment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 311 (Number of characters: 58):
“Why do I have to do this?” was a common internal
refrain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 312 (Number of characters: 140):
Resentment that should have been directed toward my parents often boomeranged onto
me and spoiled or thwarted my efforts at self-nurturance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 313 (Number of characters: 63):
Thankfully ongoing recovery work helped remedy this resentment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 314 (Number of characters: 112):
It taught me to practice
self-care in a spirit of giving to a child who needed and really deserved to be helped.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 315 (Number of characters: 162):
I find it helpful to approach developmental arrests from the viewpoint of novelist David
Mitchell’s quip that “…fire is the sun unwinding itself out of the wood”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 316 (Number of characters: 108):
Similarly, effective
recovery is unwinding the natural potential you were born with out of your unconscious.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 317 (Number of characters: 96):
This is
your innate potential which may be, as yet, unrealized because of your childhood trauma.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 318 (Number of characters: 216):
An especially tragic developmental arrest that afflicts many survivors is the loss of their
will power and self-motivation. Many dysfunctional parents react destructively to their child’s
budding sense of initiative.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 319 (Number of characters: 96):
If this occurs throughout his childhood, the survivor may feel lost
and purposeless in his life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 320 (Number of characters: 67):
He may drift through his whole life rudderless and without a motor.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 321 (Number of characters: 143):
Moreover, even when he manages to identify a goal of his own choosing, he may struggle
to follow through with extended and concentrated effort.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 322 (Number of characters: 245):
Remedying this developmental arrest is
essential because many new psychological studies now show that persistence – even more than
intelligence or innate talent - is the key psychological characteristic necessary for finding
fulfillment in life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 323 (Number of characters: 78):
I have worked with many survivors stranded in this form of adult helplessness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 324 (Number of characters: 138):
Those who
recover from it typically do so by engaging extensively in the angering work of grieving that is
discussed throughout this book.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 325 (Number of characters: 99):
The ability to invoke willpower seems to be allied to your ability
to healthily express your anger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 326 (Number of characters: 72):
With sufficient recovering, you can learn to manufacture your

volition.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 327 (Number of characters: 51):
In the beginning you can fake it until you make it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 328 (Number of characters: 123):
This is what Stephen Johnson calls
“the hard work miracle.”
What follows is a concluding comment about development arrests.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 329 (Number of characters: 51):
Some survivors have
confidence but not self-esteem.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 330 (Number of characters: 122):
In childhood, my own flight response got channeled into
acquiring academic skills for which the outside world rewarded me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 331 (Number of characters: 123):
But the benefit of these
rewards never penetrated my toxic shame enough to allow me to feel that I was a worthwhile
person.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 332 (Number of characters: 110):
My critic, like my parents, always found something flawed in me to contradict the feedback
that I was getting.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 333 (Number of characters: 58):
Ninety-nine percent on a test was never a cause for pride.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 334 (Number of characters: 92):
Rather, it was the
impetus for a great deal of self-criticism about the missing one percent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 335 (Number of characters: 87):
Like many other
survivors that I have worked with, I developed the imposter’s syndrome.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 336 (Number of characters: 78):
This syndrome
contradicted the outside positive feedback that I was receiving.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 337 (Number of characters: 77):
It insisted that if people really
knew me, they would see what a loser I was.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 338 (Number of characters: 104):
Eventually, however, I became confident in my
intelligence even though my self-esteem was still abysmal.

chunk 339 (Number of characters: 209):
COGNITIVE HEALING
The first level of recovery usually involves repairing the damage that Cptsd wreaks on our
thoughts and beliefs about ourselves. Cognitive recovery work aims to make your brain user friendly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 340 (Number of characters: 131):
It focuses on recognizing
and eliminating the destructive thoughts and thinking processes you were indoctrinated with in
childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 341 (Number of characters: 126):
Cognitive healing also depends on learning to choose healthy and more accurate ways of
talking to and thinking about yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 342 (Number of characters: 91):
On the broadest level, this involves upgrading the story
you tell yourself about your pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 343 (Number of characters: 111):
We need to understand exactly how appalling parenting created the now self-perpetuating
trauma that we live in.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 344 (Number of characters: 93):
We can learn to do this in a way that takes the mountain of unfair self-
blame off ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 345 (Number of characters: 76):
We can redirect this blame to our parents’ dreadful child-rearing practices.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 346 (Number of characters: 137):
And we can also do this in a way that motivates us to reject their influence so that we can freely
orchestrate our journey of recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 347 (Number of characters: 69):
This work then requires us to build a fierce allegiance to ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 348 (Number of characters: 141):
Such loyalty strengthens
us for the cognitive work of freeing our brains from being conditioned to attack so many normal
parts of our selves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 349 (Number of characters: 124):
Cognitive work is fundamental to helping you disidentify from the self-hating critic with
which your parents inculcated you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 350 (Number of characters: 144):
As I am writing this, my son’s friend synchronistically tells
him: “This Lego creature I made spreads brain attack and eats away at the person.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 351 (Number of characters: 96):
I marvel at
this synchronicity and think: “What a fitting image for the trauma-inducing parent”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 352 (Number of characters: 218):
Shrinking The Critic
Early abuse and abandonment forces the child to merge his identity with the superego, the part of

the child’s brain that learns the rules of his caretakers in order to get and maintain acceptance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 353 (Number of characters: 142):
However, because acceptance is impossible in the Cptsd-engendering family, the superego gets
stuck working overtime to achieve the impossible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 354 (Number of characters: 171):
Perseverating on finding a formula to win
over her parents, the child eventually embraces perfectionism as a strategy to make her parents
less dangerous and more engaging.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 355 (Number of characters: 119):
Her one hope is that if she becomes smart, helpful, pretty,
and flawless enough, her parents will finally care for her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 356 (Number of characters: 99):
Sadly, continued failure at winning their regard forces her to conclude that she is fatally
flawed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 357 (Number of characters: 74):
She is loveless not because of her mistakes, but because she is a mistake.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 358 (Number of characters: 54):
She can only
see what is wrong with or missing in her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 359 (Number of characters: 135):
Anything she does, says, thinks, imagines or feels has the potential to spiral her down into a
depressed abyss of fear and toxic shame.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 360 (Number of characters: 64):
Her superego fledges into a full-blown, trauma-
inducing critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 361 (Number of characters: 96):
Self-criticism, then, runs non-stop in a desperate attempt to avoid rejection-inducing
mistakes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 362 (Number of characters: 104):
Drasticizing becomes obsessive to help the child foresee and avoid punishment and
worsening abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 363 (Number of characters: 90):
At the same time, it continuously fills her psyche with stories and
images of catastrophe.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 364 (Number of characters: 83):
The survivor becomes imprisoned by a jailer who will accept nothing but perfection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 365 (Number of characters: 95):
He is
chauffeured by a hysterical driver who sees nothing but danger in every turn of the road.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 366 (Number of characters: 81):
Chapters 9 and 10 focus extensively on practical tools for shrinking your critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 367 (Number of characters: 124):
The Developmentally Arrested Healthy Ego
Over time the critic becomes more and more synonymous with the survivor’s identity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 368 (Number of characters: 92):
The
superego morphs into a totalitarian critic that trumps the development of a healthy ego.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 369 (Number of characters: 209):
[The ego
develops later than the superego.]
“Ego”, contrary to popular usage, is not a dirty word. In psychology, the term ego
represents what we typically mean when we use terms like my “self” or my identity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 370 (Number of characters: 59):
The healthy
ego is the user friendly manager of the psyche.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 371 (Number of characters: 169):
Unfortunately, Cptsd-inducing parents thwart the
growth of the ego by undermining the development of the crucial egoic processes of self-
compassion and self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 372 (Number of characters: 136):
They do this by shaming or intimidating you whenever you have a natural impulse to have
sympathy for yourself, or stand up for yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 373 (Number of characters: 110):
The instinct to care for yourself and to protect
yourself against unfairness is then forced to become dormant.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 374 (Number of characters: 175):
Psychoeducation And Cognitive Healing
Becoming psychoeducated about Cptsd is the first level of addressing this poisonous
indoctrination of your mind against your healthy ego.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 375 (Number of characters: 188):
When you intricately understand how
antagonistic your parents were to your healthy sense of self, you become more motivated to
engage in the self-help processes of rectifying their damage.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 376 (Number of characters: 43):
The more you identify their damage
the more

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 377 (Number of characters: 21):
you know what to fix.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 378 (Number of characters: 122):
This is essential because without a properly functioning ego, you have no center for making
healthy choices and decisions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 379 (Number of characters: 190):
All too often, your decisions are based on the fear of getting in
trouble or getting abandoned, rather than on the principles of having meaningful and equitable

interactions with the world.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 380 (Number of characters: 170):
You can learn to gradually replace the critic’s toxic perspective with a viewpoint that
supports you in your life, and that stops you from unnecessarily scaring yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 381 (Number of characters: 98):
You are free now as an adult to develop peace of mind and a supportive relationship with
yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 382 (Number of characters: 114):
A self-championing stance can transform your existence from struggling survival to a
fulfilling sense of thriving.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 383 (Number of characters: 123):
You can begin right now by inviting your instincts of self-compassion and self-protection to
awaken and bloom in your life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 384 (Number of characters: 86):
Cognitive healing may have begun or been reinforced by reading what has preceded this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 385 (Number of characters: 85):
Hopefully you are having some epiphanies about what is at the core of your suffering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 386 (Number of characters: 165):
Some readers may have been searching for cognitive answers for years, and through their
reading and therapy already created a sizable foundation for doing this work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 387 (Number of characters: 176):
At the same time, those who have only tried a Cognitive-Behavioral Approach [CBT] to
healing their trauma may feel great resistance to hearing that cognitive work is important.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 388 (Number of characters: 107):
If you
are like me, you may have been introduced to it in a way that promised more than could be
delivered.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 389 (Number of characters: 118):
Cognitive tools are irreplaceable in healing cognitive issues, but they do not address
all the levels of our wounding.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 390 (Number of characters: 81):
They are especially limited in addressing emotional issues, as we
will see below.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 391 (Number of characters: 198):
In early recovery, the psychoeducation piece of cognitive work typically comes from the wisdom
of others: teachers, writers, friends and therapists who are more informed on this subject than we
are.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 392 (Number of characters: 116):
When psychoeducation reaches its most powerful level of effectiveness, however, it begins
to morph into mindfulness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 393 (Number of characters: 190):
MINDFULNESS
Psychologically speaking, mindfulness is taking undistracted time to become fully aware of your
thoughts and feelings so that you can have more choice in how you respond to them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 394 (Number of characters: 80):
Do I really
agree with this thought, or have I been pressured into believing it?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 395 (Number of characters: 144):
How do I want to respond to
this feeling – distract myself from it, repress it, express it or just feel it until it changes into
something else?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 396 (Number of characters: 112):
Mindfulness is a perspective that weds your capacity for self-observation with your instinct
of self-compassion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 397 (Number of characters: 219):
It is therefore your ability to observe yourself from an objective and self-
accepting viewpoint. It is a key function of a healthily developed ego and is sometimes described
as the observing ego or the witnessing self.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 398 (Number of characters: 84):
Mindfulness is a perspective of benign curiosity about all of your inner experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 399 (Number of characters: 86):
Recovery is enhanced immeasurably by developing this helpful process of introspection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 400 (Number of characters: 160):
As it
becomes more developed, mindfulness can be used to recognize and dis-identify from beliefs and
viewpoints that you acquired from your traumatizing family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 401 (Number of characters: 82):
I cannot overstate the importance of becoming aware of your inner self-commentary.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 402 (Number of characters: 185):
With
enough practice, mindfulness eventually awakens your fighting spirit to resist the abusive
refrains from your childhood, and to replace them with thoughts that are self-supportive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 403 (Number of characters: 121):
Mindfulness also helps you to establish a perspective from which you can assess and guide your
own efforts of recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 404 (Number of characters: 461):
Chapter 12 contains detailed instruction for enhancing mindfulness, as do the writings of
Steven Levine, Jack Kornfield and John Kabat-Zinn. Finally, it is important to note that mindfulness tends to develop and expand in a progressive
manner to all levels of our experience, cognitive, emotional, physical and relational. Mindfulness
is essential for guiding us at every level of recovering, and we will examine this principle more
closely throughout the book.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 405 (Number of characters: 119):
EMOTIONAL HEALING
Traumatizing parents do as much damage to our emotional natures as they do to our thinking
processes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 406 (Number of characters: 89):
Consequently, there is a great deal of recovery work that needs to be done on this
level.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 407 (Number of characters: 99):
This is especially true because of the damage our wider society also does to our emotional
natures.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 408 (Number of characters: 97):
Recovering The Emotional Nature
This section is an updated version of an article I wrote in 1991.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 409 (Number of characters: 201):
I originally wrote it as a prelude
to my first book, The Tao of Fully Feeling, and it was written as an appeal to the general public
to understand the consequences of trying to sanitize one’s emotions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 410 (Number of characters: 176):
Thankfully, the response I
received encouraged me to complete that book, which is a guide to overcoming the familial and
societal damage meted out on children’s emotional life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 411 (Number of characters: 251):
The survivor, who is seeking a healthy relationship with his emotional being, will strive to
accept the existential fact that the human feeling nature is often contradictory and frequently
vacillates between opposite polarities of feeling experiences.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 412 (Number of characters: 128):
It is quite normal for feelings to
change unpredictably along continuums that stretch between a variety of emotional polarities.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 413 (Number of characters: 218):
As
such, it is especially human and healthy to have shifts of mood between such extremes as happy
and sad, enthused and depressed, loving and angry, trusting and suspicious, brave and afraid, and
forgiving and blaming.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 414 (Number of characters: 111):
Unfortunately, in this culture only the “positive” polarity of any emotional experience is
approved or allowed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 415 (Number of characters: 115):
This can cause such an avoidance of the “negative” polarity, that at least
two different painful conditions result.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 416 (Number of characters: 145):
In the first, the person injures and exhausts himself in compulsive attempts to avoid a
disavowed feeling, and actually becomes more stuck in it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 417 (Number of characters: 141):
This is like the archetypal clown
whose frantic efforts to free himself from a piece of fly paper, leave him more immobilized and

entangled.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 418 (Number of characters: 160):
In the second, repression of one end of the emotional continuum often leads to a repression
of the whole continuum, and the person becomes emotionally deadened.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 419 (Number of characters: 93):
The baby of emotional
vitality is thrown out with the bathwater of some unacceptable feeling.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 420 (Number of characters: 113):
A reluctance to participate in such a fundamental realm of the human experience results in
much unnecessary loss.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 421 (Number of characters: 218):
For just as without night there is no day, without work there is no play,
without hunger there is no satiation, without fear there is no courage, without tears there is no
joy, and without anger, there is no real love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 422 (Number of characters: 213):
Most people, who choose or are coerced into only identifying with “positive” feelings,
usually wind up in an emotionally lifeless middle ground – bland, deadened, and dissociated in
an unemotional “no-man’s-land.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 423 (Number of characters: 174):
Moreover, when a person tries to hold onto a preferred feeling for longer than its actual
tenure, she often appears as unnatural and phony as ersatz grass or plastic flowers.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 424 (Number of characters: 232):
If instead, she
learns to surrender willingly to the normal human experience that good feelings always ebb and
flow, she will eventually be graced with a growing ability to renew herself in the vital waters of
emotional flexibility.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 425 (Number of characters: 161):
The repression of the so-called negative polarities of emotion causes much unnecessary
pain, as well as the loss of many essential aspects of the feeling nature.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 426 (Number of characters: 258):
In fact, much of the
plethora of loneliness, alienation, and addictive distraction that plagues modern industrial
societies is a result of people being taught and forced to reject, pathologize or punish so many of
their own and others’ normal feeling states.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 427 (Number of characters: 181):
Nowhere, not in the deepest recesses of the self, or in the presence of his closest friends, is
the average person allowed to have and explore any number of normal emotional states.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 428 (Number of characters: 122):
Anger,
depression, envy, sadness, fear, distrust, etc., are all as normal a part of life as bread and flowers
and streets.
