--------------------------------------------------

chunk 429 (Number of characters: 74):
Yet, they have become ubiquitously avoided and shameful human experiences.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 430 (Number of characters: 124):
How tragic this is, for all of these emotions have enormously important and healthy
functions in a wholly integrated psyche.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 431 (Number of characters: 81):
One dimension where this is most true is in the arena of
healthy self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 432 (Number of characters: 428):
For without access to our uncomfortable or painful feelings, we are
deprived of the most fundamental part of our ability to notice when something is unfair, abusive,
or neglectful in our environments. Those who cannot feel their sadness often do not know when they are being unfairly
excluded, and those who cannot feel their normal angry or fearful responses to abuse, are often in
danger of putting up with it without protest.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 433 (Number of characters: 133):
Perhaps never before has humankind been so alienated from so many of its normal feeling
states, as it is in the twenty-first century.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 434 (Number of characters: 85):
Never before have so many human beings been so
emotionally deadened and impoverished.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 435 (Number of characters: 48):
The disease of emotional emaciation is epidemic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 436 (Number of characters: 160):
Its effects on health are often
euphemistically labeled as stress, and like the emotions, stress is often treated like some
unwanted waste that must be removed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 437 (Number of characters: 231):
Until all of the emotions are accepted indiscriminately (and acceptance does not imply
license to dump emotions irresponsibly or abusively), there can be no wholeness, no real sense of
well being, and no solid sense of self esteem.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 438 (Number of characters: 375):
Thus, while it may be fairly easy to like yourself
when feelings of love or happiness or serenity are present, deeper psychological health is seen
only when you can maintain a posture of self-love and self-respect in the times of emotional hurt
that accompany life’s inevitable contingencies of loss, loneliness, confusion, uncontrollable

unfairness, and accidental mistake.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 439 (Number of characters: 87):
The human feeling experience, much like the weather, is often unpredictably changeable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 440 (Number of characters: 128):
No “positive” feeling can be induced to persist as a permanent experience, no matter what
Cognitive-Behavioral Therapy tells us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 441 (Number of characters: 328):
As disappointing as this may be, as much as we might
like to deny it, as much as it causes each of us ongoing life frustration, and as much as we were
raised and continue to be reinforced for trying to control and pick our feelings, they are still by
definition of the human condition, largely outside the province of our wills.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 442 (Number of characters: 430):
EMOTIONAL INTELLIGENCE
Daniel Goleman defines emotional intelligence as our ability to successfully recognize and
manage our own feelings and to healthily respond to the feelings of others. As implied above, I
believe the quality of our emotional intelligence is reflected in the degree to which we accept all
of our feelings without automatically dissociating from them or expressing them in a way that
hurts ourselves or others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 443 (Number of characters: 84):
When we are emotionally intelligent we also extend this acceptance to
our intimates.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 444 (Number of characters: 193):
One of my clients calls this the hallmark of “relationships.”
Another way of saying this is that I have self-esteem to the degree that I keep my heart open
to myself in all my emotional states.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 445 (Number of characters: 96):
And, I have intimacy when my friend and I offer this type
of emotional acceptance to each other.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 446 (Number of characters: 129):
Once again, this does not condone destructive expressions
of anger which are, of course, counterproductive to trust and intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 447 (Number of characters: 457):
Cptsd-engendering parents often hypocritically attack their children’s emotional expression in a
bi-modal way. This occurs when the child is both abused for emoting and is, at the same time,
abused by her caretaker’s toxic emotional expression. Most traumatizing parents are especially contemptuous towards the child’s expression of
emotional pain. This contempt then forces the child’s all-important capacity for healthy grieving
into developmental arrest.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 448 (Number of characters: 345):
One archetypal example of this is seen in the parent who hurts his child to the point of tears,
and then has the nerve to say: “Stop crying or I’ll give you something to cry about!” A client
once told me that he often fantasized about giving his father this angry reply: “What are you
talking about, you already gave me something to cry about?!”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 449 (Number of characters: 145):
He did not, however, because he
had long since learned that getting angry back was a capital crime that would elicit the most
savage retaliation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 450 (Number of characters: 96):
Typically it would be delivered with homicidal rage: “I’ll knock you from
here to Kingdom come!”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 451 (Number of characters: 85):
The above is of course a blatant example of the slaughtering of emotional expression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 452 (Number of characters: 147):
Just
as common is the insidious, passive-aggressive assault on emoting which is seen in the parent
who shuns her child for expressing his feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 453 (Number of characters: 158):
This is seen in the emotionally abandoning
parent who sequesters the child in a timeout for crying, or routinely retreats from the crying child
into her room.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 454 (Number of characters: 102):
The worst, most damaging example of this occurs when this is done to the pre-verbal
toddler [or baby!]

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 455 (Number of characters: 52):
who only has emotions with which to express herself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 456 (Number of characters: 153):
Pre-verbal children are
by definition far too young to learn the 2-3 year-olds’ developmental task of using her words to

communicate about her feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 457 (Number of characters: 521):
An especially nasty form of emotional abuse occurs in the traumatizing family when the child is
even attacked for displays of pleasant emotion. As I write this I flashback to scenes of my mother
sneering at my little sister and snarling: “What are you so happy about!”, and my father’s
frequent: “What are you laughing at – wipe that smile off your face!”
Emotional abuse is also almost always also accompanied by emotional abandonment, which can
most simply be described as a relentless lack of parental warmth and love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 458 (Number of characters: 222):
Sometimes this is
most poignantly described as not being liked by your parents, which belies the many Cptsd-
inducing parents who say they love their children, but demonstrate in a thousand ways that they
do not like them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 459 (Number of characters: 90):
“The sight of you makes me sick” was very popular with such parents when I
was growing up.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 460 (Number of characters: 171):
It can still bring tears to my eyes to remember my emotionally abandoned young sister
secreted in a corner of the house begging our family dog: “Like me, Ginger, Like me!”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 461 (Number of characters: 125):
Toxic Shame And Soul Murder
The rejecting responses of our parents to our emotional expression alienate us from our feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 462 (Number of characters: 126):
Emotional abuse/neglect scares us out of our own emotions while simultaneously making us
terrified of other people’s feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 463 (Number of characters: 89):
John Bradshaw describes the devastation of the child’s emotional nature as “soul murder”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 464 (Number of characters: 418):
He explains this as involving a process where the child’s emotional expression [his first language
of self-expression] is so assaulted with disgust that any emotional experience immediately
devolves into toxic shame. I believe that toxic shame is the affect of the inner critic, and that inner critic thought-
processes are the cognitions of shame – a terrible yin/yang process emanating from our original
abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 465 (Number of characters: 147):
Because of the deadly one-two punch of familial and societal attacks on our emotional selves, we
need to recover our innate emotional intelligence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 466 (Number of characters: 116):
This is also deeply important because, as Carl
Jung emphasized, our emotions tell us what is really important to us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 467 (Number of characters: 161):
When our emotional
intelligence is restricted, we often do not know what we really want, and can consequently
struggle mightily with even the smallest decisions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 468 (Number of characters: 115):
As emotional recovery progresses, the mindfulness described above begins to extend
toward our emotional experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 469 (Number of characters: 67):
This helps us to stop automatically dissociating from our
feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 470 (Number of characters: 96):
We then learn to identify our feelings and choose healthy ways to respond to them and
from them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 471 (Number of characters: 126):
Such emotional development illuminates our own natural preferences, and, in turn

aids us in making easier and better choices.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 472 (Number of characters: 264):
Towards the end of a long term therapy, a male client told me: “Yesterday, I was
contemplating what I have discovered in the years of our work together, and I’m amazed at how
much my values have shifted away from those of the macho family and culture I grew up in.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 473 (Number of characters: 161):
I
feel now like I prefer the arts to science, novels to non-fiction, gardening to watching golf, and
hanging out with my partner at home to partying at the bar.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 474 (Number of characters: 395):
Grieving As Emotional Intelligence
Grieving is the key process for reconnecting with our repressed emotional intelligence. Grieving
reconnects us with our full complement of feelings. Grieving is necessary to help us release and
work through our pain about the terrible losses of our childhoods. These losses are like deaths of
parts of our selves, and grieving can often initiate their rebirth.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 475 (Number of characters: 176):
Grieving And Verbal Ventilation
Grieving restores our crucial, developmentally arrested capacity to verbally ventilate. Verbal
ventilation is the penultimate grieving practice.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 476 (Number of characters: 94):
It is speaking from your feelings in a way that
releases and resolves your emotional distress.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 477 (Number of characters: 132):
I believe the following description of a six panel cartoon visually conveys the powerful
transformative power of verbal ventilation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 478 (Number of characters: 253):
In the first panel of the wordless cartoon, a woman
with a dark cloud over her head is talking to a friend who has a shining sun over hers. In panel
two, as the first woman gestures in a way that indicates complaining, the cloud covers her
friend’s sun.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 479 (Number of characters: 114):
In panel three, the cloud emits a bolt of lightning, as she angrily purges, and her
friend glowers along with her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 480 (Number of characters: 104):
In panel four, the cloud rains on them as they embrace,
commiserating in the rain of their shared tears.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 481 (Number of characters: 81):
In panel 5, relief spreads over their faces as the
cloud moves away from the sun.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 482 (Number of characters: 95):
In panel 6 the sun shines over both of them, as they smile and
slip into pleasant conversation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 483 (Number of characters: 115):
This cartoon reflects the fully realized power of verbal ventilation, which is the key bonding
process in intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 484 (Number of characters: 141):
It is also the key healing process of effective therapy, and here is an
example of what verbally ventilating looks like in a therapy session.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 485 (Number of characters: 41):
A client arrives flashbacked and in pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 486 (Number of characters: 32):
He verbally ventilates about it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 487 (Number of characters: 91):
He is the regressed
hurt child, feeling bad, and part of him is sad and part of him is mad.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 488 (Number of characters: 137):
He is once again lost in the
painful feelings of his original abandonment, and this state is like a death that responds well to
grieving.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 489 (Number of characters: 85):
As he lets his feelings come into his voice, he talks, cries and angers out his pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 490 (Number of characters: 82):
Through
this processing of his pain, he then gradually moves out of his flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 491 (Number of characters: 161):
He is restored to his
normal everyday sense that he is no longer trapped in his traumatic childhood. Relief about this
returns him to his normal ability to cope.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 492 (Number of characters: 83):
If his grieving is deep enough, he customarily feels
more hopeful and lighthearted.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 493 (Number of characters: 107):
Not infrequently, his sense of humor resurfaces, and laughter
punctuates his continuing verbal ventilation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 494 (Number of characters: 136):
This laughter is usually much different than the
sarcastic, self-bullying humor of his critic that he might have begun the session with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 495 (Number of characters: 496):
The inner critic is sometimes so hostile to grieving that shrinking the critic may need to be your
first recovery priority. Until the critic is sufficiently tamed, grieving can actually make
flashbacks worse, rather than perform the restorative processes it alone can initiate. I have worked with numerous clients who were so traumatized around grieving that we
needed to spend many months working on the cognitive level before grieving was released from
the spoiling effects of the toxic critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 496 (Number of characters: 92):
Chapter 11 provides a great deal of practical guidance for
restoring your ability to grieve.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 497 (Number of characters: 225):
SPIRITUAL HEALING
Soothing Abandonment Losses Via A Higher Sense Of Belonging
Spiritual beliefs are of course a subject of personal and sometimes private concern, and I believe
and hope what I write here is not proselytizing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 498 (Number of characters: 99):
My aim, instead, is to point out psychological
concepts that have a non-sectarian spiritual aspect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 499 (Number of characters: 201):
I am aware, however, that some survivors
have suffered terrible spiritual abuse in childhood, and if the term “spiritual” is offensive or
triggering in any way, please feel free to bypass this section.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 500 (Number of characters: 50):
There are many other useful tools in
this toolbox.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 501 (Number of characters: 126):
A key aspect of the abandonment depression in Cptsd is the lack of a sense of belonging to
humanity, life, anyone or anything.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 502 (Number of characters: 119):
I have met many survivors whose first glimmer of
“belonging” came to them on a quest that began as a spiritual pursuit.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 503 (Number of characters: 91):
Finding nothing but
betrayal in the realm of humans, they turned to the spiritual for help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 504 (Number of characters: 95):
Spiritual pursuits are sometimes fueled by an unconscious hope of finding a sense of
belonging.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 505 (Number of characters: 112):
The worst thing that can happen to a child is to be unwelcomed in his family of origin
- to never feel included.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 506 (Number of characters: 334):
Moreover, many survivors have little or no experience of any social
arena that feels safe and welcoming. Many survivors also do not find a sense of belonging in traditional or organized religions. Finding conventional religion too reminiscent of their dysfunctional families, some survivors
look to more solitary spiritual approaches.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 507 (Number of characters: 134):
They find a sense of belonging to something larger
and more comforting by reading spiritual books or engaging in meditative practices.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 508 (Number of characters: 67):
This also
allows them to bypass the danger of direct human contact.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 509 (Number of characters: 162):
Other survivors have spiritual experiences of belonging to something greater and
worthwhile by being in nature, by listening to music or by appreciating the arts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 510 (Number of characters: 190):
I once marveled
at a book, whose title now eludes me, that was a compendium of quotes from many renowned
people who had numinous experiences through the direct perception of nature’s beauty.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 511 (Number of characters: 175):
A numinous experience is a powerful moving feeling of well being accompanied by a sense
that there is a positive, benign force behind the universe, as well as within yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 512 (Number of characters: 176):
This in turn
sometimes brings enough grace with it, that you have a profound feeling that you are essentially
worthwhile, that you belong in this life, and that life is a gift.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 513 (Number of characters: 84):
One of my website respondents sent me her personal account of therapeutic gratitude.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 514 (Number of characters: 22):
Her name
is Mary Quinn

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 515 (Number of characters: 13):
[of Ireland].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 516 (Number of characters: 257):
In answer to my request to reprint her writing, she replied: “Yes, and
in honor of my little one and for all the times her voice went unheard, you may use my name.”
“I went to the beach a couple of days ago in the morning and sat watching the sun coming up.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 517 (Number of characters: 49):
I
had an incredible moment of the purest clarity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 518 (Number of characters: 98):
I was watching birds flying low over the water,
the moon was still visible and the sun was rising.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 519 (Number of characters: 84):
I realized I was looking at three planets and
there was not another person in sight.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 520 (Number of characters: 107):
“It was a moment of breathtaking beauty and the tears slid down my face at how deep it is
possible to feel.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 521 (Number of characters: 29):
I have been numb for so long.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 522 (Number of characters: 147):
I wrapped my arms around myself and felt the
presence of the little one so strongly it was almost painful but in a healing way if that makes
sense.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 523 (Number of characters: 145):
I realized that all the life experiences I have had to date brought me to that exact moment
and gave me the depth to appreciate it at that level.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 524 (Number of characters: 142):
A sense of peace washed through me like a
gentle wave and for a few moments I felt a connection to a feeling of everything being part of
life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 525 (Number of characters: 32):
It was breathtakingly beautiful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 526 (Number of characters: 64):
I felt like I was experiencing this moment with all of my
senses

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 527 (Number of characters: 58):
and I never knew it was possible to be so much in my body.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 528 (Number of characters: 59):
“The gratitude feeling is deep and profound when it occurs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 529 (Number of characters: 210):
It feels like a moment of
connection to life itself on the deepest level and all life circumstances and what I deem as
problems pale to insignificance in those moments and there is only love in its purest form.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 530 (Number of characters: 109):
It
truly feels like a blessing albeit fleeting but gives enough sustenance and hope to continue the
journey.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 531 (Number of characters: 161):
Whatever the source, spiritual or numinous occurrences sometimes provide the survivor
with her first sense of belonging to something bigger and essentially good.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 532 (Number of characters: 175):
Such experiences can
lead a survivor to an author or speaker or fellow traveler with similar sensibilities, and
sometimes a door opens for finding comfort with a fellow human.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 533 (Number of characters: 125):
Eventually, this may even
grow into a sense that there are some humans out there who are good and safe enough to engage
with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 534 (Number of characters: 426):
Gratitude And Good Enough Parenting
When developing children receive “good enough parenting”, they feel that life is a gift even
though it typically comes with difficult and painful experiences. The term good enough parenting derives from the work of renowned adult and child
psychologist, D.W. Winnicott, who coined the term “good enough mothering” to describe his
observation that children do not need parents to be perfect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 535 (Number of characters: 187):
He noticed through his long career
that children grew up with their self-esteem and capacity for intimacy intact when their parents
were reasonably consistent with their love and support.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 536 (Number of characters: 112):
Nowadays, many therapists attach the phrase “good enough” to concepts like friend,
partner, therapist or person.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 537 (Number of characters: 187):
This is usually done to deconstruct perfectionistic expectations of
relationships - expectations that are so unrealistic that they are destructive to essentially
worthwhile relationships.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 538 (Number of characters: 192):
When I apply the concept of “good enough” to people, I generally mean that a person is
essentially good hearted, tries to be fair, and meets his or her commitments a large portion of the
time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 539 (Number of characters: 162):
I also like to apply “good enough” to other concepts such as a good enough job, a good

enough try, a good enough outing, a good enough day or a good enough life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 540 (Number of characters: 181):
I apply this concept
liberally to contradict the black-and-white, all-or none thinking of the critic which reflexively
judges people and things as defective unless they are perfect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 541 (Number of characters: 83):
Good enough parents provide generous amounts of support, protection and comforting.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 542 (Number of characters: 195):
They
also guide their children to deal constructively with recurring existential difficulties such as loss,
real villains, painful world events and normal disappointments with friends and family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 543 (Number of characters: 80):
Most importantly, they model how disappointments with intimates can be repaired.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 544 (Number of characters: 96):
A key
way they do this is to easily forgive their children for normal mistakes and shortcomings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 545 (Number of characters: 191):
Children who receive good enough parenting easily recognize and protect themselves from
bullying and exploitive people because they do not have to become accustomed to being treated
unfairly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 546 (Number of characters: 143):
Growing up in a safe and loving enough family naturally enhances the child’s capacity to
notice and enjoy the many gifts that life also brings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 547 (Number of characters: 104):
He learns that there is enough good in life to
significantly outweigh its necessary losses and travails.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 548 (Number of characters: 125):
In the traumatizing family however, there is little or nothing that is good enough and hence
little for which to be grateful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 549 (Number of characters: 131):
The child instead is forced to over-develop a critic that hyper-
focuses on what is dangerously imperfect in her as well as others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 550 (Number of characters: 141):
This sometimes helps her to
hide aspects of herself that might be punished. It may further assist her to avoid people who
might be punishing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 551 (Number of characters: 112):
Unfortunately, years of this habituates the child into only seeing herself, life and others in a
negative light.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 552 (Number of characters: 241):
Consequently, when she grows up and becomes free of her truly harmful family,
she cannot see that life offers her many new possibilities. Her ability to see the good in herself
and certain safe enough others remains developmentally arrested.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 553 (Number of characters: 61):
The cultivation of gratitude requires a balanced perspective.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 554 (Number of characters: 150):
You can learn to see and
appreciate the good in life without giving up your ability to discern what is truly negative and
unacceptable in the present.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 555 (Number of characters: 63):
SOMATIC HEALING
Trauma takes its toll on the body in many ways.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 556 (Number of characters: 143):
We need to comprehend the physical damage
that Cptsd wreaks on our bodies to motivate us to adopt practices that help us to heal on this
level.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 557 (Number of characters: 166):
Most of the physiological damage of extended trauma occurs because we are forced to
spend so much time in hyper-arousal – stuck in fight, flight, freeze or fawn mode.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 558 (Number of characters: 146):
When we are chronically stressed out [stuck in sympathetic nervous system activation],
detrimental somatic changes become ingrained in our bodies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 559 (Number of characters: 752):
Here are some of the most
common examples of body-harming reactions to Cptsd stress:
Hypervigilance
Shallow and Incomplete Breathing
Constant Adrenalization

Armoring, i.e., Chronic muscle tightness
Wear and tear from rushing and armoring
Inability to be fully present, relaxed and grounded in our bodies
Sleep problems from being over-activated
Digestive disorders from a tightened digestive tract
Physiological damage from excessive self-medication with alcohol, food or drugs
Moreover, in cases of physical and sexual abuse, our capacities to be physically comforted by
touch are eliminated or compromised; and, in cases of verbal and emotional abuse, our capacities
to be comforted by eye- and voice-contact are undeveloped or seriously diminished.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 560 (Number of characters: 161):
Somatic Self-Help
The good news is that some somatic repair happens automatically when we reduce our
physiological stress by more efficient flashback management.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 561 (Number of characters: 152):
Particularly potent help also comes
from the grieving work of reclaiming the ability to cry self-compassionately and to express anger
self-protectively.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 562 (Number of characters: 143):
Both processes can release armoring, promote embodiment, improve sleep,
decrease hyperarousal and encourage deeper and more rhythmic breathing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 563 (Number of characters: 109):
Without further expressly somatic work, however, a full relaxed inhabitancy of your body
may not be achieved.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 564 (Number of characters: 94):
Fortunately, there are other modes of self-help for healing the
physiological wounds of Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 565 (Number of characters: 199):
The “Somatic Mindfulness” and “Introspective Somatic Work”
sections of chapter 12 describe techniques that can help you to decrease adrenalization, to relax
more deeply and to improve your digestion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 566 (Number of characters: 190):
Moreover, Step 7 of the flashback management steps
at the beginning of chapter 8 contains six somatic, self-help techniques for relaxing out of the
physiological hyperarousal of a flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 567 (Number of characters: 58):
Another especially helpful somatic practice is stretching.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 568 (Number of characters: 366):
Regular systematic stretching of the
body’s major muscle groups can help you to reduce the armoring that occurs when your 4F
response is chronically triggered. This results from the fact that 4F activation tightens and
contracts your body in anticipation of the need to fight back, flee, get small to escape notice, or
rev up to launch into people-pleasing activity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 569 (Number of characters: 227):
Learning to stretch was a major ordeal for me because of my extreme body armoring. As
noted above, it was a task of self-nurturing that I resented intensely, and it took me a long time to
adopt stretching as a regular practice.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 570 (Number of characters: 137):
The fact that I had to weather many toxic shame attacks because I was always the least
flexible person in the group did not help matters.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 571 (Number of characters: 159):
Moreover, when various people commented
about how good it felt to stretch, I felt both puzzled and further shamed, because it was anything
but pleasant for me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 572 (Number of characters: 170):
Thankfully however, reading the literature about it convinced me about its great
importance, and persistent practice eventually gave me results that I could not discount.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 573 (Number of characters: 62):
I was
rewarded by the resolution of decades old back problems.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 574 (Number of characters: 163):
And although I still rarely enjoy the
practice, I am absolutely convinced that it explains why I am still able to run, swim and play

basketball in my mid sixties.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 575 (Number of characters: 71):
Stretching has become for me a true labor of love and self-
nurturance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 576 (Number of characters: 126):
Yoga, massage, meditation and relaxation training are formalized disciplines to aid in letting go
of unnecessary body tension.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 577 (Number of characters: 88):
Reasonably priced classes in these modalities are usually available
in most communities.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 578 (Number of characters: 133):
Finally, freeze types and freeze subtypes also typically benefit from various types of movement
therapy and aerobic exercise regimes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 579 (Number of characters: 175):
Moreover, assertiveness training and anger release work
are especially helpful for survivors who have difficulty accessing their assertiveness or instincts
of self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 580 (Number of characters: 281):
Cptsd And Somatic Therapy
There are also various somatic therapies that can help our bodies heal. As with my earlier
comments about CBT, I encourage you to be wary of somatic approaches that claim to heal
Cptsd without working on the cognitive and emotional levels described above.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 581 (Number of characters: 130):
Some approaches,
in fact, blanketly dismiss cognitive work in a way that sidesteps the crucial work of shrinking the
inner critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 582 (Number of characters: 209):
Some approaches also believe that their techniques eliminate the fundamental
necessity of grieving the losses of childhood, and understanding how abusive and negligent
parenting is at the root of our problems.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 583 (Number of characters: 212):
Nonetheless, some somatic therapists can ease the physiological traumas that are locked in
our bodies, as long as the practitioner is not actively dismissing or impeding the client’s
cognitive and emotional work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 584 (Number of characters: 56):
In this vein, it is my opinion that techniques like EMDR

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 585 (Number of characters: 114):
[Eye Movement Desensitization
Reprocessing] and Somatic Experiencing are very powerful tools for stress-reduction.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 586 (Number of characters: 53):
They are
especially helpful in resolving simple ptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 587 (Number of characters: 167):
However, they are not complete Cptsd therapies,
unless the practitioner is eclectic enough to be incorporating inner critic and grieving-the-losses-
of-childhood work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 588 (Number of characters: 91):
Other helpful somatic techniques include Rosen Work, Rolfing, Rebirthing and Reichian
work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 589 (Number of characters: 126):
These techniques can also be very helpful in aiding the recovery of the ability to
therapeutically emote both tears and anger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 590 (Number of characters: 90):
For survivors of physical and/or sexual abuse, I believe Rosen Work is especially helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 591 (Number of characters: 105):
I
found that Rosen Work’s emphasis on soft touch helped heal my Cptsd startle response to
physical touch.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 592 (Number of characters: 128):
A startle response is the sudden full body-flinching that survivors experience at
loud noises or unanticipated physical contact.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 593 (Number of characters: 55):
This is usually a somatic flashback to previous
abuses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 594 (Number of characters: 99):
In my case, the startle response was installed in me by my parents through frequent face-
slapping.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 595 (Number of characters: 157):
As a lap-swimmer in public pools, it has taken me ages to significantly reduce being
triggered by the hand and arm movements of people who swim alongside me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 596 (Number of characters: 104):
I also had to shop around to find a Rosen worker who welcomed my use of the verbal

ventilation process.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 597 (Number of characters: 118):
Some practitioners prefer to work in silence, and this limits or eliminates the
therapeutic benefit to most survivors.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 598 (Number of characters: 211):
It is also important to emphasize here that somatic therapies can be especially helpful in
healing the anxiety reaction to touch and physical closeness that many survivors of physical or
sexual abuse experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 599 (Number of characters: 158):
Exceptions to this are the survivors that I have met who have
experienced remediation of this symptom through the help of an especially kind and safe partner.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 600 (Number of characters: 326):
The Role Of Medication
As a psychotherapist, I am not authorized to give pharmaceutical advice, but I have frequently
noticed that survivors who need pharmaceutical help seem to benefit most from SSRI anti-
depressants. Taken at the right dosage SSRI’s do not usually blunt your affect in a way that
makes grieving impossible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 601 (Number of characters: 172):
Moreover, if your critic does not budge with extended critic-
shrinking work, SSRI’s can usually reduce its volume and vitriol enough so that you can
effectively shrink it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 602 (Number of characters: 63):
Once it is diminished enough, you can dispense with medication.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 603 (Number of characters: 138):
One
caveat here is that unless you do extensive critic shrinking work, the critic will be as strong as
ever when the medications wear off.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 604 (Number of characters: 195):
Self-Medication
For those who have been repeatedly unsuccessful at stopping or reducing the use of non-
therapeutic medications and substances, Gabor Mate’s work on harm reduction may be helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 605 (Number of characters: 309):
Drug and alcohol recovery is beyond the scope of this book, but if you are stuck in habits of self-
medication that are not allowing you to progress in your Cptsd recovery, I encourage you to get
help from a substance abuse recovery program or from Twelve Step programs like Alcoholics or
Narcotics Anonymous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 606 (Number of characters: 106):
Working With Food Issues
Let us explore one last arena of physical healing, and that is dietary self-help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 607 (Number of characters: 119):
I agree with John
Bradshaw who says that almost everyone who grows up in a dysfunctional family has an eating
disorder.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 608 (Number of characters: 88):
This is a key factor in the digestive track problems that are a common symptom of
Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 609 (Number of characters: 51):
Changing your eating habits is extremely difficult.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 610 (Number of characters: 132):
A client left this quote on my waiting
room bulletin board: “Alcohol and other drug recovery is like dealing with a tiger in a cage.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 611 (Number of characters: 122):
Recovery from eating disorders is like taking that tiger out of the cage three times a day and then
taking it for a walk.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 612 (Number of characters: 124):
Deconstructing food addictions, then, is daunting work that needs to be approached
gradually and with a sense of compassion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 613 (Number of characters: 92):
This is because children who are traumatically
abandoned naturally turn to food for comfort.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 614 (Number of characters: 139):
Food offers us our first outside source of self-
soothing, and when a child is starving for love, he frequently makes food his love object.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 615 (Number of characters: 65):
Over
the years he commonly “elevates” it to the status of a drug.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 616 (Number of characters: 151):
Moreover, increasing scientific
evidence is showing that processed food products combining high levels of sugar, salt and fat are
especially addictive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 617 (Number of characters: 35):
Food addictions begin pre-verbally.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 618 (Number of characters: 117):
They are functional and useful at the time and help us
to survive the unbearable feelings of the abandonment mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 619 (Number of characters: 268):
Unfortunately, we are typically
forced to rely on food-soothing for so long that this over-dependence is extremely difficult to
overcome, and I do not recommend that anyone in early recovery make this their primary focus
unless they have a life-threatening food issue.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 620 (Number of characters: 62):
Instead, I prefer to recommend Mate’s harm
reduction approach.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 621 (Number of characters: 140):
Additionally, Geneen Roth’s book, Breaking Free from Compulsive Eating,
also offers a moderate and sensible approach to dietary improvement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 622 (Number of characters: 138):
While many survivors can be unconscious of their damaging eating habits, I have met
various survivors who take it to the opposite extreme.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 623 (Number of characters: 183):
I was once in the ranks of those who
obsessively over-focus on dietary self-help hoping and expecting that all their suffering will be
resolved if they can just find the perfect diet.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 624 (Number of characters: 73):
Many also chase after every new highly touted
supplement in this pursuit.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 625 (Number of characters: 49):
Some of us also approach exercise in this manner.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 626 (Number of characters: 163):
These are understandable but simplistic versions of the salvation fantasy, and are typically
pursued at the exclusion of working on more core issues of recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 627 (Number of characters: 97):
Nonetheless, almost
everyone has some ideas about how they can eat [and exercise] more healthily.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 628 (Number of characters: 89):
My
recommendation is to try dietary adjustments when you can on a moderate, doable level.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 629 (Number of characters: 182):
IMPROVING RELATIONSHIPS
Forewarning:
There are instances of parental betrayal so extreme, that it is not fair or reasonable to expect the
survivor to try to trust human beings again.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 630 (Number of characters: 143):
If the recommendation in this chapter to open to the
help of others feels too upsetting or overwhelming, please feel free to skip this chapter.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 631 (Number of characters: 209):
There is
a great deal of other material in this book that can help alleviate the many symptoms of Cptsd,
and since recovery is relative and never complete, you do not need to implement everything in
this book.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 632 (Number of characters: 76):
As they say in the Twelve Step Movement: “Take the best and leave the rest.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 633 (Number of characters: 189):
Moreover, as I have experienced personally, and as numerous of my clients and website
respondents have demonstrated to me, real relational healing can and does come from non-
human sources.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 634 (Number of characters: 159):
This is especially true of mammalian pets whose attachment needs and wiring
are similar enough to ours that mutually healing connections can evolve between us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 635 (Number of characters: 159):
Dogs and
cats can be a tremendous source of what Carl Rogers describes as the “unconditional positive
regard” that young children must have in order to thrive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 636 (Number of characters: 72):
Other therapeutic relational sources include nature, music and the arts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 637 (Number of characters: 123):
Moreover, for some
survivors, authors of helpful books can be kept at safe distances while they contribute to your
healing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 638 (Number of characters: 169):
Finally, even with the most heinous betrayals, miracles sometime happen in terms of
discovering a healing human connection, particularly in the later stages of recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 639 (Number of characters: 84):
Cptsd As An Attachment Disorder
Many therapists see Cptsd as an attachment disorder.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 640 (Number of characters: 92):
This means that as a child the survivor
grew up without a safe adult to healthily bond with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 641 (Number of characters: 75):
As bears repeating, Cptsd almost always has

emotional neglect at its core.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 642 (Number of characters: 145):
A key outcome of this is that the child has no one in his formative
years who models the relational skills that are necessary to create intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 643 (Number of characters: 188):
When the developmental need to practice healthy relating with a caretaker is unmet,
survivors typically struggle to find and maintain healthy supportive relationships in their adult
lives.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 644 (Number of characters: 163):
The Origin Of Social Anxiety
A child who grows up with no reliable human source of love, support and protection typically
falls into a great deal of social unease.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 645 (Number of characters: 128):
He “naturally” becomes reluctant to seek support from
anyone, and he is forced to adopt self-sufficiency as a survival strategy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 646 (Number of characters: 59):
Needing anything from others can feel especially dangerous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 647 (Number of characters: 118):
The survivor’s innate capacity
to experience comfort and support in relationship becomes very limited or non-existent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 648 (Number of characters: 106):
This is
despite the fact that many high functioning survivors learn to socially function quite adequately.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 649 (Number of characters: 166):
This is particularly the case in structured situations where expectations are clear and
common goals take the focus off conversing and put it on task accomplishments.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 650 (Number of characters: 119):
Unstructured
social situations however, like attending parties or just hanging out can be considerably more
triggering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 651 (Number of characters: 92):
Spontaneous self-expression feels like the same setup for disaster that it was in
childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 652 (Number of characters: 109):
Either way, structured or spontaneous, relating often involves hiding a great deal of anxiety
and discomfort.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 653 (Number of characters: 101):
One very successful businessman client of mine told me: “I’m so cool, calm and
collected in meetings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 654 (Number of characters: 58):
A veritable wordsmith with the composure of Michael Caine.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 655 (Number of characters: 123):
I’m a king
on the outside, but on the inside I’m a drama queen anguishing in doubt and shame about
everything I say or do.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 656 (Number of characters: 111):
In worst case scenarios, social anxiety can devolve into social phobia, especially during
prolonged flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 657 (Number of characters: 75):
Extensive childhood abuse installs a powerful people-are-dangerous
program.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 658 (Number of characters: 90):
When I was at my least recovered, I couldn’t take out the garbage when I was in flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 659 (Number of characters: 131):
I feared that my neighbor – my sweet, always affirming neighbor – would look out the window
and see how wretched and pitiful I was.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 660 (Number of characters: 88):
Even worse, I dreaded the prospect that she might come
out and want to interact with me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 661 (Number of characters: 174):
Nonetheless, I socialized for decades when necessary, and seemed to be doing it with a
considerable amount of success, no matter how dreadful the reviews were from my critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 662 (Number of characters: 91):
I even
eventually came to see, when not in flashback, that a lot of people really liked me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 663 (Number of characters: 239):
Unfortunately, however, I rarely derived any satisfaction or comfort from this perception,
because underneath my smooth persona, I was writhing in discomfort, and typically measuring
the time until I could least obtrusively make my escape.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 664 (Number of characters: 143):
A Journey Of Relational Healing
The incident I am about to describe marked a huge step in my long, gradual journey of opening
to real intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 665 (Number of characters: 161):
I was sitting on my porch with my dog George, the only being I could truly
relax with, when he broke his lead and sprinted across the street in pursuit of a cat.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 666 (Number of characters: 79):
Before he
could get to the cat, he was run over by a car – both axels-run over.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 667 (Number of characters: 147):
It was the worst thing that

ever happened in my adult life, and when the shock [dissociation] wore off, I was drowning in
the abandonment mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 668 (Number of characters: 65):
Beyond devastated, I felt panicky and catatonic at the same time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 669 (Number of characters: 146):
As I had to in childhood
when feeling overwhelmed, I hid in my room for thirty-six hours - dreading contact with my fair
weather friend-roommates.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 670 (Number of characters: 69):
I was 28 and still thoroughly phobic about showing any vulnerability.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 671 (Number of characters: 164):
All my relationships had been developed under the guise of my people-pleasing, funny guy
persona, and in my current state there was not a joke anywhere to be found.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 672 (Number of characters: 84):
There was no way I
would let myself be seen in what felt like a repulsive condition.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 673 (Number of characters: 138):
I could not sleep, and as sleep deprivation deteriorated into a fear that I was truly going
crazy, out of nowhere came this amazing grace.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 674 (Number of characters: 45):
Grace disguised in a form I usually abhorred.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 675 (Number of characters: 133):
It
was the grace of a deep surrender into weeping - a long sobbing release more soothing than
anything I had ever experienced before.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 676 (Number of characters: 85):
It was the release I describe in chapter 11 and extensively throughout my first book.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 677 (Number of characters: 52):
When
the tears were cried out I knew I would be okay

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 678 (Number of characters: 39):
and I knew I was not going to go crazy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 679 (Number of characters: 100):
I could
face my roommates with the realest, perhaps the first sense of self-esteem I had ever known.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 680 (Number of characters: 79):
And
from that point on, I knew I wanted more of these incredibly healing tears.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 681 (Number of characters: 192):
Healing The Shame That Binds Us In Loneliness
I soon discovered however, that my tears were as stuck as they had ever been, or at least since I
was six – the last time I could remember crying.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 682 (Number of characters: 179):
Further reading and researching then lead me to
seek help, and so ensued my baptism into therapy, blessed by the great fortune of finding a good
enough therapist on the first try.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 683 (Number of characters: 199):
This was a milestone achievement for me, and it evolved into a long meandering journey of
finding more relational help with an array of healers, therapists, therapeutic groups and deeper
friendships.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 684 (Number of characters: 125):
These experiences ranged from extremely helpful to counter-therapeutic, but as time
went on they became increasingly helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 685 (Number of characters: 115):
A central aspect of the truly helpful relational work was what John Bradshaw called
“healing the shame that binds.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 686 (Number of characters: 68):
I believe toxic shame cannot be healed without some relational
help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 687 (Number of characters: 137):
Several therapists and groups aided me greatly to unbind from the shame that made me
hide whenever I could not invoke my perfect persona.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 688 (Number of characters: 98):
Concurrently, I learned that real intimacy
correlated with the amount I shared my vulnerabilities.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 689 (Number of characters: 104):
As I increasingly practiced emotional
authenticity, the glacier of my lifelong loneliness began to melt.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 690 (Number of characters: 113):
It is important to note here that groups can be even more powerful for the healing of shame
than individual work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 691 (Number of characters: 96):
This is because there is typically more mutual vulnerability in a group than
in individual work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 692 (Number of characters: 532):
Moreover, feeling compassion for someone who has suffered similarly to us
sometimes naturally expands into feeling the same for ourselves. Therapeutic relational experiences enhanced my self-compassion considerably further than
what I was able to accomplish on my own. Moreover, I believe that insufficient self-compassion
is the worst developmental arrest of all, and restored self-compassion is the keystone of all
effective recovery. In retrospect I can clearly see that as my self-compassion increased, my toxic shame
decreased.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 693 (Number of characters: 166):
Modern advances in neuroscience [see: A General Theory of Love] suggest that we
are intrinsically limited in our ability to emotionally regulate and soothe ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 694 (Number of characters: 150):
More and

more research suggests that our ability to metabolize painful emotional states is enhanced by
communicating with a safe enough other person.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 695 (Number of characters: 259):
Finding Good Enough Relational Help
In chapter 13, I provide guidance about how to shop for a good enough therapist. I also explore
more deeply the principles of therapeutic relational healing to help you know what is reasonable
to expect from your therapist.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 696 (Number of characters: 205):
I have also met a number of survivors who have been lucky enough to get this kind of relational
healing from a partner or a friend, typically one who had good enough parents or who “has a lot
of recovery”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 697 (Number of characters: 191):
Finally, attachment theorists have developed the concept of earned secure attachment to
describe the recovered enough state where the attachment disorder of Cptsd becomes sufficiently
healed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 698 (Number of characters: 109):
This is typically evidenced by the survivor forming at least one supportive and reliable
enough relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 699 (Number of characters: 137):
Many of the successful therapies I have guided come to an end when the client gains an
earned secure relationship outside of our therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 700 (Number of characters: 88):
This is typically a partner or best friend with
whom the person can truly be themselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 701 (Number of characters: 81):
Another potential source of relational healing is the co-counseling relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 702 (Number of characters: 86):
Guidelines
for creating a co-counseling relationship are also contained in chapter 13.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 703 (Number of characters: 133):
Many respondents to my website have reported glowingly about the help they get from others
through online recovery groups and forums.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 704 (Number of characters: 106):
These groups can be particularly helpful for those
who still find it difficult to be vulnerable in person.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 705 (Number of characters: 154):
Sometimes the distance and relative
anonymity of these forums can decrease the fear of self-disclosure, and this in turn can enhance
therapeutic relating.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 706 (Number of characters: 100):
An increasing number of therapists also seem to be offering telephone
sessions for this same reason.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 707 (Number of characters: 85):
The section “Finding an online group” in chapter 13, lists recommended online groups.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 708 (Number of characters: 205):
Parentdectomy And Relational Healing
I have worked with many clients who began therapy with me while they were still over-
controlled by their traumatizing parents – both externally, as well as internally.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 709 (Number of characters: 73):
Sometimes the
control was enforced by as little as one phone call a week.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 710 (Number of characters: 161):
Not infrequently, these clients were also being overpowered and /or abandoned in
relationships as abusive and neglectful as the ones they had with their parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 711 (Number of characters: 121):
This is repetition
compulsion at its most destructive, and it strands survivors in experiencing the worst of both
worlds.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 712 (Number of characters: 174):
Through in depth exploration of their childhood trauma, many of my still-trapped clients

achieved psychological freedom from their parents for the first time in their lives.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 713 (Number of characters: 125):
Once again,
this was a freedom that they had not actually achieved even though they had been living on their
own for decades.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 714 (Number of characters: 129):
These clients gradually learned to live more successfully on their own without their parents
over-controlling spoiling influence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 715 (Number of characters: 179):
Their ability to build self-nurturing relationships with
themselves almost always correlated with a major reduction or complete severing of their
relationships with their parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 716 (Number of characters: 133):
My client, Joe, who was variously misdiagnosed as Schizoid, Asperger’s, and Paranoid,
was living alone when he began therapy with me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 717 (Number of characters: 123):
He was extremely shut down and self-
contained but recognized himself as a freeze type from reading articles on my website.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 718 (Number of characters: 384):
Getting him to talk at first was like pulling teeth, but over time I discovered that he was
engaged in daily phone contact with his narcissistic, emasculating mother. Through our work and
tremendous courage on his part, he gradually reduced the phone contact with his mother: at first
to once a week, then once a month, then only major holidays, and after a few years to almost
never.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 719 (Number of characters: 134):
When a parent is unrelentingly toxic, hearing even a few words from them can trigger the
survivor into an intense emotional flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 720 (Number of characters: 139):
I have worked with numerous clients who made
very little progress in their recovery while they maintained contact with the toxic parent[s].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 721 (Number of characters: 74):
For
this reason, such clients usually require a parentdectomy to progress.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 722 (Number of characters: 97):
There is a classic book by
Bob Hoffman on this topic entitled Getting Divorced from Mother & Dad.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 723 (Number of characters: 119):
As external freedom from “smother-mothering” continued, Joe gradually achieved more
and more internal freedom from her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 724 (Number of characters: 198):
During this time he began to experience the first meaningful
relating of his life in an ACA group that for many years provided him with a great deal of
positive companionship and relational healing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 725 (Number of characters: 135):
Joe finally concluded therapy with me when a
healthy primary relationship that he formed with a group member reached the two year mark.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 726 (Number of characters: 229):
Learning To Handle Conflict In Relationship
One caveat for recovering the ability to authentically be yourself is that it is unreasonable and
unfair to expect anyone to accept you if you are being abusively angry or contemptuous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 727 (Number of characters: 97):
Some
trauma survivors flashback into this type of behavior by acting out from their Outer Critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 728 (Number of characters: 108):
If this
is an issue for you, chapter 10 provides guidance for deconstructing this intimacy-destroying
habit.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 729 (Number of characters: 85):
In this vein, it is important to note that intimacy does not mean unconditional love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 730 (Number of characters: 136):
As John
Gottman’s scholarly research shows, a certain amount of disagreement, disaffection and
disappointment is normal in relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 731 (Number of characters: 121):
The hallmark of successful couples is their ability to
handle feelings of anger and hurt in a constructive and civil way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 732 (Number of characters: 123):
Gottman’s studies have
identified this as a key characteristic of couples who still really like each other after ten years.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 733 (Number of characters: 180):
“Tools for Lovingly Resolving Conflict” [Toolbox 4 in chapter 16] is a pragmatic list of
techniques and perspectives to help couples resolve disruptions in their mutual attunement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 734 (Number of characters: 87):
Moreover, books by the Gottmans and Sue Johnson provide a great deal of practical help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 735 (Number of characters: 90):
I also
find that Beyond The Marriage Fantasy, by Dan Beaver is especially helpful for men.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 736 (Number of characters: 63):
Reparenting

Reparenting is a key aspect of relational healing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 737 (Number of characters: 118):
It is primarily a process of addressing the many
developmentally arrested needs of the traumatized child that we were.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 738 (Number of characters: 96):
In this book we repeatedly
address the two most fundamental of these needs: love and protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 739 (Number of characters: 35):
“Suggested Intentions for Recovery”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 740 (Number of characters: 144):
[Toolbox 1 in chapter 16] renders yet another picture
of the diverse developmental arrests that may as yet be unaddressed in the Cptsd survivor.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 741 (Number of characters: 98):
The
toolbox presents these needs as tangible goals that we can use to direct our recovery efforts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 742 (Number of characters: 134):
Self-Mothering And Self-Fathering
An important, yin/yang dynamic of reparenting involves balancing self-mothering and self-
fathering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 743 (Number of characters: 197):
When a child’s mothering needs are adequately met, self-compassion is installed at the
core of her being. When the same is true of her fathering needs, self-protection also becomes
deeply imbedded.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 744 (Number of characters: 238):
Self-compassion is the domicile of recovery, and self-protection is its foundation. When
self-compassion is sufficiently established as a “home base” to return to in difficult times, an
urge to be self-protective naturally arises from it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 745 (Number of characters: 93):
Living in the world without access to these
primal instincts of survival is truly terrifying.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 746 (Number of characters: 104):
We advance our recovery process immeasurably when we commit to re-mothering and re-
fathering ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 747 (Number of characters: 106):
I encourage you now to commit to becoming an unshakeable source of
compassion and protection for yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 748 (Number of characters: 291):
Self-Mothering Grows Self-Compassion
The most essential task of self-mothering is building a deeply felt sense that we are lovable and
deserve to be loved. Self-mothering is the practice of loving and accepting the inner child in all
phases of his mental, emotional, and physical experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 749 (Number of characters: 131):
[If “inner child” is a problematic
concept for any reason, you can imagine nurturing the developmentally arrested part of yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 750 (Number of characters: 93):
]
Self-mothering is based on the precept that unconditional love is every child’s birthright.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 751 (Number of characters: 62):
Recovering from the loss of unconditional love is problematic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 752 (Number of characters: 66):
Not getting enough of it as
children was the greatest loss we had.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 753 (Number of characters: 169):
Sadly, this loss can never be completely remediated,
because unconditional love is only appropriate and developmentally helpful during the first two
years or so of life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 754 (Number of characters: 94):
After this time, the toddler has to begin to learn that human love comes with some
conditions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 755 (Number of characters: 160):
Although love still needs to be copious at this time, the child must be gently shown
that behaviors like hitting, biting and breaking things are not acceptable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 756 (Number of characters: 153):
The period of
conditional love has begun and is successfully guided via a very gradual increase in learning
about necessary and healthy limits and rules.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 757 (Number of characters: 143):
The toddler who receives good enough parenting learns relatively easily to survive the very
gradually diminishing supply of unconditional love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 758 (Number of characters: 90):
During this time she learns little by little that
other people also have rights and needs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 759 (Number of characters: 140):
Her absolute entitlement to gratification is coming to an
end, and the needs of her parents will not always be forfeited to accommodate her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 760 (Number of characters: 129):
Once again, psychological health is based on having about two years of this no questions
asked entitlement to unconditional love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 761 (Number of characters: 83):
It is the normal healthy narcissism that Freud described
as “His Majesty the Baby”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 762 (Number of characters: 123):
Serious problems accrue however when the toddler does not begin to learn that there are
limits to his original entitlement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 763 (Number of characters: 85):
If there are no limits for too long, then the journey toward adult
narcissism begins.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 764 (Number of characters: 94):
On the other hand, if there are too many limits too soon, the matrix of trauma
begins to form.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 765 (Number of characters: 55):
Enlightened parents introduce limits slowly but surely.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 766 (Number of characters: 154):
They do it at such a rate that by the
time the child reaches adolescence he can balance satisfying his needs with helping his intimates
to satisfy theirs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 767 (Number of characters: 117):
He learns to be sharing and reciprocal, a developmental task that is essential to
keeping intimacy alive in his life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 768 (Number of characters: 240):
Cptsd is a syndrome of the dearth of unconditional love, or what the great therapist, Carl
Rogers, called “unconditional positive regard”. Cptsd can also occur when unconditional love is
shut off in an all-or-nothing way in early childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 769 (Number of characters: 39):
Some parents can shower love on babies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 770 (Number of characters: 127):
But as soon as the child begins toddling around
and expressing a will of her own, they become severely punishing and rejecting.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 771 (Number of characters: 165):
The Limits Of Unconditional Love
