The terrible absence of love - or its abrupt premature termination - is extremely painful and its
loss is very difficult to address.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 772 (Number of characters: 175):
We cannot help desperately wanting the unconditional love we
were so unfairly deprived of, but we cannot, as adults, expect others to supply our unmet early
entitlement needs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 773 (Number of characters: 97):
The one exception to this is therapy, but that of course is usually only one or two hours a
week.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 774 (Number of characters: 343):
Miraculously, I have seen the unconditional positive regard of the therapist be enough on
numerous occasions to significantly repair the damage of not being parentally loved. And when
it is enough, the therapist’s consistent caring facilitates the awakening of the developmentally
arrested need to hold yourself with enough unconditional love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 775 (Number of characters: 152):
We survivors often struggle with managing our understandable but unrealistic yearnings to
receive permanent unconditional love from a friend or partner.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 776 (Number of characters: 72):
Like the toddler, we eventually
have to accept the limits of adult love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 777 (Number of characters: 112):
This is especially true in romance where the intoxication
of unconditional love rarely lasts for more than year.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 778 (Number of characters: 134):
Around this time, partners inevitably begin
to feel some frustration with each other because of differences in their individual needs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 779 (Number of characters: 164):
Nonetheless, romantic love can be a significant source of therapeutic unconditional-like
love, especially when it survives the inevitability of some disappointment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 780 (Number of characters: 208):
Susan Campbell’s A
Couples’ Journey is a pragmatic, research-based book on how to reap more intimacy out of
normal relationship disappointments
Inner Child Work
Let us return to the concept of self-mothering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 781 (Number of characters: 102):
As mother to ourselves, we commit to increasing
our self-compassion and unconditional positive regard.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 782 (Number of characters: 84):
Self-mothering is a resolute refusal to
indulge in self-hatred and self-abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 783 (Number of characters: 77):
It proceeds from the realization that self-

punishment is counterproductive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 784 (Number of characters: 153):
It is enhanced by the understanding that patience and self-
encouragement are more effective than self-judgment and self-rejection in achieving recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 785 (Number of characters: 165):
You can enhance your self-mothering skills by imaginatively creating a safe place in your
heart where your inner child and your present time self are always welcome.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 786 (Number of characters: 181):
Consistent
tenderness towards yourself welcomes the child into the adult body you now inhabit, and shows
him that it is now a nurturing place protected by a warm and powerful adult.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 787 (Number of characters: 165):
Self-mothering can be enhanced by thought-correcting the critic’s negative messages with
healing words that the child in all likelihood never heard from his parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 788 (Number of characters: 193):
A client of mine once
shared this pearl of wisdom with me: “Thoughts - just mere thoughts - are as powerful as electric
batteries - as good for you as sunlight is, or as bad for you as poison.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 789 (Number of characters: 100):
Here then are some useful messages for nurturing the growth of your self-compassion and
self-esteem.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 790 (Number of characters: 115):
I recommend that you imagine speaking them to your inner child, especially when
you are suffering with a flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 791 (Number of characters: 52):
Reparenting Affirmations
I am so glad you were born.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 792 (Number of characters: 22):
You are a good person.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 793 (Number of characters: 66):
I love who you are and am doing my best to always be on your side.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 794 (Number of characters: 55):
You can come to me whenever you’re feeling hurt or bad.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 795 (Number of characters: 60):
You do not have to be perfect to get my love and protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 796 (Number of characters: 38):
All of your feelings are okay with me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 797 (Number of characters: 28):
I am always glad to see you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 798 (Number of characters: 88):
It is okay for you to be angry and I won’t let you hurt yourself or others when you are.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 799 (Number of characters: 47):
You can make mistakes - they are your teachers.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 800 (Number of characters: 44):
You can know what you need and ask for help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 801 (Number of characters: 45):
You can have your own preferences and tastes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 802 (Number of characters: 29):
You are a delight to my eyes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 803 (Number of characters: 31):
You can choose your own values.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 804 (Number of characters: 67):
You can pick your own friends, and you don’t have to like everyone.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 805 (Number of characters: 77):
You can sometimes feel confused and ambivalent, and not know all the answers.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 806 (Number of characters: 23):
I am very proud of you.

chunk 807 (Number of characters: 182):
Self-Fathering And Time Machine Rescue Operation
Many abandoned children enter adulthood feeling that the world is a dangerous place where they
are ill-equipped to defend themselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 808 (Number of characters: 285):
While self-mothering focuses primarily on healing the
wounds of neglect, self-fathering heals the wounds of being helpless to protect yourself from
parental abuse, and by extension from other abusive authority figures. Self-fathering aims at building assertiveness and self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 809 (Number of characters: 171):
It includes learning to
effectively confront external and/or internal abuse, as well as standing up for the adult child’s
rights, as described in Tool Box 2 of chapter 16.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 810 (Number of characters: 80):
Many survivors benefit greatly from classes and
books on assertiveness training.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 811 (Number of characters: 81):
One of my favorite self-fathering exercises is the time machine rescue operation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 812 (Number of characters: 51):
I have

used it to help myself and to help clients.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 813 (Number of characters: 141):
With clients I use it to model a process for fighting off
the overwhelming sense of helplessness that often accompanies emotional flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 814 (Number of characters: 105):
This is a version of the time machine rescue operation that I use with myself as well as with
my clients.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 815 (Number of characters: 136):
I tell my inner child that, if time travel is ever possible, I will travel back into the past
and put a stop to my parents’ abusiveness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 816 (Number of characters: 56):
In the course of this I say things like: “I’ll call 911.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 817 (Number of characters: 13):
I’ll call CPS

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 818 (Number of characters: 36):
[Child Protective Services] on them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 819 (Number of characters: 89):
I will grab their arms and pin them behind their
backs the second they try to strike you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 820 (Number of characters: 90):
I will muffle them with a gag so they can’t scream at you
or even mumble their criticisms.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 821 (Number of characters: 67):
I’ll put bags over their heads so they can’t frown or glare at you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 822 (Number of characters: 38):
I’ll send them to bed without dessert.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 823 (Number of characters: 51):
I’ll do anything you want me to do to protect you.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 824 (Number of characters: 119):
Such imagery often provides me an exit out of fear and shame, and sometimes even makes
my inner child laugh in delight.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 825 (Number of characters: 180):
I sometimes finish this exercise by telling my inner child I would
also report my parents to the authorities so they would be sent to counseling to learn how to be a
better parent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 826 (Number of characters: 133):
Or, I say that, if I could, I would take him back to live with me in the future before all those
horrible things could happen to him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 827 (Number of characters: 109):
I remind him that he in fact lives in the present with me
now, where I will always do my best to protect him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 828 (Number of characters: 124):
We now have a powerful body, greater
skills of self-protection and access to allies and a legal system that will protect us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 829 (Number of characters: 173):
When the recoveree consistently welcomes his inner child in every aspect of his being, the
child feels increasingly safe and becomes more and more alive and self-expressive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 830 (Number of characters: 174):
As he
experiences his adult self consistently rising to his defense, he will feel safe enough to begin
accessing his innate vitality, playfulness, curiosity, and spontaneity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 831 (Number of characters: 164):
Reparenting By Committee
Reparenting at its best is a yin/yang dynamic that balances the mutually enhancing processes of
reparenting by others and self-reparenting.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 832 (Number of characters: 181):
Reparenting sometimes needs to be initiated and
modeled by someone else, such as a therapist, a sponsor, a kind friend or supportive group to
show us how to self-reparent ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 833 (Number of characters: 150):
Alternatively, many survivors instinctively initiate reparenting by others, via entering what
one of my clients describes as “the community of books”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 834 (Number of characters: 89):
They receive reparenting from authors
who encourage them to value and support themselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 835 (Number of characters: 26):
Alice was such a survivor.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 836 (Number of characters: 174):
Her family traumatized her during childhood so thoroughly that
she quickly learned that being vulnerable around others was dangerous, foolish and totally out of
the question.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 837 (Number of characters: 159):
Yet the urge to get the support and the help she was so unfairly deprived of worked
its way back into her awareness via a strong attraction to self-help books.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 838 (Number of characters: 214):
By reading a great deal
of psychology, she eventually found enough help that she began to think that there might be a
kind, safe and helpful person out there in the flesh and entered into some very helpful therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 839 (Number of characters: 98):
[Chapter 15, Bibliotherapy, contains my favorite recommendations for therapeutic self-help
books].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 840 (Number of characters: 396):
I too went through a long gradual process of reading and attending lectures before I was
able to take the frightening and embarrassing plunge into therapy, where, as stated earlier, I was
fortunate enough to find a good enough therapist to take my relational healing to the next level. Therapy allowed me to internalize and mimic my therapists’ consistent and reliable stance
of being on my side.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 841 (Number of characters: 83):
This in turn led me to gravitate toward safer and more truly intimate

friendships.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 842 (Number of characters: 63):
I have seen this same result with numerous clients and friends.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 843 (Number of characters: 192):
Eventually, I achieved my first earned secure attachment outside of therapy and was
subsequently ready to let go of therapy as the only place where I could have deep and
meaningful connection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 844 (Number of characters: 130):
I believe the need to have mothering- and fathering-type support from others is a lifelong
need and not just limited to childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 845 (Number of characters: 143):
Fortunately I am now blessed many years later to
experience a multileveled form of reparenting by others which I call reparenting by committee.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 846 (Number of characters: 190):
I
conceptualize reparenting by committee as a circle of friends that has varying layers and levels of
intimacy. The inner circle of my reparenting committee includes my five closest friends.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 847 (Number of characters: 99):
I think of this inner circle as friends with whom nothing is too vulnerable or taboo to talk
about.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 848 (Number of characters: 123):
My wife, a therapist friend, my exercise buddy and two members of a long term men’s
group that I was in are in this circle.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 849 (Number of characters: 110):
This circle also has an outer layer of people who would be
inner if circumstances allowed me to see them more.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 850 (Number of characters: 290):
Outside this orb are levels of succeeding less intimate, yet still meaningful circles of
relationship. The next circle out is intimates who I rarely see anymore but who have shared
enough intimacy with me in the past that I now draw comfort from imagining them caring for me
in the present.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 851 (Number of characters: 208):
My deceased grandmother is in this circle as are three of my former therapists, a
couple of army buddies, old high school and college friends, and my four best friends from the
ten years I lived in Australia.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 852 (Number of characters: 204):
The next circle out from this consists of my nurse practitioner, the body worker I
occasionally see, some therapist colleagues and the wise old school librarian who helps me pick
books for my son to read.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 853 (Number of characters: 263):
The next circle out from this are friends I play sports with, parents of my son’s friends and
people in my neighborhood with whom my contact is not especially vulnerable, but with whom
there is an easy chemistry that adds to my general overall sense of belonging.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 854 (Number of characters: 127):
And the final circle is occasional strangers, who from time to time, I am graced to have easy
and comforting interactions with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 855 (Number of characters: 227):
I also know various survivors whose effective recovery practices have similarly rewarded
them with enough portions of love from a variety of others that their childhood starvation for
help and support is significantly assuaged.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 856 (Number of characters: 96):
And like me, their committees, started with the first
person they had good enough intimacy with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 857 (Number of characters: 117):
Counting yourself, this then is a committee of two,
which with grace can then build slowly, one friendship at a time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 858 (Number of characters: 115):
The Tao Of Self-Relating And Relating To Others
Recovering is therefore enhanced on every level by safe human help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 859 (Number of characters: 201):
Once again however,
survivors with especially harsh betrayal histories may need to do a great deal of work on other
levels before they are ready to risk the vulnerability of opening to relational help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 860 (Number of characters: 136):
Nonetheless, deep level recovering, as well as healthy “human-being” is typically a
vacillating blend of self-help and help from others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 861 (Number of characters: 197):
Relational work helps heal the initial wound
of family abandonment, and self work decreases the self-abandonment that occurs because the
child was forced to imitate his parents’ abandonment of him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 862 (Number of characters: 219):
The more time you practice the
various techniques of self-care described throughout this book, the less time you spend in self-
abandonment. With enough persistence, self-care becomes an invaluable, irreplaceable habit.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 863 (Number of characters: 82):
In advanced recovery, self-help and relational-help blend in an all important Tao.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 864 (Number of characters: 69):
A Tao is a
yin/yang combination of opposite and complementary forces.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 865 (Number of characters: 105):
The Tao of relational recovery
involves balancing healthy independence with healthy dependence on others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 866 (Number of characters: 331):
For the survivor, this therapeutic synthesis can come into being when an improved
supportive relationship with yourself allows you to choose and open to a helpful relationship. Sometimes simultaneously, the attainment of a safe, supportive relationship with another person
promotes the growth of your ability to be self-supportive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 867 (Number of characters: 89):
This then rewards you with a decrease
in your automatic tendency toward self-abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 868 (Number of characters: 149):
Complementarily, this then fosters the
gradual development of community – the vital life resource that you were so unfairly deprived of
in childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 869 (Number of characters: 145):
The more self-supportive we become the more we attract supportive others. The more we
are supported by others, the more we can support ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 870 (Number of characters: 147):
Sometimes we get initiated into this
dynamic Tao by our own efforts - sometimes by the grace of finding a supportive friend or
professional helper.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 871 (Number of characters: 210):
For many of us survivors a considerable amount of self-help work has to take place before
we are able to open to relational support – before we become discerning enough to choose truly
safe and helpful support.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 872 (Number of characters: 128):
THE PROGRESSION OF RECOVERING
Signs Of Recovering
Effective recovery work leads to an ongoing reduction of emotional flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 873 (Number of characters: 89):
Over time, with
enough practice, you become more proficient at managing triggered states.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 874 (Number of characters: 92):
This in turn results in
flashbacks occurring less often, less intensely and less enduringly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 875 (Number of characters: 250):
Another key sign of recovering is that your critic begins to shrink and lose its dominance
over your psyche. As it shrinks, your user-friendly ego has room to grow and to develop the kind
of mindfulness that recognizes when the critic has taken over.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 876 (Number of characters: 104):
This in turn allows you to
progressively reject the critic’s perfectionistic and drasticizing processes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 877 (Number of characters: 64):
More and more, you
stop persecuting yourself for normal foibles.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 878 (Number of characters: 88):
Additionally, you perseverate less in
disappointment about other people’s minor miscues.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 879 (Number of characters: 76):
A further sign of recovering is a gradual increase in your ability to relax.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 880 (Number of characters: 87):
With this comes
an increasing ability to resist overreacting from a triggered position.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 881 (Number of characters: 335):
This further allows you to
use your fight, flight, freeze and fawn instincts in healthy and non-self-destructive ways. This
means you only fight back when under real attack, only flee when odds are insurmountable, only
freeze when you need to go into acute observation mode, and only fawn when it is appropriate to
be self-sacrificing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 882 (Number of characters: 141):
An alternative way of describing this decrease in overreacting is that you have a good
balance between the polar opposites of fight and fawn.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 883 (Number of characters: 138):
As this becomes increasingly realized,
you vacillate healthily between asserting your own needs and compromising with the needs of
others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 884 (Number of characters: 127):
A further example of decreased reactivity is seen in a more balanced movement between the
polar opposites of flight and freeze.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 885 (Number of characters: 176):
This manifests as an improving equilibrium between doing
and being, between sympathetic and parasympathetic nervous system arousal, and between left
and right-brain processing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 886 (Number of characters: 143):
The importance of balancing the fight-fawn and flight-freeze

polarities within yourself is explored in greater detail at the end of chapter 6.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 887 (Number of characters: 100):
Deep-level recovery is also evidenced by you becoming gradually more relaxed in safe
enough company.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 888 (Number of characters: 110):
This in turn leads to an increasing capacity to be more authentic and
vulnerable in trustworthy relationships.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 889 (Number of characters: 174):
With enough grace, this may then culminate in you
acquiring an intimate, mutually supportive relationship where each of you can be there for the
other through thick and thin.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 890 (Number of characters: 118):
Advanced recovery also correlates with letting go of the salvation fantasy that you will
never have another flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 891 (Number of characters: 103):
Giving up the salvation fantasy is another one of those two steps
forward, one step backward processes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 892 (Number of characters: 141):
We typically have to wrestle with denial a great deal to
increasingly accept the unfair reality that we will never be totally flashback-free.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 893 (Number of characters: 168):
Unless we do
however, we impair our ability to easily recognize and quickly respond to flashbacks from a
position of self-compassion, self-soothing and self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 894 (Number of characters: 136):
The Stages Of Recovering
Although we often work on many levels of recovering at the same time, recovering is to some
degree progressive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 895 (Number of characters: 109):
It begins on the cognitive level when psychoeducation and mindfulness helps
us understand that we have Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 896 (Number of characters: 129):
This awakening then allows us to learn how to approach the
journey of deconstructing the various life-spoiling dynamics of Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 897 (Number of characters: 96):
Still on the cognitive level, we take our next steps into the long work of shrinking the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 898 (Number of characters: 167):
Some survivors will need to do a great deal of work on this level before they can move down to
the emotional layer of work which is learning how to grieve effectively.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 899 (Number of characters: 202):
The phase of intensely grieving our childhood losses can last for a couple of years. When
sufficient progress is made in grieving, the survivor naturally drops down into the next level of
recovery work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 900 (Number of characters: 79):
This involves working through fear by grieving our loss of safety in the world.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 901 (Number of characters: 101):
At
this level, we also learn to work through our toxic shame by grieving the loss of our self-esteem.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 902 (Number of characters: 155):
As we become more adept in this type of deep level grieving, we are then ready to address
the core issue of our trauma – the abandonment depression itself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 903 (Number of characters: 158):
Work here involves releasing
the armoring and physiological reactivity in our body to the abandonment depression via the
somatic work discussed in chapter 12.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 904 (Number of characters: 110):
This work culminates with learning to compassionately
support ourselves through our experiences of depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 905 (Number of characters: 201):
Finally, as we will learn more about in chapter 13, many survivors need some relational
help in achieving the complex tasks involved in deconstructing each layer of our old pain-
exacerbating defenses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 906 (Number of characters: 112):
Cultivating Patience With The Gradual Progression Of Recovery
As stated earlier, recovery from Cptsd is complex.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 907 (Number of characters: 127):
Sometimes, it can feel so hopelessly complex
that we totally give up and get stuck in inertia for considerable lengths of time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 908 (Number of characters: 205):
This is why it is
so important to understand that recovery is gradual and frequently a backwards and forwards
process. Effective recovery is often limited to only progressing in one or two areas at a time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 909 (Number of characters: 103):
Biting
off more than we can chew and trying to accomplish too much too soon is often
counterproductive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 910 (Number of characters: 133):
As a flight type, I spent years in mid-range recovery workaholically spinning

my wheels trying to fix and change everything at once.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 911 (Number of characters: 122):
I describe this at greater length in the
“When Recovery becomes Obsessive-Compulsive” section of my first book [p140-141].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 912 (Number of characters: 66):
We often need to simplify our self-help efforts in early recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 913 (Number of characters: 124):
Accordingly, I
recommend making shrinking the critic [chapter 9] your “go to” response if you feel unsure of
how to proceed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 914 (Number of characters: 172):
Once the critic is reduced enough that you can notice increasing periods of your brain being
user-friendly, impulses to help and care for yourself naturally begin to arise.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 915 (Number of characters: 95):
As this happens it
becomes easier to tell whether you are guiding yourself with love or a whip.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 916 (Number of characters: 179):
When you realize
it’s the whip, please try to disarm your critic and treat yourself with the kindness you would
extend to any young child who is struggling and having a hard time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 917 (Number of characters: 82):
Nowhere is patience with ourselves more important than with the inner critic work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 918 (Number of characters: 76):
Typically the
inner critic is too omnipresent to confront on every occasion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 919 (Number of characters: 53):
To do so would often leave no time
for anything else.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 920 (Number of characters: 189):
But when we practice critic-shrinking in a gradually increasing way over time, we can more
consistently disidentify from its negative focus and switch to a more self-supportive perspective.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 921 (Number of characters: 101):
Eventually a new positive habit of rescuing ourselves from shame and self-hate takes on its own
life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 922 (Number of characters: 91):
I still have my unfair share of flashbacks, but rarely do I ever side with my toxic critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 923 (Number of characters: 88):
Any self-help practices that we are trying to make second nature often work in this way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 924 (Number of characters: 77):
When we practice enough, self-help starts to become a matter of common sense.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 925 (Number of characters: 162):
It reverberates
as right action and gradually takes on its own life as we attune to the true nature of our spirits
and souls which are inherently self-supportive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 926 (Number of characters: 146):
We also aid our recovery greatly by challenging the all-or-none thinking of the critic whenever it
judges us for not being perfect in our efforts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 927 (Number of characters: 90):
“Progress not perfection” is a powerful mantra for
guiding our self-help recovery efforts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 928 (Number of characters: 150):
Moreover as recovering progresses, and especially as the critic shrinks, the desire to help
yourself- to care for yourself - becomes more spontaneous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 929 (Number of characters: 97):
This is especially true when we
mindfully do things for ourselves in a spirit of loving-kindness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 930 (Number of characters: 192):
As such, we can do it for the
child we were – the child who was deprived through no fault of her own. And, we can do it
because we believe every child, without exception, deserves loving care.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 931 (Number of characters: 180):
Finally, if the reader is like I was in the past and has no overall perspective on his suffering,
he may feel like he is spinning his wheels on one icy patch of road after another.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 932 (Number of characters: 117):
I had decades of
trying everything under the sun with what felt like a deepening sense of futility and
defectiveness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 933 (Number of characters: 105):
Gratefully, I eventually reached an invisible critical mass, and realized I had
actually come a long way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 934 (Number of characters: 128):
I had acquired quite a few pieces in this puzzle of recovery, and only
needed to organize them into a map to move along further.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 935 (Number of characters: 167):
As such, I have designed a ground
plan that has helped me, my clients and website respondents to make sense of their suffering and
to see how to effectively reduce it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 936 (Number of characters: 77):
I hope and pray that the cartography in this book will also
offer you relief.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 937 (Number of characters: 115):
Surviving Versus Thriving
Recovery involves learning to handle unpredictable shifts in our inner emotional weather.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 938 (Number of characters: 88):
Perhaps the ultimate dimension of this is what I call the Surviving 
Thriving
continuum.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 939 (Number of characters: 301):
Before we enter into recovery, it may feel like life is nothing but a struggle to survive. However, when recovery progresses enough, we begin to have some experiences of feeling like
we are thriving. These may start out as feelings of optimism, hopefulness and certainty that we
are indeed recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 940 (Number of characters: 89):
And then, the bottom inevitably drops out because recovery is never all forward progress.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 941 (Number of characters: 66):
Oh so unfairly, we are back to feeling that we can barely survive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 942 (Number of characters: 81):
To make matters worse, we are
amnesiac that we even had a respite from surviving.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 943 (Number of characters: 87):
Another flashback has hit and we polarize
back onto the surviving end of the continuum.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 944 (Number of characters: 77):
We are stuck in the anxious and deadened feelings
of the abandonment mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 945 (Number of characters: 97):
In survival mode, even the most trivial and normally easy task can feel excruciatingly
difficult.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 946 (Number of characters: 47):
As in childhood, it is all feels just too hard.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 947 (Number of characters: 86):
And if the flashback is especially intense,
Thanatos may start knocking down the door.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 948 (Number of characters: 133):
Thanatos is the death urge described by Freud and
in a flashback it corresponds with the suicidal ideation we looked at in chapter 1.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 949 (Number of characters: 150):
Once again, it is important to repeat that this feeling-state is a flashback to the worst times
in childhood when our will to live was so compromised.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 950 (Number of characters: 162):
As mindfulness improves we can
recognize suicidal ideation as evidence of a flashback and begin to rescue ourselves with the
chapter 8 flashback management steps.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 951 (Number of characters: 128):
As recovery progresses, polarizations back into survival mode do not take us to the utter
despair end of the continuum so often.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 952 (Number of characters: 134):
Nonetheless survival mode can still feel pretty awful,
especially when it is characterized by high anxiety or immobilizing depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 953 (Number of characters: 179):
Being in survival is especially difficult during those times when flashback management is
less effective, and feelings that life is a struggle can hang on for days and even weeks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 954 (Number of characters: 71):
This is the
territory where flashbacks morph into extended regressions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 955 (Number of characters: 102):
I believe regressions are sometimes a call from our psyche to address important
developmental arrests.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 956 (Number of characters: 105):
In this case, it is the need to learn unrelenting self-acceptance during a
period of extended difficulty.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 957 (Number of characters: 81):
It is also the need to develop a staunch and unyielding sense of
self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 958 (Number of characters: 163):
This fundamental instinct of fiery willingness to defend ourselves from
unfairness needs to strengthen progressively so that we can withstand inner critic attacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 959 (Number of characters: 152):
Moreover we can grow in our ability to survive “survival” by using the chapter 13
mindfulness techniques to practice and build enduring self-compassion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 960 (Number of characters: 168):
Moreover, if we are far
enough along in recovery to have a safe ally, we can enlist their support to help us verbally
ventilate out our pain at being stuck in survival.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 961 (Number of characters: 126):
Temptations can be great at such times to revert to the less functional ways of self-soothing
that we learned when we younger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 962 (Number of characters: 133):
Depending on your 4F type this commonly manifests as
increased eating, substance abuse, working, sleeping and/or sexually acting out.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 963 (Number of characters: 149):
Sometimes we are triggered into self-medicating in this way because we are desperately
trying to keep ourselves on the thriving end of the continuum.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 964 (Number of characters: 119):
Desperately clinging to thriving is
a hard impulse to resist, even when we are in reality way past its expiration date.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 965 (Number of characters: 142):
Yet as recovery and mindfulness increase we begin to notice that this type of self-

medicating indicates that we are in a survival-flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 966 (Number of characters: 68):
We are no longer authentically on the
thriving end of the continuum.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 967 (Number of characters: 124):
We have compounded our regression, by regressing further - by
self-medicating to unnaturally prolong a preferred experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 968 (Number of characters: 174):
At such times, we benefit most by
reinvoking our intention to practice self-acceptance – by recommitting to being there for
ourselves no matter where we are on the continuum.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 969 (Number of characters: 128):
As bears repeating, all human beings are existentially challenged to handle disappointing
shifts out of thriving into surviving.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 970 (Number of characters: 150):
We survivors however have greater difficulties handling
these transitions because we were abandoned for so long at the surviving end of the continuum.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 971 (Number of characters: 299):
Yet as our recovery progresses, we can learn to become increasingly self-supportive in times of
being stuck in survival.
Difficulties In Identifying The Signs Of Recovering
Some readers may work on their recovery for a long time, and erroneously and shamefully feel
they are not making any progress.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 972 (Number of characters: 171):
Because of the all-or-none thinking that typically accompanies
Cptsd, survivors in the early stages of recovery often fail to notice or validate their own actual
progress.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 973 (Number of characters: 127):
If we do not notice the degrees of our own improvement in our recovery work, we are in
great danger of giving up on recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 974 (Number of characters: 141):
Because of black-and-white thinking, we can regularly
fall into the trap of not acknowledging and valuing what we are actually accomplishing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 975 (Number of characters: 86):
Perfectionistic dismissal of improvement that is not 100% is common in early recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 976 (Number of characters: 140):
Here are some common areas where I see that recovering survivors fail to notice and self-
validate their progressive degrees of improvement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 977 (Number of characters: 2):
1.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 978 (Number of characters: 44):
Less intense launching into a 4F response
2.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 979 (Number of characters: 104):
Increasing resistance to the critic
3. Increased Mindfulness about flashbacks or inner critic attacks
4.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 980 (Number of characters: 52):
Increased time feeling good enough about yourself
5.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 981 (Number of characters: 64):
Progress in meeting arrested developments listed in chapter 2
6.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 982 (Number of characters: 60):
Decreased overeating or use of self-medicating substances
7.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 983 (Number of characters: 60):
Increased experiences of good enough relating with others
8.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 984 (Number of characters: 308):
Decrease in the painfulness and intensity of flashback feelings
In terms of number 3 above, it is important to note that even when mindfulness does not
immediately terminate a flashback or critic attack, noticing and identifying these Cptsd
phenomena is more progressive than just being blindly lost in them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 985 (Number of characters: 82):
Moreover, ongoing
recognition makes effective ameliorative action more accessible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 986 (Number of characters: 102):
It makes us increasingly likely
to remember to use the flashback management steps listed in chapter 8.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 987 (Number of characters: 138):
Furthermore, it is important that we notice the gradually decreasing intensity of the
flashback feelings of anxiety, shame and depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 988 (Number of characters: 179):
In this regard, social anxiety can gradually
reduce along a continuum that stretches from panicky withdrawal... to a more tolerable social
discomfort... to periods of social ease.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 989 (Number of characters: 231):
Additionally, depression can gradually diminish along a
continuum that stretches from paralyzing despair... to anhedonia – an inability to enjoy normal
life pleasures... to a state of tired, and relatively unmotivated peacefulness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 990 (Number of characters: 88):
Of course both these

processes typically improve at a vacillating, back-and-forth rate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 991 (Number of characters: 155):
As I write this I feel some old sadness about the many decades that I judged my emotional
tone and mood as either good or bad in a very all-or-nothing way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 992 (Number of characters: 288):
If I was not feeling very good
than I felt as if everything was really bad. And since feeling very good is something most human
beings only get to experience a relatively small proportion of the time, my perception of feeling
bad became a much more dominant experience than was necessary.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 993 (Number of characters: 125):
In fact, mildly unpleasant
feeling typically morphed me quickly into feeling terrible via shame-tinged, all-or-none thinking.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 994 (Number of characters: 285):
I am so grateful for the life-changing epiphany that lead me to trade in my old primary
aspiration of “Celebration” for my new one of “Serenity.”
Inner critic thought processes refute signs of progress whenever a new flashback occurs, no
matter how much less intense it is than before.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 995 (Number of characters: 166):
Every recurrence of feeling shame, fear or
depression is interpreted as proof that nothing has changed, even when there are increasing
periods of not being triggered.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 996 (Number of characters: 97):
The critic’s black-and-white assessment is: “Either I’m cured or I’m still hopelessly
defective.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 997 (Number of characters: 269):
And once you identify with your critic’s pronouncement of defectiveness, you are off
and spiraling downward into a full-fledged flashback - captured once again in the ice veneer of
toxic shame that freezes one in the Cptsd stranglehold of helplessness and hopelessness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 998 (Number of characters: 140):
Accepting Recovery As A Lifelong Process It is exceedingly difficult to accept the proposition – the fact – that recovery is never complete.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 999 (Number of characters: 356):
And although we can expect our flashbacks to markedly decrease over time, it is tremendously
difficult, and sometimes impossible, to let go of the salvation fantasy that we will one day be
forever free of them. Yet when we do not loosen our grip on the salvation fantasy, we remain extremely
susceptible to blaming ourselves every time we have a flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1000 (Number of characters: 257):
Understanding this is so crucial
because recovery typically progresses in a process that has many temporary regressions. Moreover, most recoverees often have the unfortunate subjective experience that the temporary
regression feels as permanent as concrete.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1001 (Number of characters: 233):
This is especially true because of the interminability
feeling of flashbacks. When we flashback, we regress to our child-mind which was incapable of
imagining a future any different than the everlasting present of being so abandoned.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1002 (Number of characters: 102):
So how can we come to bear the knowledge that our awful childhoods have created some
permanent damage?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1003 (Number of characters: 348):
It helps me to see my Cptsd as somewhat analogous to diabetes, i.e., a
condition that will need management throughout my life. This is a piece of bad news that
naturally feels offensively unpalatable, but the good news, as with diabetes, is that as we become
more skilled at flashback management, Cptsd can gradually become infrequently bothersome.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1004 (Number of characters: 95):
And even more importantly, we can evolve towards leading increasingly rich and rewarding
lives.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1005 (Number of characters: 83):
Even better news is that Cptsd, when efficiently managed, eventually bestows gifts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1006 (Number of characters: 124):
It
comes with significant silver linings - unavailable to those less traumatized - as we will see at the
end of the chapter.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1007 (Number of characters: 183):
Therapeutic Flashbacks And Growing Pains

Healing from childhood trauma is also a long gradual process because recovering your full self-
expression requires a great deal of practice.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1008 (Number of characters: 59):
Being yourself can be intimidating and flashback-
inducing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1009 (Number of characters: 88):
Healthy self-assertion was punished like a capital crime in many dysfunctional
families.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1010 (Number of characters: 101):
Expressing yourself in ways that your parents forbade typically triggers intense
flashbacks at first.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1011 (Number of characters: 112):
This can cause you to lose sight of how this practice gradually reduces the
chronic pain of remaining invisible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1012 (Number of characters: 105):
We can encourage ourselves to face these growing pains by conceptualizing them as
therapeutic flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1013 (Number of characters: 208):
We then choose to weather these flashbacks to stop the past from holding
us back, to reclaim the fundamental human rights that our parents denied us, and to finally own
what is rightfully ours for the taking.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1014 (Number of characters: 130):
We can further bolster ourselves for such necessary flashbacks by comparing “speaking up”
to going to the dentist for a toothache.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1015 (Number of characters: 125):
Unless we accept the acute pain of the dentist’s
therapeutic procedure, we will suffer chronic dental discomfit indefinitely.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1016 (Number of characters: 75):
Unless we speak up,
the loneliness of our silence will imprison us forever.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1017 (Number of characters: 135):
Recovering from overwhelmingly painful childhoods is also so difficult because we
understandably want to avoid any further pain at all.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1018 (Number of characters: 78):
We may even believe that we need to risk a
flashback and practice speaking up.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1019 (Number of characters: 131):
But at the moment of facing the triggering that silence can so
easily avoid, we cannot sometimes help giving up and remaining mute.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1020 (Number of characters: 98):
However, if we are ever to recover our real voice, we must sometimes invoke the energy of
bravery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1021 (Number of characters: 43):
Bravery is, in my opinion, defined by fear.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1022 (Number of characters: 47):
It is taking right action despite being afraid.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1023 (Number of characters: 48):
It is not brave to do things that are not scary.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1024 (Number of characters: 73):
The anger work described in chapter 11 can help you with this enormously.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1025 (Number of characters: 141):
With a strong
enough intention you can begin by occasionally invoking the kind of courage that involves
feeling the fear and doing it anyway.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1026 (Number of characters: 108):
You can nudge yourself to do it to rescue your inner child
from the loneliness of never being seen or heard.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1027 (Number of characters: 145):
Moreover, when we embrace this practice we will eventually learn that fear does not have
to disabling. We can be afraid and still act powerfully.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1028 (Number of characters: 135):
We can refuse to tolerate never speaking
up, never having our say, never stating a preference, and never saying “no” to set a boundary.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1029 (Number of characters: 166):
With enough practice, therapeutic flashbacks not only diminish, but begin to be replaced by
a healthy sense of pride in ourselves for our courageous self-championing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1030 (Number of characters: 75):
More and more we
are rewarded with feelings of safe belonging in the world.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1031 (Number of characters: 155):
It is crucial for deeper level recovery that we learn that feelings of fear, shame and guilt are
sometimes signs that we have said or done the right thing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1032 (Number of characters: 101):
They are emotional flashbacks to how
we were traumatized for trying to claim normal human privileges.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1033 (Number of characters: 152):
As our recovery progresses, we need to learn to endure these feelings. Reinterpreting the
deeper meaning of these feelings is key to accomplishing this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1034 (Number of characters: 54):
Typically this involves epiphanies
like the following.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1035 (Number of characters: 66):
“I feel afraid now, but I am not in danger like I was as a child.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1036 (Number of characters: 147):
“I feel guilty
not because I am guilty, but because I was intimidated into feeling guilty for expressing my
opinions, my needs and my preferences.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1037 (Number of characters: 67):
“I feel shame because my parents rained disgust on me
for being me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1038 (Number of characters: 106):
I say no to these toxic parental curses, and I am proud and right to see how they
tried to murder my soul.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1039 (Number of characters: 198):
I give them their shame back as disgust – the disgust any healthy adult

feels when he sees a parent bullying a child with contempt, or when he sees a parent heartlessly
ignoring a suffering child.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1040 (Number of characters: 195):
Optimal Stress
The quest to ongoingly grow and evolve out of my childhood trauma sometimes becomes more
embraceable to me when I remember the poet’s words: “He not busy being born is busy dying.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1041 (Number of characters: 116):
In fact, some of the latest research in neuroscience suggests that we actually need a modicum of
stress in our life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1042 (Number of characters: 425):
This type of stress is called optimal stress. Optimal stress is the balanced, moderate amount of stress that appears to be necessary to
grow the new neurons and neuronal connections that correlate with keeping the brain healthy. Research shows that just as too much stress creates a biochemical condition that damages
neurons in the brain, too little stress leads to the atrophy, death and lack of replacement of old
neurons.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1043 (Number of characters: 196):
This is why lifelong learning is widely recognized as one of the key practices necessary
to avoid Alzheimer’s disease. In my opinion, lifelong recovering is an exalted subset of lifelong learning.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1044 (Number of characters: 122):
I believe that
optimal stress is frequently attained when we practice the behaviors that remedy our
developmental arrests.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1045 (Number of characters: 241):
Examples of this include reading self-help books, attending self-
improvement workshops, working at deeper self-discovery through journaling, or struggling to
be more vulnerable and authentic in a therapy session or an evolving relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1046 (Number of characters: 81):
Moreover, it
might be that minor flashbacks sometimes function as optimal stress.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1047 (Number of characters: 112):
I certainly know a number
of long term recoverees who seem to be evolving and becoming sharper in their old age.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1048 (Number of characters: 14):
SILVER LININGS

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1049 (Number of characters: 169):
We live in an emotionally impoverished culture, and those who stick with a long term recovery
process are often rewarded with emotional intelligence far beyond the norm.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1050 (Number of characters: 315):
This is somewhat
paradoxical, as survivors of childhood trauma are initially injured more grievously in their
emotional natures than those in the general population. The silver lining in this, however, is that many of us were forced to consciously address our
suffering because our wounding was so much more severe.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1051 (Number of characters: 174):
Those who work an effective
recovery program not only recover significantly from emotional damage, but also evolve out of
the emotional impoverishment of the general society.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1052 (Number of characters: 99):
One of my clients described this as
becoming “way more emotionally intelligent than the ‘normies’.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1053 (Number of characters: 277):
Perhaps the greatest reward of improved emotional intelligence is seen in a greater capacity
for deeper intimacy. Emotional intelligence is a foundational ingredient of relational intelligence
– a type of intelligence that is also frequently diminished in the general populace.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1054 (Number of characters: 111):
As stated earlier, intimacy is greatly enhanced when two people dialogue about all aspects
of their experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1055 (Number of characters: 88):
This is especially true when they transcend taboos against full emotional
communication.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1056 (Number of characters: 175):
Feelings of love, appreciation and gratitude are naturally enhanced when we
reciprocally show our full selves - confident or afraid, loving or alienated, proud or embarrassed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1057 (Number of characters: 109):
What an incredible achievement it is when any two of us create such an authentic and supportive
relationship!

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1058 (Number of characters: 173):
Many of the most intimate relationships that I have seen are between people who
have done a great deal of freeing themselves from the negative legacies of their upbringings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1059 (Number of characters: 127):
“The Unexamined Life Is Not Worth Living”
A further silver lining in recovery is the attainment of a much richer internal life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1060 (Number of characters: 121):
The
introspective process, so fundamental to effective recovery work, eventually deepens and
enriches survivors’ psyches.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1061 (Number of characters: 160):
Ongoing mindful exploration of all aspects of our experience helps
us see firsthand what Socrates meant when he said: “The unexamined life is not worth living”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1062 (Number of characters: 230):
The survivor who follows the introspective “road less travelled” becomes increasingly free
of compulsive and unconscious allegiance to unhelpful familial, religious and societal values that
were instilled at an impressionable age.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1063 (Number of characters: 103):
The recoveree now gets to choose her own values and reject those that are not in her own
best interest.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1064 (Number of characters: 146):
She develops a deeper more grounded self-respect that is not contingent upon going
with the herd and shifting center with every new popular trend.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1065 (Number of characters: 115):
In psychological parlance, she
becomes free and brave enough to individuate and develop more of her full potential.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1066 (Number of characters: 75):
In Joseph Campbell’s words, the survivor learns to “follows his own bliss”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1067 (Number of characters: 76):
He is freer to
pursue activities and interests that naturally appeal to him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1068 (Number of characters: 39):
He evolves into his own sense of
style.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1069 (Number of characters: 100):
He may even feel emboldened to coif and dress himself without adherence to the standards
of fashion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1070 (Number of characters: 47):
He may extend this freedom into his home décor.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1071 (Number of characters: 129):
In this vein, I have seen many
survivors discover their own aesthetic, as well as an increased appreciation of beauty in general.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1072 (Number of characters: 195):
How this contrasts with many of the homes of my “normal” sports-buddies, whose homes are
often sparsely decorated, as if they are too afraid to put something out or up lest it not be cool
enough.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1073 (Number of characters: 171):
As the survivor recovers the right of free choice, she becomes more open to trying new
things – healthy things that mainstream society might consider uncool or even taboo.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1074 (Number of characters: 292):
Here are
some examples of this that I believe are conducive to both recovery and healthy everyday living:
voluntary simplicity, improved diet, meditation, alternative medicine, broad scale compassion,
environmentalism, deeper emotional communication and a broader use of the grieving process.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1075 (Number of characters: 146):
The survivor who pursues long-term development on his journey of recovering generally
achieves greater overall evolution than the average citizen.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1076 (Number of characters: 160):
For many untraumatized people, the
pursuit of ongoing learning often stops after their last formal learning experience – whether that
is high school or college.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1077 (Number of characters: 119):
Introspective development also rewards the recoveree with more perspective and wisdom in
making important life choices.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1078 (Number of characters: 122):
It also improves his everyday instinctual choices, such as whether
to fight, flee, freeze or fawn in times of real danger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1079 (Number of characters: 164):
Finally, another silver lining, often achieved in later stage recovery, is a greater ability to handle
normal pain in the most healthy and least retraumatizing way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1080 (Number of characters: 171):
By normal pain, I mean the
recurring existential pain all human beings experience from time to time via encounters with
loss, illness, money troubles, time pressures, etc.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1081 (Number of characters: 97):
Such painful encounters can produce emotional
reactions like anger, sadness, fear and depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1082 (Number of characters: 109):
The average person has not learned how to
verbally ventilate and metabolize their feelings about such events.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1083 (Number of characters: 118):
This results in them getting
stuck in painful emotional places, especially depression, for inordinate amounts of time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1084 (Number of characters: 243):
The Emotional Imperialism Of “Don’t Worry, Be Happy”
One reason that recovering survivors attain greater emotional intelligence is that they eventually
see through the mainstream media’s indoctrination that people should be happy all the time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1085 (Number of characters: 152):
Much of the general populace, however, becomes increasingly dissociated from their full
emotional experience by anxiously pushing to pump up their mood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1086 (Number of characters: 95):
Many “normal” people strive
to fulfill the pursuit of happiness as if it were a patriotic duty.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1087 (Number of characters: 76):
More and more they employ
socially acceptable addictions to accomplish this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1088 (Number of characters: 117):
Snacking, spending, self-medicating, and
online puttering are widespread addictions that seem to be ever on the rise.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1089 (Number of characters: 199):
A particularly rampant example of unhealthy mood-altering behavior is porn addiction. Addiction to pornography creates a terrible narrowing of consciousness in the many men who are
afflicted with it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1090 (Number of characters: 54):
It commonly destroys their capacity for real intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1091 (Number of characters: 94):
Tragically, the use of
porn is more and more “normalized”, even in many psychological circles.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1092 (Number of characters: 335):
Here 
are 
two 
enlightening 
references 
on 
this 
latter 
subject:
http://www.interchangecounseling.com/blog/why-men-are-so-obsessed-with-sex/ 
and
http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wSF82AwSDiU.
As we become more emotionally intelligent, we free ourselves from the hysteria-inducing
pressure to continuously pump up the joy in our life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1093 (Number of characters: 48):
Please do not read this as an “Ode against Joy”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1094 (Number of characters: 77):
It is a blessing to have our natural fair share
of laughter and feeling good.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1095 (Number of characters: 117):
But I believe it also a blessing to resist the growing emotional
imperialism that demands we become fountains of joy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1096 (Number of characters: 265):
We are assaulted daily with messages
from advertisements, from laugh track-saturated TV shows, and from new age enlightenment
gurus who shame us into believing that we are “less than”, if we are not constantly bubbling over
with ecstatic Disneyland-like enthusiasm.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1097 (Number of characters: 78):
The pressure to be always up was an enormous shame trigger for me for decades.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1098 (Number of characters: 103):
Sadly, I
increasingly see clients and friends struggling with self-contempt for not being happy enough.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1099 (Number of characters: 124):
Once again, I am certainly not knocking joy, but when it is inauthentic, it is disconcertingly
sad and sometimes alienating.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1100 (Number of characters: 114):
In worst case scenarios, a controlling narcissist can emotionally
blackmail us to join him in falsely emoting joy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1101 (Number of characters: 95):
Just as painful is when we codependents force
ourselves to laugh to cover up our fear or shame.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1102 (Number of characters: 196):
This is also not to say that authentic joy cannot be contagious. Contagious joy is the
wonderful experience of being positively triggered into vicariously sharing someone else’s
authentic delight.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1103 (Number of characters: 89):
[For an experience of this, go to www.youtube.com and search for
“Quadruplets Laughing”].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1104 (Number of characters: 250):
In my experience, it seems that authentic joy is much more common in the lives of well
parented children. I also do not think that joy is typically as dominant an emotional theme in
adult life unless it is synthetically induced with drugs or alcohol.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1105 (Number of characters: 169):
On the other hand, experiences
of joy for survivors can gradually become more frequent as a person’s recovery efforts promote
increasing feelings of safety in the world.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1106 (Number of characters: 121):
As our emotional intelligence increases, I see considerable evidence that our expectations of
joy become more reasonable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1107 (Number of characters: 85):
This allows us to let go of permanent happiness as the unrealistic

goal of recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1108 (Number of characters: 118):
Until this happens, we remain at the mercy of the critic’s contemptuous
diatribes that we are not being joyful enough.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1109 (Number of characters: 142):
One of my clients recently became mindful enough
to see how he was shaming himself for not being as jubilant as those in the beer commercials.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1110 (Number of characters: 241):
As a concluding comment to this overview, it is important to emphasize that, like most things in
life, there are degrees of Cptsd. The continuum of Cptsd ranges from mild neurosis to psychosis,
and from highly functioning to non-functioning.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1111 (Number of characters: 119):
Its severity ranges from having extended
periods without flashbacks to being in full flashback horror much of the time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1112 (Number of characters: 123):
This range also
varies from a condition of increased experiences of thriving to a condition of barely surviving
disability.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1113 (Number of characters: 133):
Progress in recovery is seen, then, in flashbacks becoming more manageable and life
satisfaction becoming continuously more frequent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1114 (Number of characters: 101):
A friend of mine once joked with me: “I’ve
got so much recovery, I’m beyond normal – I’m supernormal.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1115 (Number of characters: 58):
I make the normies look like
they’re the ones with Cptsd.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1116 (Number of characters: 136):
As we end the overview, we are ready to move to the next chapter, which explains how varying
childhood trauma histories can cause Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1117 (Number of characters: 154):
Here we will also see how verbal and emotional
abuse alone can cause Cptsd, and how profound emotional abandonment is typically at the core
of most Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1118 (Number of characters: 63):
PART II
THE FINE POINTS OF RECOVERING

WHAT IF I WAS NEVER HIT?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1119 (Number of characters: 117):
Physical and sexual abuse are the most obvious traumas that a child can experience, especially
when they are ongoing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1120 (Number of characters: 83):
However, much that is also traumatic goes unnoticed in Cptsd-
engendering families.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1121 (Number of characters: 127):
This often occurs because parental acts of physical abuse are more blatant
than acts of verbal and emotional abuse and neglect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1122 (Number of characters: 134):
It appears to me that just as many children
acquire Cptsd from emotionally traumatizing families as from physically traumatizing ones.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1123 (Number of characters: 215):
Denial about the traumatic effects of childhood abandonment can seriously hamper your
ability to recover. In childhood, ongoing emotional neglect typically creates overwhelming
feelings of fear, shame and emptiness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1124 (Number of characters: 83):
As an adult survivor, you may continuously flashback into
this abandonment mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1125 (Number of characters: 114):
Recovering depends on realizing that fear, shame and depression are
the lingering effects of a loveless childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1126 (Number of characters: 142):
Without such understanding, your crucial, unmet
needs for comforting human connection can strand you in a great deal of unnecessary suffering.

--------------------------------------------------
