chunk 1127 (Number of characters: 60):
Denial And Minimization
Confronting denial is no small task.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1128 (Number of characters: 158):
Children so need to believe that their parents love and care
for them, that they will deny and minimize away evidence of the most egregious neglect and
abuse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1129 (Number of characters: 58):
De-minimization is a crucial aspect of confronting denial.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1130 (Number of characters: 103):
It is the process by which a
person deconstructs the defense of “making light” of his childhood trauma.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1131 (Number of characters: 119):
The lifelong process
of de-minimizing the impact of childhood trauma is like peeling a very slippery and caustic
onion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1132 (Number of characters: 118):
The outer layer for some is the stark physical evidence of abuse, e.g., sexual abuse or
excessive corporal punishment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1133 (Number of characters: 133):
Subsequent layers involve verbal, spiritual and emotional abuse. Core layers have to do with verbal, spiritual and emotional neglect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1134 (Number of characters: 265):
In a perversely ironic way, my parents’ physical abuse of me was a blessing, for it was so
blatant that my attempts to suppress, rationalize, make light of and laugh it off lost their power in

adolescence, and I was able to see my father for the bully that he was.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1135 (Number of characters: 59):
[Seeing my idealized
mother’s abusiveness came much later].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1136 (Number of characters: 237):
Identifying my father’s behavior as abusive eventually helped me become aware of less
blatant aspects of my parents’ oppression, and I subsequently discovered the verbal and
emotional abuse layer of the onion of my childhood abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1137 (Number of characters: 27):
Verbal And Emotional Abuse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1138 (Number of characters: 207):
The fact that verbal and emotional abuse can be traumatic is lost on many childhood trauma
victims, though it is rarely lost on recovering victims of cult brainwashing who also are prone to
developing Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1139 (Number of characters: 95):
Many survivors of verbal and emotional abuse never learn to validate its soul-damaging
effects.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1140 (Number of characters: 58):
They never accurately assign current time suffering to it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1141 (Number of characters: 159):
Attempts to acknowledge it are
typically blindsided with thoughts that it was nothing compared to kids who were repeatedly
beaten – who “had it so much worse.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1142 (Number of characters: 119):
As a child, I minimized my father’s frequent face-slapping
by comparing it to my friend’s father who used to punch him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1143 (Number of characters: 149):
Much later, however, I finally realized that for me, and many of my clients, verbal and
emotional abuse damaged us much more than our physical abuse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1144 (Number of characters: 158):
Ongoing assault with critical words systematically destroys our self-esteem and replaces it
with a toxic inner critic that incessantly judges us as defective.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1145 (Number of characters: 105):
Even worse, words that are
emotionally poisoned with contempt infuse the child with fear and toxic shame.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1146 (Number of characters: 119):
Fear and shame
condition him to refrain from asking for attention, from expressing himself in ways that draw
attention.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1147 (Number of characters: 85):
Before long, he learns to refrain from seeking any kind of help or connection at all.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1148 (Number of characters: 191):
Theoretical Neurobiology Of The Critic
Unrelenting criticism, especially when it is ground in with parental rage and scorn, is so injurious
that it changes the structure of the child’s brain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1149 (Number of characters: 125):
Repeated messages of disdain are internalized and adopted by the child, who eventually
repeats them over and over to himself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1150 (Number of characters: 104):
Incessant repetitions result in the construction of thick
neural pathways of self-hate and self-disgust.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1151 (Number of characters: 105):
Over time a self-hate response attaches to more and
more of the child’s thoughts, feelings and behaviors.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1152 (Number of characters: 127):
Eventually, any inclination toward authentic or vulnerable self-expression activates internal
neural networks of self-loathing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1153 (Number of characters: 139):
The child is forced to exist in a crippling state of self-attack,
which eventually becomes the equivalent of full-fledged self-abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1154 (Number of characters: 76):
The ability to
support himself or take his own side in any way is decimated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1155 (Number of characters: 155):
With ongoing parental reinforcement, these neural pathways expand into a large complex
network that becomes an Inner Critic that dominates mental activity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1156 (Number of characters: 94):
The inner critic’s negative
perspective creates many programs of self-rejecting perfectionism.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1157 (Number of characters: 74):
At the same time, it obsesses
about danger and catastrophizes incessantly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1158 (Number of characters: 85):
Chapters 9 and 10 expand on shrinking and
deconstructing these life-ruining programs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1159 (Number of characters: 116):
Until this is accomplished, the survivor typically
lives in varying degrees of emotional flashback much of the time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1160 (Number of characters: 86):
The verbal and emotional layer of the abuse onion has many sub-layers of minimization.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1161 (Number of characters: 192):
I
have heard clients jokingly repeat numerous versions of this over and over: “I know I’m hard on

myself, but if I don’t constantly kick my own ass, I’ll be more of a loser than I already am.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1162 (Number of characters: 82):
In
fact, I really need you to come down on me if I try to get away with anything!”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1163 (Number of characters: 159):
A childhood rife
with verbal and emotional abuse forces the child to so thoroughly identify with the critic, that it
is as if the critic is his whole identity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1164 (Number of characters: 61):
Disidentification from the critic is the fight of a lifetime.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1165 (Number of characters: 107):
To liberate your identity from the
toxic critic, you will have to repetitively confront it for a long time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1166 (Number of characters: 134):

success if you are prepared to forgive yourself for repeatedly collapsing back into the old habit of
self-blame.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1167 (Number of characters: 52):
Progress is always a gradual back and forth process.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1168 (Number of characters: 161):
Ironically, a pernicious type of
self-hate can constellate around the self-judgment that one is especially defective because she
cannot simply banish the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1169 (Number of characters: 62):
This is the typical toxic, all-or-none thinking of the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1170 (Number of characters: 112):
Sadly, many survivors give up on fighting the critic before recognizing the myriad subtle
ways it tortures them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1171 (Number of characters: 109):
Yet, there is no more noble recovery battle than that which gradually frees
the psyche from critic dominance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1172 (Number of characters: 107):
Until this happens to a significant degree, there is minimal
development of the healthy, user-friendly ego.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1173 (Number of characters: 85):
Let us look now at how emotional neglect alone can create a psyche-dominating critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1174 (Number of characters: 159):
Emotional Neglect: The Core Wound In Complex PTSD
Minimization about the damage caused by extensive emotional neglect is at the core of the Cptsd
denial onion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1175 (Number of characters: 133):
Our journey of recovering takes a quantum leap when we really feel and
understand how devastating it was to be emotionally abandoned.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1176 (Number of characters: 124):
An absence of parental loving
interest and engagement, especially in the first few years, creates an overwhelming emptiness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1177 (Number of characters: 114):
Life feels harrowingly frightening to the infant or toddler who is left for long periods without
comfort and care.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1178 (Number of characters: 146):
Children are helpless and powerless for a long time, and when they sense that
no one has their back, they feel scared, miserable and disheartened.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1179 (Number of characters: 139):
Much of the constant anxiety
that adult survivors live in is this still aching fear that comes from having been so frighteningly
abandoned.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1180 (Number of characters: 89):
Many survivors never discover and work through the wounds that correlate with this level.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1181 (Number of characters: 301):
This happens because they over-assign their suffering to overt abuse and never get to the core
issue of their emotional abandonment. As stated above, this is especially likely to occur with
survivors who dismissively compare their trauma to those who were abused more noticeably and
more dramatically.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1182 (Number of characters: 106):
I find this painfully ironic because some people suffer significant active
abuse without developing Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1183 (Number of characters: 98):
Typically, they are “spared” because there is one caretaker who
does not emotionally neglect them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1184 (Number of characters: 129):
Traumatic emotional neglect occurs when a child does not have a single caretaker to whom
she can turn in times of need or danger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1185 (Number of characters: 67):
Cptsd then sets in to the degree that there is no
alternative adult

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1186 (Number of characters: 86):
[relative, older sibling, neighbor, or teacher] to turn to for comfort and
protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1187 (Number of characters: 98):
This is especially true when the abandonment occurs 24/7, 365 days a year for the
first few years.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1188 (Number of characters: 215):
Growing up emotionally neglected is like nearly dying of thirst outside the fenced off
fountain of a parent’s warmth and interest. Emotional neglect makes children feel worthless,
unlovable and excruciatingly empty.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1189 (Number of characters: 76):
It leaves them with a hunger that gnaws deeply at the center
of their being.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1190 (Number of characters: 41):
They starve for human warmth and comfort.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1191 (Number of characters: 370):
The Failure To Thrive Syndrome
When a child is continuously deprived of a nurturing caretaker, love-starvation steadily increases
and sometimes devolves into the Failure to Thrive Syndrome. Failure to thrive is a term coined in the mid twentieth century to describe the epidemic of
baby deaths that occurred when new germ-phobic practices were introduced into hospitals.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1192 (Number of characters: 100):
The
new standard was that nurses were prohibited from holding babies for fear of contaminating
them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1193 (Number of characters: 44):
Infant mortality immediately began to climb.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1194 (Number of characters: 104):
Modern medical practice has abandoned this heartless approach because of the Failure to
thrive research.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1195 (Number of characters: 162):
This research has since been corroborated by data from Eastern European
orphanages where there are insufficient staff to meet the contact-comfort needs of babies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1196 (Number of characters: 142):
Modern medicine now accepts as scientific fact the principle that babies need a great deal of
physical touch and nurturing in order to thrive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1197 (Number of characters: 149):
In my experience, failure to thrive is not an all-or-none phenomenon, but rather a
continuum that stretches from the abandonment depression to death.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1198 (Number of characters: 45):
Many Cptsd survivors never
thrived as babies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1199 (Number of characters: 108):
I believe that many suffered painful bouts of lingering near the end of the
continuum that feels death-like.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1200 (Number of characters: 113):
Several of my clients commonly have quipped that they “feel
like death warmed over” when they are in a flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1201 (Number of characters: 81):
Moreover, I suspect that some traumatized children do die from their abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1202 (Number of characters: 80):
Perhaps, their immune systems weaken and make them more susceptible to diseases.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1203 (Number of characters: 114):
Perhaps, as
David Kalshed hints, they unconsciously gravitate toward lethal “accidents” to terminate their
misery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1204 (Number of characters: 107):
One of my clients reported this painful memory when we were processing a flashback that
she was trapped in.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1205 (Number of characters: 76):
She was ten, in a daze, and walked out between two parked cars into traffic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1206 (Number of characters: 77):
She was hit by a truck and it took months of hospitalization to save her leg.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1207 (Number of characters: 156):
Her most tearful re-
experiencing of this event was remembering how she woke up in the hospital and felt
tremendous disappointment that she was still alive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1208 (Number of characters: 451):
Emotional Hunger And Addiction
The emotional hunger that comes from parental abandonment often morphs over time into an
insatiable appetite for substances and/or addictive processes. Minimization of early abandonment
often transforms later in life into the minimizing that some survivors use to rationalize their
substance and process addictions. Fortunately, many survivors eventually come to see their
substance or process addictions as problematic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1209 (Number of characters: 138):
But many also minimize the deleterious effects
of their addiction and jokingly dismiss their need to end or reduce their reliance on them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1210 (Number of characters: 196):
When the survivor has no understanding of the effects of trauma or no memory of being
traumatized, addictions are often understandable, misplaced attempts to regulate painful
emotional flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1211 (Number of characters: 94):
However many survivors are now in a position to see how self-destructive
their addictions are.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1212 (Number of characters: 65):
They are now old enough to learn healthier ways of self-soothing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1213 (Number of characters: 108):
Accordingly, substance and process addictions can be seen as misguided attempts to distract
from inner pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1214 (Number of characters: 162):
The desire to reduce such habits can therefore be used as motivation to learn the
more sophisticated forms of self-soothing that Cptsd recovery work has to offer.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1215 (Number of characters: 106):
As we will see in chapter 11, grieving work offers us irreplaceable tools for working

through inner pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1216 (Number of characters: 79):
This then helps obviate the need to harmfully distract ourselves from our
pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1217 (Number of characters: 147):
The Evolutionary Basis Of Attachment Needs
The human brain evolved during the Hunter-Gatherer era that represents 99.8% of our time on
this planet.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1218 (Number of characters: 271):
For a child, safety from predators during these times depended on being in very close
proximity to an adult. Even the briefest loss of contact with a parental figure could trigger
panicky feelings as beasts of prey only needed seconds to snatch away an unprotected child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1219 (Number of characters: 258):
Fear hard-wired in the child as a healthy response to separation from a protective adult. Fear
also linked automatically with the fight response so that the infant and toddler would
automatically cry angrily for attention, help, and cessation of abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1220 (Number of characters: 183):
Cptsd-inducing families however loathe angry crying, and many can find professionals to
back them up for routinely leaving babies and very young children to “cry it out” on their own.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1221 (Number of characters: 106):
In most dysfunctional families, parents disdain children for needing any kind of help or
attention at all.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1222 (Number of characters: 196):
Moreover, even the most well-intentioned parent can seriously neglect their
children by subscribing to the egregious 20th century “wisdom” that “Kids need quality time -
quantity does not matter.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1223 (Number of characters: 154):
When children experience long periods of being powerless to obtain needed connection
with a parent, they become increasingly anxious, upset and depressed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1224 (Number of characters: 74):
In Cptsd-engendering
families, the absence of care and concern is extreme.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1225 (Number of characters: 76):
A caretaker is rarely or never available for
support, comfort or protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1226 (Number of characters: 77):
If this is what you suffered, you then grew up feeling that no one likes you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1227 (Number of characters: 126):
No one ever
listened to you or seemed to want you around. No one had empathy for you, showed you
warmth, or invited closeness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1228 (Number of characters: 69):
No one cared about what you thought, felt, did, wanted or dreamed
of.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1229 (Number of characters: 165):
You learned early that, no matter how hurt, alienated, or terrified you were, turning to a
parent would do nothing more than exacerbate your experience of rejection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1230 (Number of characters: 247):
When caretakers turn their backs on a child’s need for help and support, her inner world
becomes an increasingly nightmarish amalgam of fear, shame and depression. The child who is
abandoned in this way experiences the world as a terrifying place.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1231 (Number of characters: 162):
Over time the child’s dominant experience of herself is so replete with emotional pain and
so unmanageable that that she has to dissociate, self-medicate, act out

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1232 (Number of characters: 88):
[aggression against others]
or act in [aggression against the self] to distract from it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1233 (Number of characters: 180):
The situation of the abandoned child further deteriorates as an extended absence of warmth
and protection gives rise to the cancerous growth of the inner critic as described above.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1234 (Number of characters: 312):
The child
projects his hope for being accepted onto self-perfection. By the time the child is becoming self-
reflective, cognitions start to arise that sound like this: “I’m so despicable, worthless, unlovable,
and ugly; maybe my parents would love me if I could make myself like those perfect kids I see
on TV.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1235 (Number of characters: 90):
In this way, the child becomes hyperaware of imperfections and strives to become flawless.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1236 (Number of characters: 113):
Eventually she roots out the ultimate flaw – the mortal sin of wanting or asking for her parents’
time or energy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1237 (Number of characters: 222):
Intrinsic to this process is noticing – more and more hyper-vigilantly - how her
parents turn their back or become angry or disgusted whenever she needs anything, whether it be
attention, listening, interest, or affection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1238 (Number of characters: 107):
Emotional neglect, alone, causes children to abandon themselves, and to give up on the
formation of a self.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1239 (Number of characters: 141):
They do so to preserve an illusion of connection with the parent and to
protect themselves from the danger of losing that tenuous connection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1240 (Number of characters: 158):
This typically requires a
great deal of self-abdication, e.g., the forfeiture of self-esteem, self-confidence, self-care, self-
interest, and self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1241 (Number of characters: 196):
Moreover, endangerment programs proliferate in the critic as the child learns that he cannot
ask his parent to protect him from dangers and injustices in the outside world, never mind in the
home.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1242 (Number of characters: 76):
His only recourse is to become hypervigilant about things that can go wrong.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1243 (Number of characters: 111):
His critic
compiles lists of possible calamities, especially those that are graphically portrayed in the media.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1244 (Number of characters: 75):
The media gives the critic of the abandoned child much fodder to play with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1245 (Number of characters: 92):
She may be
exposed daily to hours of programs that glorify sarcasm, backbiting and bullying.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1246 (Number of characters: 152):
Moreover
news programs, with a ninety percent content of bad news, fill her head with impressions that the
world is predominantly hostile and dangerous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1247 (Number of characters: 113):
Even worse, emotionally neglectful parents
commonly abandon their children to their favorite babysitter – the TV.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1248 (Number of characters: 300):
Through such neglect the child’s consciousness eventually becomes overwhelmed with the
processes of drasticizing and catastrophizing. Drasticizing and catastrophizing are critic
processes that lead the child to constantly rehearse fearful scenarios in a vain attempt to prepare
himself for the worst.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1249 (Number of characters: 166):
This is the process by which Cptsd with its overdeveloped stress and toxic
shame programs sets in and becomes triggerable by a plethora of normally innocuous stimuli.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1250 (Number of characters: 124):
Most notable of these stimuli are other people, especially unknown people or people even
vaguely reminiscent of the parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1251 (Number of characters: 198):
Over time, the critic comes to assume that all other people
are dangerous and automatically triggers the fight, flight, freeze or fawn response whenever a
stranger or unproven other comes into view.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1252 (Number of characters: 115):
This people-are-dangerous process typically devolves into the social anxiety that is
frequently a symptom of Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1253 (Number of characters: 70):
In worst case scenarios it manifests as social phobia and
agoraphobia.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1254 (Number of characters: 61):
In my opinion, agoraphobia is rarely the fear of open spaces.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1255 (Number of characters: 113):
It is instead a
disguised form of social phobia. It is the fear of going out lest you run into someone or anyone.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1256 (Number of characters: 219):
Abandonment Stultifies Emotional And Relational Intelligence
As stated above, emotionally abandoned children often devolve into experiencing all people as
dangerous, no matter how benign or generous they may in fact be.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1257 (Number of characters: 78):
Even love, coming their way,
reverberates threateningly on a subliminal level.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1258 (Number of characters: 196):

momentarily “trick” someone into liking them, the forbidden prize will vanish once their social
perfectionism inevitably fails and exposes their unworthiness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1259 (Number of characters: 97):
Moreover, when this occurs, they
will be triggered even more deeply into the abandonment mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1260 (Number of characters: 123):
Emotional intelligence and its cohort, relational intelligence, are forced into developmental
arrest by abandoning parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1261 (Number of characters: 95):
Children never learn that a relationship with a healthy person can
be comforting and enriching.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1262 (Number of characters: 103):
The ability to open to and benefit from love and caring from others
often lays dormant and undeveloped.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1263 (Number of characters: 138):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1264 (Number of characters: 104):
Emotional intelligence about the healthy and
functional aspects of anger, sadness, and fear lies fallow.

chunk 1265 (Number of characters: 202):

As with physical abuse, effective work on the wounds of verbal and emotional abuse can

My mother
never hit me!”

chunk 1279 (Number of characters: 151):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1280 (Number of characters: 259):

learned to assign the pain of numerous current time emotional flashbacks to the abject loneliness

chunk 1281 (Number of characters: 171):

chunk 1282 (Number of characters: 196):
Practicing Vulnerability
Emotional abandonment is healed by the type of real intimacy that we have been discussing. And
once again real intimacy depends on us showing up in times of vulnerability.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1283 (Number of characters: 192):
Deep-level
recovering occurs when we successfully connect with a safe enough other during the
flashbacked-times of feeling trapped in the fear, shame and depression of the abandonment
mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1284 (Number of characters: 78):
In this vein, I had to painstakingly practice showing up in my pain for years.

--------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1288 (Number of characters: 184):

not just the shiny ones.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1289 (Number of characters: 135):

chunk 1290 (Number of characters: 32):
How could I help but conceal it?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1291 (Number of characters: 598):

especially during my deepest flashbacks. Gratefully, sufficient positive experiences with my therapist eventually emboldened me to
bring my authentic vulnerability to other select and gradually proven relationships, where I found
the acceptance, safety and support that, previously, I would not have known to wish for.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1300 (Number of characters: 233):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1301 (Number of characters: 156):

chunk 1303 (Number of characters: 526):

again because I can still emotionally flashback to that bereft state of feeling stranded from the
comfort of others, even occasionally from my wife and son. And then my tears were sweet again
because my flashbacks are so much easier to handle these days, especially as I increasingly
master the use of the tools I describe in chapter 8.

chunk 1304 (Number of characters: 502):
The Power Of Narrative
There is also growing evidence that recovery from Complex PTSD is reflected in the narrative a
person tells about her life. The degree of recovery matches the degree to which a survivor’s story
is complete, coherent, and emotionally congruent and told from a self-sympathetic perspective. In my experience, deep level recovery is often reflected in a narrative that highlights the
role of emotional neglect in describing what one has suffered and what one continues to deal
with.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1305 (Number of characters: 108):

even more.

chunk 1321 (Number of characters: 406):
‘Thanks Mom
for never knowing what grade I was in’; or ‘Thanks Mom for all the memories of you walking

Understanding how profoundly derelict your parents were in their duty to nurture and protect you
is a master key to your recovery.

chunk 1322 (Number of characters: 139):

chunk 1327 (Number of characters: 115):

chunk 1328 (Number of characters: 333):

kick-starting the process of resolving any given flashback.

chunk 1329 (Number of characters: 130):
WHAT IS MY TRAUMA TYPE? This chapter describes a trauma typology for recognizing and recovering from the different types
of Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1330 (Number of characters: 66):
We human beings respond with some variability to childhood trauma.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1331 (Number of characters: 151):
This model
elaborates four basic survival strategies and defensive styles that develop out of our instinctive
Fight, Flight, Freeze and Fawn responses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1332 (Number of characters: 141):
Variances in your childhood abuse/neglect pattern, birth order and genetics result in you
gravitating toward a specific 4F survival strategy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1333 (Number of characters: 79):
You do this as a child to prevent, escape or
ameliorate further traumatization.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1338 (Number of characters: 169):
Healthy Employment Of The 4 F’s
People who experience “good enough parenting” in childhood arrive in adulthood with a healthy
and flexible response repertoire to danger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1339 (Number of characters: 84):
In the face of real danger, they have appropriate
access to all of their 4F choices.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1340 (Number of characters: 129):

aggressive self-protectiveness if necessary.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1341 (Number of characters: 155):
Untraumatized people also easily and appropriately access their flight instinct and
disengage and retreat when confrontation would exacerbate their danger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1342 (Number of characters: 146):
Untraumatized people also freeze appropriately and give up and quit struggling when
further activity or resistance is futile or counterproductive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1343 (Number of characters: 236):
Additionally, the freeze response is
sometimes our first response to danger, as when we become still, quiet and camouflaged to buy
time, to assess the danger and decide whether fight, flight, continued freeze or fawn is our best
option.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1344 (Number of characters: 208):
And finally, untraumatized people also fawn in a non-groveling manner and are able to

rights and points of view.

chunk 1346 (Number of characters: 160):
POSITIVE CHARACTERISTICS OF THE FOUR F’S
Those who are repetitively traumatized in childhood often learn to survive by over-using one or
two of the 4F Reponses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1347 (Number of characters: 158):

the others, but also severely impairs our ability to relax into an undefended state.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1348 (Number of characters: 73):
Additionally, it
strands us in a narrow, impoverished experience of life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1349 (Number of characters: 140):

critic and the painful feelings that underlie it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1350 (Number of characters: 121):
Preoccupation with 4F behaviors dulls our
awareness of our unresolved past trauma and the pain of our current alienation.

[compulsion].

Left-Brain Dissociation
When the obsessive/compulsive flight type is not doing, she is worrying and planning about
doing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1459 (Number of characters: 81):

chunk 1460 (Number of characters: 128):
Obsessiveness is left-brain dissociation, as opposed to the classic right-brain dissociation of the
freeze type described below.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1461 (Number of characters: 106):
Left-brain dissociation is using constant thinking to distract yourself from underlying

abandonment pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1462 (Number of characters: 96):

thinking process.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1463 (Number of characters: 147):

pain, obsessing is worrying to stay one level above underlying pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1503 (Number of characters: 44):
THE FREEZE TYPE AND THE DISSOCIATIVE DEFENSE

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1504 (Number of characters: 136):
The freeze response, also known as the camouflage response, often triggers a survivor into
hiding, isolating and avoiding human contact.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1505 (Number of characters: 125):
The freeze type can be so frozen in the retreat
mode that it seems as if their starter button is stuck in the “off” position.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1506 (Number of characters: 332):
Of all the 4F’s, freeze types seem to have the deepest unconscious belief that people and
danger are synonymous. While all 4F types commonly suffer from social anxiety as well, freeze
types typically take a great deal more refuge in solitude. Some freeze types completely give up
on relating to others and become extremely isolated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1507 (Number of characters: 74):
Outside of fantasy, many also give up
entirely on the possibility of love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1508 (Number of characters: 24):
Right-Brain Dissociation

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1509 (Number of characters: 134):
It is often the scapegoat or the most profoundly abandoned child, “the lost child”, who is forced
to habituate to the freeze response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1510 (Number of characters: 623):
Not allowed to successfully employ fight, flight or fawn
responses, the freeze type’s defenses develop around classical or right-brain dissociation. Dissociation allows the freeze type to disconnect from experiencing his abandonment pain, and
protects him from risky social interactions - any of which might trigger feelings of being
retraumatized. If you are a freeze type, you may seek refuge and comfort by dissociating in prolonged
bouts of sleep, daydreaming, wishing and right-brain-dominant activities like TV, online
browsing and video games. Freeze types sometimes have or appear to have Attention Deficit Disorder

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1511 (Number of characters: 6):
[ADD].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1512 (Number of characters: 107):
They
often master the art of changing the internal channel whenever inner experience becomes
uncomfortable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1513 (Number of characters: 118):

like detachment from ordinary reality.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1514 (Number of characters: 155):
And in worst case scenarios, they can decompensate into a
schizophrenic experience like the main character in the book, I Never Promised You a Rose
Garden.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1515 (Number of characters: 100):
Recovering From A Polarized Freeze Response
Recovery for freeze types involves three key challenges.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1516 (Number of characters: 60):
First, their positive relational experiences are few if any.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1517 (Number of characters: 114):
They are therefore extremely
reluctant to enter into the type of intimate relationship that can be transformative.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1518 (Number of characters: 53):
They are even
less likely to seek the aid of therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1519 (Number of characters: 96):
Moreover, those who manage to overcome this reluctance
often spook easily and quickly terminate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1520 (Number of characters: 61):
Second, freeze types have two commonalities with fight types.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1521 (Number of characters: 91):
They are less motivated to
try to understand the effects of their childhood traumatization.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1522 (Number of characters: 94):
Many are unaware that they have
a troublesome inner critic or that they are in emotional pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1523 (Number of characters: 116):
Furthermore, they tend to project the
perfectionistic demands of the critic onto others rather than onto themselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1524 (Number of characters: 114):
This survival
mechanism helped them as children to use the imperfections of others as justification for
isolation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1525 (Number of characters: 58):
In the past, isolation was smart, safety-seeking behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1526 (Number of characters: 141):
Third, even more than workaholic flight types, freeze types are in denial about the life
narrowing consequences of their singular adaptation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1527 (Number of characters: 111):
Some freeze types that I have worked with
seem to have significant periods of contentment with their isolation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1528 (Number of characters: 173):
I think they may be able to
self-medicate by releasing the internal opioids that the animal brain is programmed to release
when danger is so great that death seems imminent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1529 (Number of characters: 152):
Internal opioid release is more accessible to freeze types because the freeze response has its
own continuum that culminates with the collapse response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1530 (Number of characters: 65):
The collapse response is an extreme
abandonment of consciousness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1531 (Number of characters: 77):
It appears to be an out-of-body experience that is the ultimate
dissociation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1532 (Number of characters: 214):
It can sometimes be seen in prey animals that are about to be killed. I have seen
nature films of small animals in the jaws of a predator that show it letting go so thoroughly that
its death appears to be painless.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1533 (Number of characters: 152):
However, the opioid production that some freeze types have access to, only takes the
survivor so far before its analgesic properties no longer function.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1534 (Number of characters: 59):
Numbed out contentment then
morphs into serious depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1535 (Number of characters: 105):
This in turn can lead to addictive self-medicating with
substances like alcohol, marijuana and narcotics.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1536 (Number of characters: 113):
Alternatively, the freeze type can gravitate
toward ever escalating regimens of anti-depressants and anxiolytics.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1537 (Number of characters: 156):
I also suspect that some
schizophrenics are extremely traumatized freeze types who dissociate so thoroughly that they
cannot find their way back to reality.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1538 (Number of characters: 138):
Several of my freeze type respondents highly recommend a self-help book by Suzette Boon,
entitled Coping with Trauma-related Dissociation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1539 (Number of characters: 89):
This book is filled with very helpful work
sheets that are powerful tools for recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1540 (Number of characters: 182):
More than any other type, the freeze type usually requires a therapeutic relationship,
because their isolation prevents them from discovering relational healing through a friendship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1541 (Number of characters: 193):
That said, I know of some instances where good enough relational healing has come through pets
and the safer distant type of human healing that can be found in books and online internet
groups.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1542 (Number of characters: 96):
Phyllis, a self-proclaimed couch potato, began therapy with me with a great deal of ambivalence.

chunk 1543 (Number of characters: 113):

starting to scare him.”

chunk 1548 (Number of characters: 90):

rarely around and gone in the computer when he was home.

chunk 1550 (Number of characters: 71):
This is not un

chunk 1580 (Number of characters: 66):
The progression of recovery for a freeze type is often as follows.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1581 (Number of characters: 125):
Gradual trust building

suffering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1582 (Number of characters: 130):

the work of grieving the losses of childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1583 (Number of characters: 103):
The anger work of grieving is especially therapeutic
for freeze types as is an aerobic exercise regime.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1584 (Number of characters: 60):
Both help resuscitate the survivor’s dormant
will and drive.

chunk 1585 (Number of characters: 122):
THE FAWN TYPE AND THE CODEPENDENT DEFENSE

Fawn types seek safety by merging with the wishes, needs and demands of others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1586 (Number of characters: 149):
They act as if
they believe that the price of admission to any relationship is the forfeiture of all their needs,
rights, preferences and boundaries.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1587 (Number of characters: 60):
The disenfranchisement of the fawn type begins in childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1588 (Number of characters: 143):
She learns early that a
modicum of safety and attachment can be gained by becoming the helpful and compliant servant
of her exploitive parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1589 (Number of characters: 81):
A fawn type/codependent is usually the child of at least one narcissistic parent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1590 (Number of characters: 54):
The
narcissist reverses the parent-child relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1591 (Number of characters: 234):
The child is parentified and takes care of the
needs of the parent, who acts like a needy and sometimes tantruming child. When this occurs, the child may be turned into the parent’s confidant, substitute spouse,
coach, or housekeeper.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1592 (Number of characters: 67):
Or, she may be pressed into service to mother the younger siblings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1593 (Number of characters: 55):
In
worst case scenarios, she may be exploited sexually.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1594 (Number of characters: 57):
Some codependent children adapt by becoming entertaining.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1595 (Number of characters: 115):
Accordingly, the child learns
to be the court jester and is unofficially put in charge of keeping his parent happy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1596 (Number of characters: 117):
Pressing a child into codependent service usually involves scaring and shaming him out of
developing a sense of self.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1597 (Number of characters: 225):
Of all the 4F types, fawn types are the most developmentally arrested
in their healthy sense of self. Recovering From A Polarized Fawn Response
Fawn types typically respond to psychoeducation about the 4F’s with great relief.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1598 (Number of characters: 121):
This
eventually helps them to recognize the repetition compulsion that draws them to narcissistic
types who exploit them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1599 (Number of characters: 91):
The codependent needs to understand how she gives herself away by over-listening to
others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1600 (Number of characters: 144):
Recovery involves shrinking her characteristic listening defense, as well as practicing and
broadening her verbal and emotional self-expression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1601 (Number of characters: 190):
I have seen numerous inveterate codependents become motivated to work on their
assertiveness when they realize that even the thought of saying “no” triggers them into an
emotional flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1602 (Number of characters: 142):
After a great deal of work, one client was shocked by how intensely he
dissociated when he contemplated confronting his boss’s awful behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1603 (Number of characters: 118):
This shock then
morphed into an epiphany of outrage about how dangerous it had been to protest anything in his
family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1604 (Number of characters: 118):
This in turn aided him greatly in overcoming his resistance to role-playing assertiveness
in our future work together.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1605 (Number of characters: 143):
With considerable practice, this client learned to overcome the critic voices that
immediately short-circuited him from ever asserting himself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1606 (Number of characters: 100):
In the process, he remembered how
he was repeatedly forced to stifle his individuality in childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1607 (Number of characters: 105):
Grieving these losses then
helped him to work at reclaiming his developmentally arrested self-expression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1608 (Number of characters: 88):
Recovering from
the fawn position will be explored more extensively in the next chapter.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1609 (Number of characters: 52):
TRAUMA HYBRIDS
There are, of course, few pure types.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1610 (Number of characters: 68):
Moreover each type is on a continuum that runs from mild
to extreme.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1611 (Number of characters: 51):
Most trauma survivors are also hybrids of the 4F’s.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1612 (Number of characters: 93):
Most of us have a backup
response that we go to when our primary one is not effective enough.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1613 (Number of characters: 87):
When neither of these

work, we generally then have a third or fourth “go to” position.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1614 (Number of characters: 34):
Here are some common hybrid
types.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1615 (Number of characters: 96):
The Fight-Fawn Hybrid
The Fight-Fawn type corresponds with the charming bully described earlier.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1616 (Number of characters: 93):
This type combines
two opposite polarities of relational style – narcissism and codependence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1617 (Number of characters: 83):
Narcissistic
entitlement, however, is typically at the core of the fight-fawn type.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1618 (Number of characters: 70):
This type, in the extreme,
can also be Borderline Personality Disorder

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1619 (Number of characters: 6):
[BPD].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1620 (Number of characters: 45):
She can frequently and dramatically vacillate

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1621 (Number of characters: 41):
[split] between a fight and fawn defense.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1622 (Number of characters: 165):
When a fight-fawn type is upset with someone, she can
fluctuate over and over between attacking diatribes and fervent declarations of caring in a single
interaction.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1623 (Number of characters: 111):
The fight-fawn is more deeply understood by contrasting him with the fawn-fight, described
in the next chapter.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1624 (Number of characters: 139):
This fawn-fight type is also subject to vacillating during an emotional
flashback, but typically does so with less vitriol and entitlement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1625 (Number of characters: 111):
The fight-fawn also differs from the fawn-fight in that his “care-taking” often feels coercive
or manipulative.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1626 (Number of characters: 88):
It is frequently aimed at achieving personal agendas which range from blatant to
covert.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1627 (Number of characters: 107):
Moreover, the fight-fawn rarely takes any real responsibility for contributing to an
interpersonal problem.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1628 (Number of characters: 93):
He typically ends up in the classic fight position of projecting
imperfection onto the other.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1629 (Number of characters: 144):
This essentially narcissistic type is also different than the fawn-fight
in that entitlement is typically much more ascendant in the fight-fawn.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1630 (Number of characters: 68):
His fawn behavior is
typically devoid of real empathy or compassion.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1631 (Number of characters: 96):
I have worked with several clients who were unfairly labeled borderline by themselves or others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1632 (Number of characters: 72):
I could however tell by the quality of their hearts, that they were not.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1633 (Number of characters: 127):
This was evidenced by their
essential kindness and goodwill to others, which they always return to when the flashback
resolves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1634 (Number of characters: 141):
They also exhibit this in their ability to feel and show true remorse when they hurt
another, as we are all destined to do from time to time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1635 (Number of characters: 118):
Unlike the true borderline who has a
narcissistic core, they can sincerely apologize and make amends when appropriate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1636 (Number of characters: 128):
Another variant of the fight/fawn is seen in the person who acts like a fight type in one
relationship while fawning in another.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1637 (Number of characters: 159):
An example of this is the archetypal henpecked husband
who is a tyrant at work, and who also stays at work to all hours because he so prefers the fight
stance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1638 (Number of characters: 80):
This type also occurs in reverse: monster at home and lovely lady at the office.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1639 (Number of characters: 97):
The Flight-Freeze Hybrid
The Flight-Freeze type is the least relational and most schizoid hybrid.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1640 (Number of characters: 53):
He prefers the safety of
do-it-yourself isolationism.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1641 (Number of characters: 68):
Sometimes this type may also be misdiagnosed as Asperger’s
Syndrome.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1642 (Number of characters: 125):
The flight-freeze type avoids potential relationship-retraumati-zation with an obsessive-
compulsive/dissociative “two-step.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1643 (Number of characters: 171):
Step one is working to complete exhaustion. Step two is
collapsing into extreme “veging out”, and waiting until his energy reaccumulates enough to

relaunch into step one.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1644 (Number of characters: 87):
The price for this type of no-longer-necessary safety is a severely
narrowed existence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1645 (Number of characters: 118):
The flight-freeze cul-de-sac is more common among men, especially those traumatized for
being vulnerable in childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1646 (Number of characters: 83):
This then drives them to seek safety in isolation or “intimacy-lite”
relationships.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1647 (Number of characters: 117):
Some non-alpha type male survivors combine their flight and freeze defenses to become
stereotypical technology nerds.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1648 (Number of characters: 50):
Telecommuting is, of course, their preferred mode.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1649 (Number of characters: 233):
Flight-freeze
types are the computer addicts who focus on work for long periods of time and then drift off
dissociatively into computer games, substance abuse or sleep-bingeing. Flight-freeze types are prone to becoming porn addicts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1650 (Number of characters: 110):
When in flight mode, they
obsessively surf the net for phantom partners and engage in compulsive masturbation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1651 (Number of characters: 106):
When in
freeze mode, they drift off into a right-brain sexual fantasy world if pornography is unavailable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1652 (Number of characters: 186):
Moreover, if they are in intimacy-lite relationship, they typically engage more with their
idealized fantasy partners than with their actual partner during real time sexual interactions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1653 (Number of characters: 81):
The Fight-Freeze Hybrid
These types rarely seek recovery on their own initiative.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1654 (Number of characters: 95):
A colleague of mine told me about a
fight-freeze type who was dragged into therapy by his wife.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1655 (Number of characters: 72):
She complained that she was lucky
to get ten words out of him in a week.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1656 (Number of characters: 90):
She was at the end of her rope and if therapy did not fix
him, she was filing for divorce.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1657 (Number of characters: 155):
The husband was a computer engineer who telecommuted and only left his home office for
bathroom breaks and meals which were eaten separately from his wife.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1658 (Number of characters: 103):
He bullied his wife into
providing these meals according to a written schedule that he e-mailed to her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1659 (Number of characters: 79):
My colleague’s initial “Hello” to the husband was met with a scowl and a grunt.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1660 (Number of characters: 149):
Intuitively,
she kept the focus off him as much as possible, but each delicate attempt to make connection
with him was rebuffed with sarcastic scorn.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1661 (Number of characters: 99):
“You expect me to fall for that phony smile?”;
“You’re not gonna shrink me with your psychobabble!”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1662 (Number of characters: 175):
My colleague, who is the most compassionate, non-intrusive person I know, was not able to
crack the prickly fight shell that guarded this poor man’s extreme social withdrawal.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1663 (Number of characters: 165):
No miracle
was performed, and my colleague said she was amazed in retrospect that he even lasted twenty
minutes before he left in a wake of hostility and resentment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1664 (Number of characters: 138):
I have met with fight-freeze types a few times in similar circumstances, i.e., they were
dragged into therapy under the threat of divorce.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1665 (Number of characters: 86):
Each was like the character in the famous poem:
“The Autocrat at the Breakfast Table.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1666 (Number of characters: 48):
The fight-freeze is a yin or passive narcissist.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1667 (Number of characters: 97):
He demands that things go his way, but he is
not much interested in having any human interaction.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1668 (Number of characters: 105):
No one gets to talk at the table, not even
him – unless of course someone needs to be put in their place.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1669 (Number of characters: 126):
The fight-freeze type is a John Wayne couch potato, dominating family life with foul
moods and monosyllabic grunts and curses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1670 (Number of characters: 92):
He is typically as untreatable as the extreme fight
types mentioned earlier.
SELF-ASSESSMENT

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1671 (Number of characters: 210):
I recommend that you self-assess your own hierarchical use of the 4F responses. Try to
determine your dominant type and hybrid, and think about what percentage of your time is spent
in each of the 4F responses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1672 (Number of characters: 131):
You can also assess where you lie on the relevant continuums that stretch between the two
extremes in each line of the chart below.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1673 (Number of characters: 205):
Continuums of Positive and Negative 4F Responses
Fight: Assertiveness 
 Bullying
Flight: Efficiency 
 Driven-ness
Freeze: Peacefulness 
 Catatonia
Fawn: Helpfulness 
 Servitude
Recovery And Self-Assessment

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1674 (Number of characters: 100):
As stated earlier, a key goal of recovery is to have easy and appropriate access to all of the 4F’s.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1675 (Number of characters: 67):
There are also two more continuums that can be used to assess this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1676 (Number of characters: 90):
The degree to which we are
balanced along each of them reflects the degree of our healing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1677 (Number of characters: 164):
The Fight 
 Fawn Continuum of Healthy Relating to Others
Healthy relating occurs when two people move easily and reciprocally between assertiveness and
receptivity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1678 (Number of characters: 176):
Common and important examples of this are an easy back and forth [1] between
talking and listening, [2] between helping and being helped, and [3] between leading and
following.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1679 (Number of characters: 83):
Normal healthy narcissism and codependence happen at the midpoint of the continuum.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1680 (Number of characters: 120):
To
the degree that I polarize to the narcissistic/fight end of the continuum, I monologue and
dominate the conversation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1681 (Number of characters: 158):
To the degree that I polarize to the codependent/fawn end, I get stuck
in a listening defense, hiding from the vulnerability of showing what I think and feel.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1682 (Number of characters: 126):
Conversations, of course, will not always be exactly in the middle or it would be a Ping-
Pong-like exchange of monosyllables.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1683 (Number of characters: 39):
The real balance occurs more over time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1684 (Number of characters: 84):
For instance, in
an hour’s conversation, we each generally talk about half the time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1685 (Number of characters: 345):
The Flight 
 Freeze Continuum of Healthy Relating to Self
A healthy relationship with yourself is seen in your ability to move in a balanced way[1] between
doing and being, [2] between persistence and letting go, [3] between sympathetic and
parasympathetic nervous system activation, and [4] between intense focus and relaxed,
daydreamy reverie.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1686 (Number of characters: 255):
RECOVERING FROM TRAUMA-BASED CODEPENDENCY
If you assessed yourself in the last chapter as a fawn subtype or as being on the right side of the
fight 
 fawn spectrum, you may find this chapter relevant even if the fawn response is not
your primary position.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1687 (Number of characters: 95):
Moreover the first section below contains important information about the
origins of all types.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1688 (Number of characters: 242):
I have dedicated a whole chapter to codependency because it is the 4F trauma response that
I know the most about. This knowledge comes from my own personal recovery journey, and
from specializing in treating codependency for over two decades.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1689 (Number of characters: 135):
I wrote the gist of this chapter one satori-blessed night when I noticed that I anxiously
apologized to a chair that I had bumped into.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1690 (Number of characters: 122):
I think I probably apologized to inanimate objects
many times before in my life, but this was the first time I noticed it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1691 (Number of characters: 172):
Realizing that I had just apologized to a chair suddenly made me feel enraged. I felt furious
that something had happened to me to give me a Pavlovian “I’m sorry” response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1692 (Number of characters: 177):
I had been pursuing family of origin exploration for quite some time, and the accumulated
evidence quickly convinced me that my parents deeply imprinted me with a fawn response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1693 (Number of characters: 132):
I was
brainwashed with a default program to ingratiatingly apologize when anything in the natural
order of things changed around me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1694 (Number of characters: 338):
Sudden anxiety responses to apparently innocuous circumstances like my example are often
emotional flashbacks to earlier traumatic events. Sometimes a current event can have only the
vaguest resemblance to a past traumatic situation, and this can be enough to trigger the psyche’s
hard-wiring for a fight, flight, freeze or fawn response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1695 (Number of characters: 196):
In this case I fawned to the chair, subliminally experiencing it as a dangerous parent and
codependently apologizing to it like a toddler anticipating punishment for touching something

forbidden.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1696 (Number of characters: 80):
As I free-associated on this I also realized that I was addicted to apologizing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1697 (Number of characters: 132):
I had
apologized for long traffic lights, for changes in the weather, and most especially for other
people’s mistakes and bad moods.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1698 (Number of characters: 226):
COMPARING FAWN ORIGINS WITH FIGHT, FLIGHT AND FREEZE
ORIGINS
I chose the name fawn for the fourth ‘F’ in the fight/flight/freeze/fawn typology, because
according to Webster, it means: “to act servilely; to cringe and flatter”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1699 (Number of characters: 81):
I believe it is this
response that is at the core of many codependents’ behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1700 (Number of characters: 119):
As a toddler, the codependent learns quickly that protesting abuse leads to even more
frightening parental retaliation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1701 (Number of characters: 155):
Thus she responds by relinquishing her fight response, deleting
“no” from her vocabulary and never developing the language skills of healthy assertiveness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1702 (Number of characters: 157):
Moreover, many abusive parents reserve their most harsh punishments for “talking back”,
and hence ruthlessly extinguish the fight response in their children.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1703 (Number of characters: 106):
Unfortunately, this typically
happens at such an early age that they later have little or no memory of it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1704 (Number of characters: 121):
The future codependent also learns early on that her natural flight response intensifies her
danger if she tries to flee.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1705 (Number of characters: 121):
“I’ll teach you to run away from me!” is a common response that
precedes the spanking typically awarded to such behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1706 (Number of characters: 162):
Later, when the child is older she may also learn that the ultimate flight response, running
away from home, is hopelessly impractical and even more danger-laden.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1707 (Number of characters: 170):
Traumatizing families,
however, seem to be on the rise, as there is an epidemic of children [as young as pre-teens]
becoming runaways and ending up in dire circumstances.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1708 (Number of characters: 108):
Many toddlers, at some point, transmute the flight urge into the running around in circles of
hyperactivity.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1709 (Number of characters: 117):
This adaptation “works” on some level to help them escape from the
uncontainable feelings of the abandonment mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1710 (Number of characters: 71):
Many of these unfortunates later
symbolically run away from their pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1711 (Number of characters: 161):
They deteriorate into the obsessive-compulsive
adaptations of workaholism, busyholism, spend-aholism, and sex and love addiction that are
common in flight types.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1712 (Number of characters: 136):
The toddler who bypasses the adaptation of the flight defense may drift into developing the
freeze response and become the “lost child.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1713 (Number of characters: 79):
This child escapes his fear by slipping more and
more deeply into dissociation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1714 (Number of characters: 91):
He learns to let his parents’ verbal and emotional abuse “go in one
ear and out the other.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1715 (Number of characters: 142):
It is not uncommon for this type to devolve in adolescence into the
numbing substance addictions of pot, alcohol, opiates and other “downers”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1716 (Number of characters: 99):
The future codependent toddler, however, wisely gives up on the fight, flight and freeze
responses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1717 (Number of characters: 92):
Instead she learns to fawn her way into the occasional safety of being perceived as
helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1718 (Number of characters: 138):
It bears repeating that the fawn type is often one of the gifted children that Alice Miller
writes about in The Drama Of The Gifted Child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1719 (Number of characters: 125):
She is the precocious one who discovers that a
modicum of safety can be purchased by becoming variously useful to her parent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1720 (Number of characters: 81):
Servitude, ingratiation, and obsequiousness become important survival strategies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1721 (Number of characters: 69):
She
cleverly forfeits all needs that might inconvenience her parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1722 (Number of characters: 64):
She stops having preferences and
opinions that might anger them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1723 (Number of characters: 108):
Boundaries of every kind are surrendered to mollify her parents,
who repudiate their duty of caring for her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1724 (Number of characters: 115):
As we saw in the last chapter, she is often parentified
and becomes as thoroughly helpful to the parent as she can.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1725 (Number of characters: 84):
I wonder how many therapists besides me were prepared for their careers in this way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1726 (Number of characters: 87):
All this loss of self begins before the child has many words, and certainly no insight.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1727 (Number of characters: 127):
For
the budding codependent, all hints of danger soon immediately trigger servile behaviors and
abdication of rights and needs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1728 (Number of characters: 247):
These response patterns are so deeply set in the psyche, that as adults, many codependents
automatically respond to threat like dogs, symbolically rolling over on their backs, wagging their
tails, hoping for a little mercy and an occasional scrap.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1729 (Number of characters: 115):
Webster’s second entry for fawn is: “to
show friendliness by licking hands, wagging its tail, etc.: said of a dog.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1730 (Number of characters: 89):
I find it tragic that some
codependents are as loyal as dogs to even the worst “masters”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1731 (Number of characters: 126):
Finally, I have noticed that extreme emotional abandonment, as described in chapter 5, also
creates this kind of codependency.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1732 (Number of characters: 167):
The severely neglected child experiences extreme lack of
connection as traumatic, and sometimes responds to this fearful condition by overdeveloping the
fawn response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1733 (Number of characters: 158):
Once a child realizes that being useful and not requiring anything for herself gets
her some positive attention from her parents, codependency begins to grow.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 1734 (Number of characters: 58):
It becomes an
increasingly automatic habit over the years.
