chunk 2186 (Number of characters: 199):
Discerning the trigger of a flashback is a slippery slope. Seeing the trigger can often rescue
us from blaming and hating ourselves for the flashback, but there is not always an identifiable
trigger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2187 (Number of characters: 104):
In such situations, looking for the trigger can quickly deteriorate into self-pathologizing
vivisection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2188 (Number of characters: 100):
This slippery slope can quickly become a cliff as we plummet deeper into the abyss
of the flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2189 (Number of characters: 44):
It is almost always a matter of perspective.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2190 (Number of characters: 84):
Am I trigger-searching from a place of being on
my side or a place of fault-finding?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2191 (Number of characters: 156):
When it is the latter, it is best to abandon the search and
move toward invoking self-acceptance, as there will always be triggerings that are unfathomable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2192 (Number of characters: 97):
The process of self-support needs to trump the healthy urge to “figure it ALL out” at such times.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2193 (Number of characters: 172):
The process of self-acceptance also needs to trump any of your efforts to fix the flashback
when this striving becomes tainted with self-irritation and self-disappointment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2194 (Number of characters: 146):
Sometimes, as
described above, the best understanding you can achieve is an overarching one that your inner
child is feeling profoundly abandoned.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2195 (Number of characters: 151):
She is cowering from a humiliating attack from your
critic and needs for you to switch gears and demonstrate that you will care for her no matter
what.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2196 (Number of characters: 138):
Existential Triggers
Many psychologists use the term existential to describe the fact that all human beings are subject
to painful events.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2197 (Number of characters: 79):
These are normal recurring afflictions that everyone suffers from time to time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2198 (Number of characters: 135):
Horrible world events, difficult choices, illnesses and periodic feelings of abject loneliness are
common examples of existential pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2199 (Number of characters: 164):
Existential calamities can be especially triggering for
survivors, because we typically have so much family-of-origin calamity for them to trigger us
into reliving.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2200 (Number of characters: 123):
Another particularly triggering existential phenomenon is the fact that we all suffer
invisible, unpredictable mood shifts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2201 (Number of characters: 60):
Good moods sometimes inexplicably deteriorate into bad
ones.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2202 (Number of characters: 106):
As novelist, David Mitchell wrote “Good moods are as fragile as eggs… and bad moods as
fragile as bricks”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2203 (Number of characters: 82):
Unpredictable shifts in your emotional weather are typically problematic in Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2204 (Number of characters: 67):
These
shifts can quickly trigger you into a full-fledged flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2205 (Number of characters: 112):
This is usually because you were
punished or abandoned in the past for showing your full complement of feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2206 (Number of characters: 96):
So now, out of
old habit, you automatically dissociate when your emotional weather is inclement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2207 (Number of characters: 215):
The inner child often experiences this as you reverting to the pre-recovery adult who had no
time for feelings. The child then feels that he is once again trapped in the past where he was so
devastatingly abandoned.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2208 (Number of characters: 78):
Perhaps, the resultant flashback is his only way to really get your
attention.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2209 (Number of characters: 146):
This is, again, why I try to make my default position turning to myself and my inner
child with unconditional positive regard as much as possible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2210 (Number of characters: 491):
Later Stage Recovery
When your recovery matures sufficiently, you realize that much of the emotional pain of your
flashbacks is appropriate but delayed reactions to your childhood abuse and neglect. You process
your feelings in a way that resolves flashbacks, and also builds an increasingly healthy, sense of
self. This, in turn, leads to an ongoing reduction of the unresolved childhood pain that fuels your
emotional flashbacks. Flashbacks then become less frequent, intense and enduring.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2211 (Number of characters: 108):
Eventually,
you learn to invoke your self-protective instinct as soon as you realize that you are triggered.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2212 (Number of characters: 195):
As
flashbacks decrease and become more manageable, the defensive structures built around them
(narcissistic, obsessive-compulsive, dissociative and/or codependent) are more readily
deconstructed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2213 (Number of characters: 124):
At this stage of your recovery, you may now experience an ironically satisfying experience
when you come out of a flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2214 (Number of characters: 270):
You may sense on many levels of your awareness that life as
a child in your parents’ house was even worse than you realized. Simultaneously, you may feel a

corresponding sense of relief that you are now freer from your parents’ life-spoiling influence
than ever before.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2264 (Number of characters: 122):
SHRINKING THE INNER CRITIC
This chapter explores what one of my clients calls the “nasty and sneaky tricks of the critic.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2265 (Number of characters: 110):
ORIGIN OF THE CPTSD CRITIC
A flashback-inducing critic is typically spawned in a danger-ridden childhood home.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2266 (Number of characters: 113):
This is true
whether the danger comes from the passive abandonment of neglect or the active abandonment
of abuse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2267 (Number of characters: 111):
When parents do not provide safe enough bonding and positive feedback, the child
flounders in anxiety and fear.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2268 (Number of characters: 244):
Many children appear to be hard-wired to adapt to this
endangering abandonment with perfectionism. A prevailing climate of danger forces the child’s superego to over-cultivate the various
programs of perfectionism and endangerment listed below.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2269 (Number of characters: 112):
Once again, the superego is the part
of the psyche that learns parental rules in order to gain their acceptance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2270 (Number of characters: 138):
The inner critic is the superego gone bad. The inner critic is the superego in overdrive
desperately trying to win your parents’ approval.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2271 (Number of characters: 128):
When perfectionist striving fails to win
welcoming from your parents, the inner critic becomes increasingly hostile and caustic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2272 (Number of characters: 113):
It festers
into a virulent inner voice that increasingly manifests self-hate, self-disgust and self-
abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2273 (Number of characters: 206):
The inner critic blames you incessantly for shortcomings that it imagines to be the
cause of your parents’ rejection. It is incapable of understanding that the real cause lies in your
parents’ shortcomings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2274 (Number of characters: 122):
As a traumatized child, your over-aroused sympathetic nervous system also drives you to
become increasingly hypervigilant.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2275 (Number of characters: 323):
Hypervigilance is a fixation on looking for danger that comes
from excessive exposure to real danger. In an effort to recognize, predict and avoid danger,
hypervigilance is ingrained in your approach to being in the world. Hypervigilance narrows your
attention into an incessant, on-guard scanning of the people around you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2276 (Number of characters: 92):
It also frequently
projects you into the future, imagining danger in upcoming social events.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2277 (Number of characters: 113):
Moreover,

hypervigilance typically devolves into intense performance anxiety on every level of self-
expression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2278 (Number of characters: 105):
Like the soldier overlong in combat, ptsd sets in because you feel as if you are constantly
under attack.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2279 (Number of characters: 145):
Unfortunately, internal attack is now added to external attack, and you become
locked into hypervigilance and sympathetic nervous system arousal.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2280 (Number of characters: 91):
A traumatized child becomes desperate to relieve the anxiety and depression of abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2281 (Number of characters: 84):
The critic-driven child can only think about the ways she is too much or not enough.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2282 (Number of characters: 80):
The child’s
unfolding sense of self [the healthy ego], finds no room to develop.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2283 (Number of characters: 42):
Her identity virtually
becomes the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2284 (Number of characters: 28):
The superego trumps the ego.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2285 (Number of characters: 186):
In this process, the critic becomes increasingly virulent and eventually switches from the
parents’ internalized voice: “You’re a bad boy/girl” to the first person: “I’m a bad boy/girl.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2286 (Number of characters: 69):
Over time, self-goading increasingly deteriorates: “I’m such a loser.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2287 (Number of characters: 59):
I’m so pathetic… bad...
ugly…worthless…stupid...defective.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2288 (Number of characters: 73):
This is unlike the soldier in combat who does not develop a toxic critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2289 (Number of characters: 102):
This process
whereby the superego becomes carcinogenic is a key juncture where ptsd morphs into Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2290 (Number of characters: 78):
The cruel, totalitarian inner critic is a key distinguishing feature of Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2291 (Number of characters: 402):

chunk 2437 (Number of characters: 206):
The Critic As The Shaming Internalized Parents
Not infrequently, a client comes into a session and shamefully confesses something that sounds

like this: “I called myself a f*ckwit over and over last night.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2438 (Number of characters: 80):
I must really be inherently messed
up, because I know my mother never said that.

chunk 2440 (Number of characters: 69):
The explanation for this is that the critic is essentially a process.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2441 (Number of characters: 145):
It is an ever developing
process that co-opts our creativity and funnels it into “new and improved” ways of imitating our
parents’ disparagement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2442 (Number of characters: 150):
Parental contempt is the key piece of the emotional abuse that creates toxic shame. Toxic
shame is the emotional matrix of the abandonment depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2443 (Number of characters: 65):
It is also the glue that keeps us
stuck helplessly in flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2444 (Number of characters: 73):
As such, toxic shame is the affect or emotional tone of the inner
critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2445 (Number of characters: 90):
Shame besmirches us as it emotionally intensifies each of the 14 assaults described above.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2446 (Number of characters: 229):
In main stream psychology, shame is often described as a social emotion. Normal shame is
a somewhat healthy, self-regulating emotional reaction that arises when someone witnesses us
acting in an unfair, offensive, or hurtful way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2447 (Number of characters: 46):
This is not the case with toxic shame however.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2448 (Number of characters: 124):
Many Cptsd survivors in recovery soon
realize that they do not need a witness to suddenly be catapulted into a shame attack.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2449 (Number of characters: 52):
Dmitri was all alone when he knocked over the glass.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2450 (Number of characters: 10):
Or was he?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2451 (Number of characters: 323):
There is an invisible social context to toxic shame attacks. Toxic shame is social
because the inner critic came into existence through pathological interactions with our parents. Moreover, toxic shame is social in the moment of the solitary flashback, because at the time it is
as if we are in the presence of our parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2452 (Number of characters: 103):
For me, the strongest evidence of this occurs when I am on my own and trying to do
something difficult.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2453 (Number of characters: 143):
If I make a mistake or do not accomplish my task as efficiently as possible, I
often feel very anxious as if I am being watched and criticized.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2454 (Number of characters: 77):
I believe this phenomenon corresponds with an internalization of our parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2455 (Number of characters: 140):
Our parents
were such formative and formidable presences in our developing life, that we have strong
representations of them in our psyches.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2456 (Number of characters: 70):
These representations include their beliefs and
condemnation about us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2457 (Number of characters: 132):
Until we work on shrinking their influence, our internalized parents exist
in our psyches as the key controlling force of our lives.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2458 (Number of characters: 122):
Facing The Stubbornness Of The Critic
The work of shrinking the critic is one of the most essential processes of recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2459 (Number of characters: 152):
As obvious as
its value may seem as you read this, embracing the task of renouncing the critic is much more
challenging than it may seem at first blush.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2460 (Number of characters: 160):
The critic’s programs are not only burned deeply into our psyches by our parents, but we
also unknowingly emblazon them into our minds by mimicking our parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2461 (Number of characters: 60):
We are now the key
reinforcing agents of their toxic legacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2462 (Number of characters: 119):
With little mindfulness of it, we injure ourselves with
countless angry, self-disgusted repetitions of their judgments.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2463 (Number of characters: 124):
Recovery now depends on you
withdrawing your blind allegiance to this terrible process of only noticing yourself negatively.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2464 (Number of characters: 65):
The task of diminishing these self-negating patterns is daunting.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2465 (Number of characters: 106):
It is typically lifetime work
– often negotiable only at the rate of two-steps-forward, one-step backward.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2466 (Number of characters: 73):
And oh how unfair
it is that the step backward often feels more like six!

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2467 (Number of characters: 35):
Yet recent findings in neuroscience

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2468 (Number of characters: 182):
[The General Theory of Love; The Talking Cure] have
shown that biologically ingrained mental patterns can be diminished and replaced with new ones

through long term repetitive work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2469 (Number of characters: 162):
I believe this is analogous to adding or subtracting girth to
parts of your physique, which typically takes seemingly innumerable repetitions of a given
exercise.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2470 (Number of characters: 132):
In the last couple of decades my brain has gone from being my own worst enemy almost all
the time to being very reliably on my side.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2471 (Number of characters: 85):
I have also seen similar gains with many of the clients
I have worked with long-term.

chunk 2472 (Number of characters: 447):
Perfectionism And Emotional Neglect As stated earlier, perfectionism also seems to be an instinctual defense for emotionally
abandoned children. The existential impossibility of perfection saves the child from giving up,
unless or until lack of success forces her to retreat into a dissociative freeze response or an anti-
social fight response. Perfectionism also provides a sense of meaning and direction for the powerless and
unsupported child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2473 (Number of characters: 68):
Striving to be perfect offers her a semblance of a sense of control.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2474 (Number of characters: 159):
Self-
control is also safer to pursue because abandoning parents typically reserve their severest
punishment for children who are vocal about their negligence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2475 (Number of characters: 303):
As the quest for perfection fails over and over, and as parental acceptance and nurturing
remain elusive, imperfection becomes synonymous with shame and fear. Perceived imperfection
triggers fear of abandonment, which triggers self-hate for imperfection, which expands
abandonment into self-abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2476 (Number of characters: 84):
This in turn amps fear up even further, which in turn
intensifies self-disgust, etc.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2477 (Number of characters: 78):
On and on it goes in a downward spiral of fear and shame-encrusted
depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2478 (Number of characters: 110):
It can go on for hours, days, weeks, and for those with severe Cptsd, can become
their standard mode of being.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2479 (Number of characters: 109):
More On Endangerment
The importance and magnitude of the critic’s endangerment programs cannot be overstated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2480 (Number of characters: 185):
I
have worked with numerous “well-therapized” people who were relatively free from
perfectionism, but still seriously afflicted with the critic’s addiction to noticing potential danger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2481 (Number of characters: 341):
Said another way, I have seen survivors eliminate much of their perfectionist, self-attacking
thinking without realizing that the critic was still flooding their minds with fear-inducing
thoughts and images. I learned to disidentify from perfectionism long before I learned to stop perseverating on
my critic’s harrowing snapshots of danger.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2482 (Number of characters: 107):
In fact, I became quite adept at morphing these
snapshots into feature long films about my imminent demise.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2483 (Number of characters: 166):
Permanent abandonment, public humiliation, lethal illness, lonely death, imminent attack,
and penniless homelessness are common endangerment themes of many survivors.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2484 (Number of characters: 110):
One of my
clients identified his inner critic endangerment process as: “My critic, the horror movie
producer”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2485 (Number of characters: 46):
This made me think: “My critic the terrorist”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2486 (Number of characters: 80):
If I had to describe the two most key processes of the critic, I would say this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2487 (Number of characters: 88):
First, the critic
is above all a self-perpetuating process of extreme negative noticing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2488 (Number of characters: 134):
Second the critic is a
constant hypervigilance that sees disaster hovering in the next moment about to launch into a
full-court-press.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2489 (Number of characters: 158):
Using Anger To Thought-Stop The Critic
Thought-stopping is the process of using willpower to disidentify from and interrupt toxic
thoughts and visualizations.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2490 (Number of characters: 88):
Sometimes visualizing a stop sign at the same time can help
strengthen thought-stopping.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2491 (Number of characters: 155):
Since traumatizing parents cripple the instinctive fight response of their child, recovering
the anger of the fight response is essential in healing Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2492 (Number of characters: 92):
We need the aid of our fight
response to empower the process of thought-stopping the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2493 (Number of characters: 194):
I cannot over-encourage you to use your anger to stop the critic in its tracks. We can re-
hijack the anger of the critic’s attack, and forcefully redirect it at the critic instead of ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2494 (Number of characters: 138):
We can then silently and internally say “No!” or “Stop!” or “Shut Up!” to short-circuit
drasticizing and perfectionistic mental processes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2495 (Number of characters: 100):
Angrily saying “No!” to the critic sets an internal boundary against unnatural, anti-self
processes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2496 (Number of characters: 93):
It is the hammer of self-renovating carpentry that rebuilds our instinct of self-
protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2497 (Number of characters: 168):
Furthermore recovery is deepened by directing our anger at anyone who helped
install the critic, as well as at anyone who is currently contributing to keeping it alive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2534 (Number of characters: 204):
Shame Is Blame Unfairly Turned Against The Self
The great psychologist, Erik Eriksen, gave us a great tool when he formulated this emotional
mathematics equation. “Shame is blame turned against the self”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2535 (Number of characters: 85):
Our parents were too big and
powerful to blame, so we had to blame ourselves instead.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2536 (Number of characters: 132):
Now, however we are free of them,
and we can cut off the critic’s shame supply by redirecting unfair self-blame back to our parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2537 (Number of characters: 170):
You can redirect the anger of the critic’s blaming messages away from you. You can direct
the anger onto the installers of the critic, or sideways onto the critic itself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2538 (Number of characters: 221):
You can give shame
back by allowing yourself to feel angry and disgusted at the image of your parent bullying you. You can rage at them for overwhelming you with shame when you were too young and small to
defend yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2539 (Number of characters: 116):
An inner critic that has dominated us since childhood, however, does not give up its
rulership of the psyche easily.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2540 (Number of characters: 142):
It stubbornly refuses to accept the updated information that
adulthood now offers the possibility of increasing safety and healthy attachment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2541 (Number of characters: 102):
It is as if the
critic has worn a flashback-inducing groove in the brain the size of the Grand Canyon.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2542 (Number of characters: 131):
Now, any
of the thinking patterns listed earlier can hair-trigger an amygdala-hijacking that dumps us into
the abandonment mélange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2543 (Number of characters: 86):
Progress in critic-shrinking is often infinitesimally slow and indiscernible at first.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2544 (Number of characters: 85):
Our
brains have become addicted to only noticing what is wrong and what is dangerous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2545 (Number of characters: 99):
And as with
most addictions, breaking this deeply entrenched habit may require lifelong management.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2546 (Number of characters: 133):

over with all the ferocity we can muster.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2547 (Number of characters: 137):

that is mad about how grossly unfair our parents’ bullying and indifference was.

--------------------------------------------------

and bullying ourselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2549 (Number of characters: 103):

even know what was happening to us.

--------------------------------------------------

up!”

chunk 2552 (Number of characters: 291):
With enough healthy inner self-defense, the survivor gradually learns to reject her
unconscious acceptance of self-abuse and self-abandonment. Her sense of healthy self-protection
begins to emerge and over time grows into a fierce willingness to stop unfair criticism - internal
or external.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2553 (Number of characters: 177):
Psychologically speaking, this is part of the process of working through repetition
compulsion. Deconstructing repetition compulsion has both an internal and external dimension.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2554 (Number of characters: 273):
On the internal dimension, we decrease the habit of repetitively perpetrating our parents’ abuse
against ourselves by staunchly confronting the inner critic. This then allows us to become more
mindful on the external dimension when others reenact our parents’ mistreatment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2555 (Number of characters: 65):

confront them to stop, or banish them from our lives.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2556 (Number of characters: 131):

in Soul Without Shame, by Byron Brown, and Healing Your Emotional Self by Beverly Engel.

chunk 2558 (Number of characters: 213):
Embracing The Critic
In my experience, until the fight response is substantially restored, the Cptsd client benefits little
from CBT, psychodynamic or mindfulness techniques that encourage us to accept the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2559 (Number of characters: 126):
In
later recovery, when the survivor has removed the venomous stinger from the critic, these
techniques can be quite valuable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2560 (Number of characters: 93):
Then, and only then, are we able to reconnect with the helpful
side of healthy self-criticism

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2561 (Number of characters: 57):
[see Stone and Stone’s book Embracing Your Inner Critic].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2562 (Number of characters: 124):
A typical indication that the critic has mellowed into being functional is that it speaks to us
in a kind and helpful voice.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2563 (Number of characters: 104):
It reminds us dispassionately to adjust our behavior when we can and
ought to be doing something better.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2564 (Number of characters: 123):
If, however, it blasts us for imperfection, it is giving itself
away as the toxic critic that was installed by our parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2565 (Number of characters: 171):
A left-brained, objective approach of embracing the critic is rarely helpful unless it is
balanced with a subjective, right-brained capacity for assertive self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2566 (Number of characters: 127):
Perhaps this is
because the inner critic appears to operate simultaneously with hyper-emotional right-brain
flashback dynamics.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2567 (Number of characters: 157):
Perhaps toxic inner critic processes are so emotionally overwhelming that
efforts to resist them rationally and dispassionately are too weak to be effective.

chunk 2568 (Number of characters: 193):
THOUGHT-SUBSTITUTION AND THOUGHT-CORRECTION
Thought-substitution, especially in the form of thought-correction, is another essential tool for
empowering the work of thought-stopping the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2569 (Number of characters: 109):
Many years ago, I sensed that my critic
became as tough as a body-builder’s bicep through myriad repetitions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2570 (Number of characters: 118):
I guessed that similarly
exercising self-protective responses to the critic would build my thought-correction muscles.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2571 (Number of characters: 127):
It

did in fact, and my instinct to protect myself almost always arises automatically now when I am
triggered into a flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2572 (Number of characters: 174):
I believe I am not exaggerating when I say that tens of thousands of
positive thought-substitutions have rewarded me with a psyche that is fairly consistently user-
friendly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2573 (Number of characters: 158):
Accordingly, I encourage you to immediately confront the critic’s negative messages with
positive ones like those in the list at the beginning of the chapter.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2574 (Number of characters: 195):
This is essential in Cptsd
recovery, because a single unconfronted toxic thought can act like a virus and rage infectiously
out of control into a flu-like mélange of shame, fear and helplessness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2575 (Number of characters: 133):
Moving quickly into thought-stopping and thought correction often obviates a headlong
tumble into the downward spiral of a flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2576 (Number of characters: 122):
This is essential in critic-work, as the critic
typically attacks us more viciously once it has gotten up a head of steam.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2577 (Number of characters: 120):
At such times, the critic
can hypocritically scorn us for falling back into self-criticism when we “should” know better.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2578 (Number of characters: 127):
This is the time then, more than ever, to “thought-correct and not self-berate,” as my last intern
liked to say to her clients.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2579 (Number of characters: 149):
Additionally, I encourage you to write out a list of your positive qualities and
accomplishments to read it to yourself if you get lost in self-hate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2580 (Number of characters: 106):
Toolbox 5 in chapter 16 is a
practical exercise to help you elaborate this list in a multidimensional way.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2581 (Number of characters: 166):
Making a written record of your positive attributes is especially helpful as flashbacks often
create a temporary amnesia about your essential worthiness and goodness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2582 (Number of characters: 90):
Flashbacks seem to
involve a temporary loss of access to more current left-brain learning.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2583 (Number of characters: 80):
MRI’s show greatly
reduced left-brain activity in hyper-aroused Cptsd survivors.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2584 (Number of characters: 87):
In my experience, memorizing your
list enhances your capacity to dissolve that amnesia.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2585 (Number of characters: 153):
Reciting part or all of your list over and over like a mantra can also help you during those
times when the critic is particularly severe and relentless.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2586 (Number of characters: 106):
If you have trouble making the list or
filling out Toolbox 5, ask a friend or a therapist for their input.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2587 (Number of characters: 120):
Additionally, please let me
remind you that qualities do not have to be perfect or ever-present to qualify as qualities.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2588 (Number of characters: 60):
If it is
true of you most of the time then, it is a quality.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2589 (Number of characters: 82):
Finally, positive visualization can be a powerful adjunct to thought-substitution.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2590 (Number of characters: 221):
Some
survivors gradually learn to short-circuit the fear-mongering processes of the critic by invoking
images of past successes and accomplishments, as well as picturing safe places, loving friends or
comforting memories.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2591 (Number of characters: 191):
There are also a variety of CD’s available at places like Amazon.com that
contain guided meditations that use positive language and imagery in a way that enhances
deactivation and relaxation.

chunk 2592 (Number of characters: 201):
Perspective-Substitution And Correction
The most important thought correction of all is a switch in the perspective of our thinking. Perspective-substitution is a broadening of our overall perspective.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2593 (Number of characters: 239):
It moves our viewpoint
from the critic’s narrow, negative focus to the more balanced and accurate focus of the observing
ego – the mindful self. Perspective-substitution helps us to dethrone the critic from its life-negating point of view.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2594 (Number of characters: 164):
This resembles the firing of a bad manager or inept coach – one with a distorted view who dwells
so much on what is wrong that he cannot see anything that is right.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2595 (Number of characters: 107):
As stated in chapter 1, perspective-substitution can be enhanced with the spiritual practice

of gratitude.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2596 (Number of characters: 343):
In this vein, gratitude is a type of mindfulness that looks for empirical proof that life
is essentially good even though it is also quite difficult at times. Perspective-Substitution And Gratitude
Gratitude is a delicate subject to write about because many survivors have been abused by
shaming advice to “just be grateful for what you have”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2597 (Number of characters: 123):
Consequently many survivors totally
reject the concept of gratitude and throw the baby out with the scorn-sodden bathwater.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2598 (Number of characters: 111):
Once
again, this is quite understandable when you legitimately had little to be grateful for in your
childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2599 (Number of characters: 123):
Moreover, the concept of gratitude is damagingly used by some psychologists to support the
psychological defense of denial.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2600 (Number of characters: 67):
They tout gratitude as a fast track that can bypass traumatic
pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2601 (Number of characters: 58):
This is worse than absurd when applied to Cptsd survivors.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2602 (Number of characters: 147):
It is in fact shamefully abusive
to survivors because profound, extended trauma cannot be resolved until it is fully understood
and worked through.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2603 (Number of characters: 378):
Gratitude is nevertheless a wonderful natural experience that can recurrently enhance the
quality of your life. You can cultivate a perspective that is open to noticing what there is to be
grateful about as long as you do not do it with the intention of creating a permanent feeling of
gratitude. Over time an attitude of gratitude can gradually increase authentic gratefulness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2604 (Number of characters: 54):
This can best be illustrated with the example of love.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2605 (Number of characters: 151):
While it is of course healthy to adopt a
cognitive attitude of love toward our friends and chosen family, it is impossible to feel loving all
the time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2606 (Number of characters: 109):
If I expect that of myself, I give my inner critic endless fodder to attack me for not
feeling loving enough.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2607 (Number of characters: 138):
Similarly if I expect myself to feel grateful all the time, I keep the critic’s
prodigious program of self-disappointment hale and hearty.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2608 (Number of characters: 86):
Nonetheless, aligning with attitudes like love and gratitude is generally therapeutic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2609 (Number of characters: 425):
When I
am temporarily stuck in a flashback feeling alienated from life, remembering what I am usually
grateful for in life can sometimes pull me out of the polarized negative thinking that helps keep
the flashback alive. Invoking gratitude is particularly difficult, and often impossible at first, because flashbacks
typically strand us in an emotional overwhelm that cancels out our ability to feel anything good
about life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2610 (Number of characters: 121):
Reminding ourselves of what is worthwhile in our lives does not seem to help much in
the early phases of using this tool.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2611 (Number of characters: 293):
However, with enough practice of positive-noticing, we can
sometimes relax out of a flashback by invoking our memories of gratitude. When I experience this at the end of an especially long flashback, positive-noticing
sometimes arises spontaneously and brings with it sweet tears of gratitude.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2612 (Number of characters: 151):
These are also
typically tears of relief, and tears of an achieved sense of belonging. These tears typically arise unbidden, seemingly out of the blue.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2613 (Number of characters: 303):
Typically they are
positively triggered by experiences of beauty or connection, such as when flowers authentically
strike me as beautiful once again, or when my appreciation of music returns and deeply moves
my soul, or when I suddenly fully feel how much I love my wife, my son, my friend or my client.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2614 (Number of characters: 467):
After a painful lapse in being able to emotionally enjoy these experiences, this return brings
these gratitude-laden tears which on really momentous occasions can vacillate between crying
and laughing as I resurface into authentically being grateful to be alive. Once again, my experience is that the more I practice the thought substitution of focusing on
what I am grateful for, the sooner genuine gratitude returns to me on the occasions that I lose
touch with it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2615 (Number of characters: 64):
A powerful way to practice perspective-correction is as follows.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2616 (Number of characters: 79):
After you go to bed at
night, list at least ten positive happenings of the day.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2617 (Number of characters: 112):
More often than not these will not be peak
experiences, but rather basic and simple pleasures and appreciations.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2618 (Number of characters: 302):
They may be as simple as a
catchy tune, an engaging color, a sweet scent, an enjoyable food serving of the day, a new flower
in a local garden, a satisfying TV show, a neighbor’s hello, a feeling of fitness climbing the
stairs, soothing words from a favorite author, or a pleasant encounter with a pet.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2619 (Number of characters: 113):
Decades of this practice have helped me immeasurably to upgrade the sour perspective I
inherited from my parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2620 (Number of characters: 140):
Alignment with this function of the healthy observing ego provides us
with a more balanced and accurate perception of life and other people.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2621 (Number of characters: 243):
The Neuroplasticity Of The Brain
I am repeatedly heartened to read the accumulating evidence from neuroscience research that
proves the neuroplasticity of the brain. Neuroplasticity means that the brain can grow and change
throughout our life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2622 (Number of characters: 95):
Old self-destructive neural pathways can be diminished and new healthier
ones can replace them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2623 (Number of characters: 74):
A General Theory of Love by Thomas Lewis inspiringly explicates this
fact.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2624 (Number of characters: 198):
This fact helps me to remember that the critic can indeed literally be shrunk via longterm,
frequent and dedicated use of the thought-stopping, thought-substitution and thought-correction
practices.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2625 (Number of characters: 96):
As recovery progresses, you notice the critic sooner before its attack becomes multidimensional.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2626 (Number of characters: 67):
This then allows you to take more immediate self-protective action.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2627 (Number of characters: 131):
Moreover, Cptsd flashbacks
can be utilized as evidence of, and in later stages of recovery, proof of your childhood
traumatization.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2628 (Number of characters: 136):
Flashbacks point irrefutably to the fact that your parent’s abandonment forced
you to habituate to hypervigilance and negative noticing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2629 (Number of characters: 144):
SHRINKING THE OUTER CRITIC
THE OUTER CRITIC: THE ENEMY OF RELATIONSHIP
In Cptsd, the critic can have two aspects: inner critic and outer critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2630 (Number of characters: 260):
The inner critic is the part
of your mind that views you as flawed and unworthy. The outer critic is the part that views
everyone else as flawed and unworthy. When the outer critic is running your mind, people
appear to be too awful and too dangerous to trust.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2631 (Number of characters: 109):
When she was stuck in an outer critic attack, one of my clients would often rant like this:
“Everybody s*cks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2632 (Number of characters: 32):
People are so selfish and scary.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2633 (Number of characters: 48):
They either f*ck you over or they let you
down.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2634 (Number of characters: 70):
She eventually named this an “I’m-moving-to-another-planet flashback.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2635 (Number of characters: 79):
The outer critic is the counterpart of the self-esteem-destroying inner critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2636 (Number of characters: 120):
It uses the same
programs of perfectionism and endangerment against others that your inner critic uses against
yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2637 (Number of characters: 132):
Via its all-or-none programming, the outer critic rejects others because they are never
perfect and cannot be guaranteed to be safe.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2638 (Number of characters: 129):
As with the inner critic, outer critic attacks are usually internal and silent, unless you are a
fight type as we will see below.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2639 (Number of characters: 71):
When we regress into the outer critic, we obsess about the unworthiness

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2640 (Number of characters: 34):
[imperfection] and
treacherousness

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2641 (Number of characters: 26):
[dangerousness] of others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2642 (Number of characters: 73):
Unconsciously, we do this to avoid emotional
investment in relationships.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2643 (Number of characters: 355):
The outer critic developed in reaction to parents who were too dangerous to trust. The outer
critic helped us to be hyperaware of the subtlest signal that our parents were deteriorating into
their most dangerous behaviors. Over time the outer critic grew to believe that anyone and
everyone would inevitably turn out to be as untrustworthy as our parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2644 (Number of characters: 89):
Now, in situations where we no longer need it, the outer critic alienates us from others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2645 (Number of characters: 141):
It
attacks others and scares them away, or it builds fortresses of isolation whose walls are laundry
lists of their exaggerated shortcomings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2646 (Number of characters: 101):
In an awful irony, the critic attempts to protect us from

abandonment by scaring us further into it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2647 (Number of characters: 128):
If we are ever to discover the comfort of soothing connection with others, the critic’s
dictatorship of the mind must be broken.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2648 (Number of characters: 114):
The outer critic’s arsenal of intimacy-spoiling dynamics
must be consciously identified and gradually deactivated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2649 (Number of characters: 267):
4F TYPES AND OUTER CRITIC/INNER CRITIC RATIOS
Depending on your 4F type, you may gravitate to either the inner or the outer critic. Different 4F
types generally have different ratios of outer and inner critic dynamics, and some polarize
extremely to one or the other.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2650 (Number of characters: 63):
Freeze and Fight types are often polarized to the outer critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2651 (Number of characters: 52):
Fawn types tend to be
dominated by the inner critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2652 (Number of characters: 72):
Flight types can have the most variance in inner and outer critic
ratio.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2653 (Number of characters: 51):
Your subtype can also have a big influence on this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2654 (Number of characters: 128):
The Freeze type can judgmentally denounce the entire outside world to justify her all-or-
none belief that people are dangerous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2655 (Number of characters: 127):
The Flight type can use his own perfectionistic striving to
excel so that his outer critic can judge everyone else as inferior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2656 (Number of characters: 126):
The Fawn type uses inner critic
self-hate to self-censor and avoid the fear of being authentic and vulnerable in relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2657 (Number of characters: 270):
The
Fight type, in a paradoxical twist, controls others through the outer critic to prevent them from
abandoning him while at the same time using prickliness to not let them get too close. Fight types can also leave at the first sign that the other cannot be controlled.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2658 (Number of characters: 100):
One flight-
fight type, who I worked with briefly, told me with great upset about a recent betrayal.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2659 (Number of characters: 132):
His new
partner “insisted” on replacing the empty toilet paper roll so that the new roll unwound from the
bottom instead of the top.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2660 (Number of characters: 107):
He asked her once to do it his way and felt so betrayed when she did
not comply, that he broke up with her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2661 (Number of characters: 66):
I could not help feeling that she was fortunate that she got
away.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2662 (Number of characters: 102):
Unfortunately, this client was not able to take in that the lion’s share of his upset was a
flashback.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2663 (Number of characters: 132):
He had flashed back to his rigidly controlling mother frightening him into believing
that the toilet paper must unwind from the top.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2664 (Number of characters: 68):
She had punished him into believing that this was
a universal truth.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2665 (Number of characters: 79):
Perfectionism, in the hands of the outer critic, can be paranoiacally picayune.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2666 (Number of characters: 180):
Finally it is not unusual for survivors, who have significantly shrunk their dominant critic mode,
to experience a reciprocal increase in the virulence of its opposite counterpart.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2667 (Number of characters: 142):
This came as a
disappointing shock to me at a time when I was congratulating myself that my inner critic was a
mere shadow of its former self.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2668 (Number of characters: 99):
Soon thereafter, I noticed that I was plagued by a new
judgmentalness that seemed out of character.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2669 (Number of characters: 121):
Curiosity and a growing mindfulness about this
development lead me to a lot of the insights that I share in this chapter.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2670 (Number of characters: 158):
With enough
mindfulness, this shift in critic mode can then become an opportunity to further shrink the overall
combined agency of the outer and inner critic.

chunk 2671 (Number of characters: 122):
PASSSIVE-AGGRESSIVENESS AND THE OUTER CRITIC
Children are initially wired to respond angrily to parental abuse or neglect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2672 (Number of characters: 130):
Outside of the fight

types, most traumatized children learn early that protesting parental unfairness is an

chunk 2682 (Number of characters: 231):
When silently blaming the wrong person becomes habitual, it manifests as passive-

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2683 (Number of characters: 134):

chunk 2685 (Number of characters: 242):

The outer critic is the author of this intimacy-spoiling program: Being honest to a fault. In the
guise of honesty, the outer critic can negatively notice only what is imperfect in another.

chunk 2731 (Number of characters: 165):
OUTER CRITIC MODELLING IN THE MEDIA
Outer critic entrenchment is also difficult to dislodge because its parlance is normalized, and
worse, celebrated in our society.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2732 (Number of characters: 67):
Skewering people seems to be standard practice in most TV
comedies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2733 (Number of characters: 168):
Moreover, many influential, seemingly healthy adults model a communication style
that is rife with judgmentalness, sarcasm, negativity, fear-mongering and scapegoating.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2734 (Number of characters: 149):
Giving control of our social interactions to the outer critic prohibits the cultivation of the
vulnerable communication that makes intimacy possible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2735 (Number of characters: 251):
We must renounce unconscious outer

critic strategies such as: [1] “I will use angry criticism to make you afraid of me, so I can be safe
from you”; [2] “Why should I bother with people when everyone is so selfish and corrupt” [all-
or-none thinking];

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2736 (Number of characters: 232):
[3] “I will perfectionistically micromanage you to prevent you from betraying
or abandoning me”; [4] “I will rant and rave or leave at the first sign of a lonely feeling, because
‘if you really loved me, I would never feel lonely’”.

chunk 2737 (Number of characters: 124):
The Critic: Subliminal B-Grade Movie Producer
The outer critic typically arises most powerfully during emotional flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2738 (Number of characters: 134):
At such times, it
transmutes unconscious abandonment pain into an overwhelmingly negative perception of
people and of life in general.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2739 (Number of characters: 97):
It obsessively fantasizes, consciously and unconsciously, about how
people have or could hurt us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2740 (Number of characters: 101):
Over the years these fantasies typically expand from scary snapshots into film clips and
even movies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2741 (Number of characters: 143):
Without realizing it, we can amass a video collection of real and imagined
betrayals that destroy our capacity to be nurtured by human contact.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2742 (Number of characters: 315):
“Don’t trust anyone”, “Proud to be a loner”, “You can only depend on yourself”, “Lovers
always leave you”, “Kids will break your heart”, “Only fools let on what they really think”,
“Give them an inch and they’ll take a mile”, are titles of video themes survivors may develop in
their quest for interpersonal safety.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2743 (Number of characters: 162):
These defensive and often subliminal daydreams are analogs of the critic-spawned
nightmares that also shore up the “safety” work of frightening us into isolation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2744 (Number of characters: 175):
Over time, with
enough recovery, intrusive anti-intimacy reveries become clues that we are actually in a
flashback, and that we need to invoke our flashback management skills.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2745 (Number of characters: 79):
The dynamics of the outer critic are often obscured by minimization and denial.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2746 (Number of characters: 80):
Its obsessions
and “daymares” often occur just below the level of our awareness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2747 (Number of characters: 226):
They become subliminal via
their repetitiveness like the sound of waves at the beach - like the sounds of traffic in the city -
like the sound of the critic repetitively calling you or someone else a jerk, a loser, a dumbsh*t!

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2748 (Number of characters: 158):
Watching The News As A Trigger
Sometimes the outer critic’s penchant for raising false alarms ensnares us with an insatiable
hunger for listening to the news.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2749 (Number of characters: 181):
When we do not resist this junk food feeding of our psyches
with a news “service” that exults so thoroughly in the negative, we can be left floundering in a
dreadful hypervigilance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2750 (Number of characters: 102):
The critic can then work overtime to amass irrefutable proof that the world is unforgivably
dangerous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2751 (Number of characters: 80):
Isolation, and minimal or superficial relating, is therefore, our only recourse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2752 (Number of characters: 131):
At such
times any inclination to call a friend triggers images of rejection and humiliation before the
phone can even be picked up.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2753 (Number of characters: 156):
When flashbacks are particularly intense, impulses to venture out
may immediately trigger fantasies of being verbally harassed or even mugged on the street.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2754 (Number of characters: 158):
In worse case scenarios, outer critic drasticizing deteriorates into paranoia. At its worst
paranoia deteriorates into fantasies and delusions of persecution.

chunk 2774 (Number of characters: 29):
INTIMACY AND THE OUTER CRITIC

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2775 (Number of characters: 135):
As stated earlier, Cptsd typically includes an attachment disorder that comes from the absence of
a sympathetic caregiver in childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2776 (Number of characters: 138):
When the developing child lacks a supportive parental
refuge, she never learns that other people can soothe loneliness and emotional pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2777 (Number of characters: 79):
She never
learns that real intimacy grows out of sharing all of her experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2778 (Number of characters: 177):
To the degree that our caretakers attack or abandon us for showing vulnerability, to that
degree do we later avoid the authentic self-expression that is fundamental to intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2779 (Number of characters: 105):
The outer
critic forms to remind us that everyone else is surely as dangerous as our original caretakers.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2780 (Number of characters: 145):
Subliminal memories of being scorned for seeking our parents’ support then short-circuit our
inclinations to share our troubles and ask for help.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2781 (Number of characters: 120):
Even worse, retaliation fantasies can plague us for hours and days on the occasions when
we do show our vulnerabilities.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2782 (Number of characters: 108):
I once experienced this after being very honest and vulnerable in
a job interview with a committee of eight.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2783 (Number of characters: 187):
Over the next three insomnia-plagued nights, my outer
critic ran non-stop films featuring my interviewers’ contempt about everything I had said, and
disgust about all that I had left out.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2784 (Number of characters: 181):
Even after they subsequently and enthusiastically hired me,
the outer critic plagued me with “imposter syndrome” fantasies of eventually being exposed as
incompetent in the new job.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2785 (Number of characters: 134):
The No-Win Situation
While scaring us out of trusting others, the outer critic also pushes us to over-control them to
make them safer.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2786 (Number of characters: 123):
Over-controlling behaviors include shaming, excessive criticism, monologing
[conversational control] and overall bossiness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2787 (Number of characters: 97):
An extreme example of the latter is the no-win
situation, which is also known as the double bind.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2788 (Number of characters: 80):
It is described in the vernacular as “damned if
you do, and damned if you don’t.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2789 (Number of characters: 55):

Scaring Others Away
To avoid the vulnerability of being close, the outer critic can also broadcast from the various
inner critic endangerment program.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2808 (Number of characters: 116):
Catastrophizing out loud can be very triggering to others and
can be an unconscious way of making them afraid of us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2809 (Number of characters: 109):

gloom news station.

--------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2812 (Number of characters: 157):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2813 (Number of characters: 137):

others to avoid and abandon them when their negative noticing reaches a critical mass and
becomes noise pollution.

chunk 2814 (Number of characters: 220):
VACILLATING BETWEEN OUTER AND INNER CRITIC
Many Cptsd survivors flounder in caustic judgmentalness, shuffling back and forth between

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2815 (Number of characters: 38):
[the toxic
shame of the inner critic].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2816 (Number of characters: 107):
They get stuck in endless loops of detailing the relational inadequacies
of others, and then of themselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2817 (Number of characters: 110):
My parents’ twisted version of this boiled down to: “As f*cked up as we are, we’re still way
better than you”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2818 (Number of characters: 136):
Karen Horney described this trauma two-step as all-or-none lurching between

the polarities of the grandiose self and the despised self.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2819 (Number of characters: 114):
When we become lost in this process, we miss out on our crucial emotional need to
experience a sense of belonging.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2820 (Number of characters: 123):
We live in permanent estrangement oscillating between the
extremes of too good for others or too unlikeable to be included.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2821 (Number of characters: 142):
This is the excruciating social
perfectionism of the Janus-faced critic: others are too flawed to love and we are too defective to
be lovable.

--------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2825 (Number of characters: 89):

chunk 2826 (Number of characters: 65):

chunk 2829 (Number of characters: 72):

us “safe” in the hiding of silent disengagement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2837 (Number of characters: 104):
A Case Example Of The Vacillating Critic
My wife and I have been living together for more than a decade.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2838 (Number of characters: 199):
We have come a long way in
negotiating what seems to both of us - most of the time – a fair and flexible approach to handling
the innumerable tasks involved in running a household with a young child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2839 (Number of characters: 128):
But sometimes, when
I am experiencing an extended flashback, I start over-noticing imperfections in the general
household order.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2840 (Number of characters: 48):
Where the critic first points the finger varies.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2841 (Number of characters: 122):
If I am triggered into tired survival mode, the
inner critic can launch into berating me for my sub-standard contribution.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2842 (Number of characters: 123):
If on the other hand I
am triggered into flight mode and have been speed-cleaning, my outer critic can start keeping
score.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2843 (Number of characters: 102):
In this latter mode, my outer critic can perseverate about how little my wife is doing
compared to me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2844 (Number of characters: 89):
The comparisons are typically in the areas where I have recently been over-
contributing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2845 (Number of characters: 132):
But my fawn side is pretty strong and before too long, I can start noticing all the venues
where I do not contribute as much as she.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2846 (Number of characters: 52):
And suddenly I am the selfish slacker of the family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2847 (Number of characters: 96):
As
the flashback continues, I may then flip into berating myself for being picky and ungenerous.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2848 (Number of characters: 224):
In an especially strong flash back, the outer critic will come back sooner or later and start
assigning more weight and importance to my contributions, and then belittle her for being, slack,
thoughtless, self-involved, etc.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2849 (Number of characters: 146):
In our early relationship I could loop this loop for quite some time, losing hours even days
to feeling disaffected from my wife, and from myself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2850 (Number of characters: 145):
My peace of mind would deteriorate into
an inner battleground of feeling abandoned by her while simultaneously judging myself for
abandoning her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2851 (Number of characters: 105):
In the worst flashbacks, the process did not stay internal, and we would have
conflicts about this issue.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2852 (Number of characters: 46):
These days conflict rarely occurs over chores.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2853 (Number of characters: 115):
Because of what I have learned about the
outer critic, internal looping about this has also decreased immeasurably.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2854 (Number of characters: 154):
Mindfulness about my
outer and inner critic processes allows me to identify them sooner and rescue myself and my
relationship from them much more quickly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2855 (Number of characters: 88):
The scenario above is also a typical example of what worrying looks like in a flashback.

chunk 2856 (Number of characters: 100):
THE CRITIC AS JUDGE, JURY AND EXECUTIONER
As noted above, not all survivors hide their outer critic.

chunk 2857 (Number of characters: 100):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2858 (Number of characters: 158):
The survivor who is polarized to
the outer critic often develops a specious belief that his subjectively derived standards of
correctness are objective truth.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2859 (Number of characters: 145):
When triggered, he can use the critic’s combined detective-
lawyer-judge function to prosecute the other for betrayal with little or no evidence.

Imagined
slights, insignificant peccadilloes, misread facial expressions, and inaccurate “psychic”

chunk 2865 (Number of characters: 108):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2866 (Number of characters: 81):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2867 (Number of characters: 65):

chunk 2868 (Number of characters: 146):

chunk 2869 (Number of characters: 77):

chunk 2870 (Number of characters: 220):

treat others like captive audiences, give them unsolicited performance evaluations, make

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2872 (Number of characters: 93):

chunk 2873 (Number of characters: 202):
Scapegoating
Scapegoating is an outer critic process whereby personal frustration is unfairly dumped onto
others. Scapegoating is typically fuelled by unworked through anger about childhood
abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2874 (Number of characters: 98):
Displacing anger on the wrong target however, fails to release or resolve old or

unrelated hurts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2875 (Number of characters: 63):
Scapegoating is often a reenactment of a parent’s abusive role.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2876 (Number of characters: 101):
It is blind imitation of a
parent who habitually released his frustration by indiscriminately raging.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2877 (Number of characters: 95):
When a fight type
parent scapegoats those around him, he enforces a perverse kind of mirroring.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2878 (Number of characters: 64):
He is making sure
that when he feels bad, so does everyone else.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 2879 (Number of characters: 88):
It is like a bumper sticker I saw the other day: “If
Momma ain’t happy, Nobody’s happy.”
