chunk 3749 (Number of characters: 366):
AUTHENTIC VULNERABILITY “Realationship” Makes Healthy
Relationship
Authentic vulnerability is a second quality of intimate relating. Authentic vulnerability often
begins with emotionally reverberating with the client. I have found that emotional reflection of
the client’s feelings is irreplaceable in fostering the development of trust and real relational
intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3750 (Number of characters: 145):
Emotional reflection requires the therapist to be emotionally vulnerable himself and reveal
that he too feels mad, sad, bad and scared sometimes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3751 (Number of characters: 159):
Modeling vulnerability, as with empathy,
demonstrates to the client the value of being vulnerable and encourages her to risk wading into
her own vulnerability.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3752 (Number of characters: 148):
I came to value therapeutic vulnerability the hard way via its absence in my own therapy
with a therapist who was of the old, “blank screen” school.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3753 (Number of characters: 122):
She was distant, laconic and over-
withholding in her commitment to the psychoanalytic principle of “optimal frustration.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3754 (Number of characters: 521):
Therapy
with her was actually counter-therapeutic and shame-exacerbating for me as we reenacted a
defective child/perfect parent dynamic. Therapeutic Emotional Disclosure
Thankfully, I eventually realized that I had unresolved attachment issues, and sought out a
Relational therapist who valued the use of her own vulnerable and emotionally authentic self as a
tool in therapy. Her tempered and timely emotional self-disclosures helped me to deconstruct the veneer of
invincibility I had built as a child to hide my pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3755 (Number of characters: 52):
Here are some examples that were especially
helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3756 (Number of characters: 33):
“God, the holidays can be awful.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3757 (Number of characters: 40):
“I get scared when I teach a class too.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3758 (Number of characters: 14):
“I’m so sorry.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3759 (Number of characters: 28):
I just missed what you said.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3760 (Number of characters: 84):
I got a little distracted by my anxiety about my dental appointment
this afternoon.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3761 (Number of characters: 111):
“I feel sad that your mother was so mean to you.” “It makes me angry that you
were so bullied by your parents.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3762 (Number of characters: 202):
My therapist’s modeling that anger, sadness, fear, and depression were emotions that could
be healthily expressed helped me to renounce the pain-repressing, emotional perfectionism in
which I was mired.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3763 (Number of characters: 75):
With her, I learned to stop burying my feelings in the hope of being loved.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3764 (Number of characters: 115):
I
renounced my just-get-over-it philosophy and embraced vulnerability as a way of finally getting

close to people.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3765 (Number of characters: 180):
I needed this kind of modeling, as so many of my clients have, to begin to emerge from my
fear of being attacked, shamed or abandoned for feeling bad and having dysphoric feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3766 (Number of characters: 188):
In
order to let go of my Sisyphean salvation fantasy of achieving constant happiness, I needed to
experience that all the less than shiny bits of me were acceptable to another human being.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3767 (Number of characters: 145):
Seeing
that she was comfortable with and accepting of her own unhappy feelings eventually convinced
me that she really was not disgusted by mine.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3768 (Number of characters: 255):
The therapist’s judicious use of emotional self-disclosure helps the client move out of the
slippery, shame-lined pit of emotional perfectionism. Here are some self-revealing things that I
say to encourage my clients to be more emotionally self-accepting.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3769 (Number of characters: 47):
“I feel really sad about what
happened to you.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3770 (Number of characters: 70):
“I feel really angry that you got stuck with such a god-awful family.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3771 (Number of characters: 381):
“When
I’m temporarily confused and don’t know what to say or do, I…” “When I’m having a shame
attack, I…” “When something triggers me into fear, I…” “When my inner critic is overreacting,
I remind myself of the Winnicottian concept that I only have to be a ‘good enough person.’”
Here are two examples of emotional self-disclosure that are fundamental tools of my
therapeutic work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3772 (Number of characters: 89):
I repeatedly express my genuine indignation that the survivor was taught to
hate himself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3773 (Number of characters: 96):
Over time, this often awakens the survivor’s instinct to also feel incensed about this
travesty.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3774 (Number of characters: 64):
This then empowers him to begin standing up to the inner critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3775 (Number of characters: 107):
This in turn aids him to
emotionally invest in the multidimensional work of building healthy self-advocacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3776 (Number of characters: 95):
Furthermore, I also repeatedly respond with empathy and compassion to the survivor’s
suffering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3777 (Number of characters: 84):
With time, this typically helps to awaken the recoveree’s capacity for self-empathy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3778 (Number of characters: 108):
She then gradually learns to comfort herself when she is in a flashback or otherwise painful life
situation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3779 (Number of characters: 116):
Less and less often does she surrender to an inner torture of self-hate, self-
disappointment, and self-abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3780 (Number of characters: 242):
My most consistent feedback from past clients is that responses like these - especially ones
that normalize fear and depression – helped them immeasurably to deconstruct their
perfectionism, and open up to self-compassion and self-acceptance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3781 (Number of characters: 285):
Guidelines For Self-disclosure
What guidelines, then, can we use to insure that our self-disclosure is judicious and therapeutic? I believe the following five principles help me to disclose therapeutically and steer clear of
unconsciously sharing for my own narcissistic gratification.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3782 (Number of characters: 145):
First, I use self-disclosure sparingly. Second, my disclosures are offered primarily to promote a matrix of safety and trust in the
relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3783 (Number of characters: 211):
In this vein my vulnerability is offered to normalize and de-shame the inexorable,
existential imperfection of the human condition, e.g., we all make mistakes, suffer painful
feelings, experience confusion, etc.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3784 (Number of characters: 78):
Third, I do not share vulnerabilities that are currently raw and unintegrated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3785 (Number of characters: 149):
Fourth, I never disclose in order to work through my own “stuff,” or to meet my own
narcissistic need for verbal ventilation or personal edification.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3786 (Number of characters: 153):
Fifth, while I may share my appreciation or be touched by a client’s attempt or offer to
focus on or soothe my vulnerabilities, I never accept the offer.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3787 (Number of characters: 143):
I gently thank them for their
concern, remind them that our work is client-centered, and let them know that I have an outside

support network.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3788 (Number of characters: 265):
Emotional Self-Disclosure And Sharing Parallel Trauma History Since many of my clients have sought my services after reading my somewhat autobiographical
book on recovery from the dysfunctional family, self-disclosure about my past trauma is
sometimes a moot point.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3789 (Number of characters: 136):
This condition has at the same time helped me realize how powerful
this kind of disclosure can be in healing shame and cultivating hope.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3790 (Number of characters: 213):
Over and over, clients have told me that my vulnerable and pragmatic stories of working
through my parents’ traumatizing abuse and neglect gives them the courage to engage the long
difficult journey of recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3791 (Number of characters: 188):
Now whether or not someone has read my book, I will – with appropriate clients -
judiciously and sparingly share my own experiences of dealing with an issue they have currently
brought up.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3792 (Number of characters: 108):
I do this both to psychoeducate them and to model ways that they might address their
own analogous concerns.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3793 (Number of characters: 60):
One common example sounds like this: “I hate flashbacks too.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3794 (Number of characters: 119):
Even though I get them
much less than when I started this work, falling back into that old fear and shame is so awful.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3795 (Number of characters: 121):
I also sometimes say: “I really reverberate with your feelings of hopelessness and
powerlessness around the inner critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3796 (Number of characters: 73):
In the early stages of this work, I often felt
overwhelmingly frustrated.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3797 (Number of characters: 58):
It seemed that trying to shrink it actually made it worse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3798 (Number of characters: 130):
But now
after ten thousand repetitions of thought-stopping and thought-correction, my critic is a mere
shadow of its former self.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3799 (Number of characters: 60):
A final example concerns a purely emotional self-disclosure.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3800 (Number of characters: 160):
When a client is verbally
ventilating about a sorrowful experience, I sometimes allow my tears to brim up in my eyes in
authentic commiseration with their pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3801 (Number of characters: 107):
The first time my most helpful therapist did this with
me, I experienced a quantum leap in my trust of her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3802 (Number of characters: 114):
3. DIALOGICALITY
Dialogicality occurs when two conversing people move fluidly and interchangeably between
speaking

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3803 (Number of characters: 83):
[an aspect of healthy narcissism] and listening [an aspect of healthy codependence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3804 (Number of characters: 1):
]

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3805 (Number of characters: 666):
Such reciprocal interactions prevent either person from polarizing to a dysfunctional narcissistic
or codependent type of relating
Dialogicality energizes both participants in a conversation. Dialogical relating stands in
contrast to the monological energy-theft that characterizes interactions whereby a narcissist
pathologically exploits a codependent’s listening defense. Numerous people have reverberated
with my observation that listening to a narcissist monologue feels as if it is draining them of
energy. I have become so mindful of this dynamic that, in a new social situation, a sudden sense of
tiredness often warns me that I am talking with a narcissist.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3806 (Number of characters: 107):
How different than the elevation I
sense in myself and my fellow conversant in a truly reciprocal exchange.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3807 (Number of characters: 61):
Again, I wonder if
there are mirror neurons involved in this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3808 (Number of characters: 174):
I was appalled the other day while perusing a home shopping catalog to see a set of coffee
cups for sale that bore the monikers “Designated Talker” and “Designated Listener”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3809 (Number of characters: 118):
My wife

and I pondered it for a few minutes, and hypothesized that it had to be a narcissist who designed
those mugs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3810 (Number of characters: 128):
We imagined we could see the narcissists who order them presenting them to their
favorite sounding boards as Christmas presents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3811 (Number of characters: 126):
In therapy, dialogicality develops out of a teamwork approach – a mutual brainstorming
about the client’s issues and concerns.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3812 (Number of characters: 100):
Such an approach cultivates full exploration of
ambivalences, conflicts and other life difficulties.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3813 (Number of characters: 95):
Dialogicality is enhanced when the therapist offers feedback from a take-it-or-leave-it
stance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3814 (Number of characters: 48):
Dialogicality also implies respectful mutuality.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3815 (Number of characters: 188):
It stands in stark contrast to the blank
screen neutrality and abstinence of traditional psychoanalytic therapy, which all too often
reenacts the verbal and emotional neglect of childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3816 (Number of characters: 206):
I believe abstinence commonly flashes the client back into feelings of abandonment, which
triggers them to retreat into “safe” superficial disclosure, ever-growing muteness and/or early
flight from therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3817 (Number of characters: 134):
Meeting Healthy Narcissistic Needs
All this being said, extensive dialogicality is often inappropriate in the early stages of therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3818 (Number of characters: 132):
This is especially true, when the client’s normal narcissistic needs have never been gratified, and
remain developmentally arrested.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3819 (Number of characters: 52):
In such cases, clients need to be extensively heard.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3820 (Number of characters: 135):
They need to discover through the
agency of spontaneous self-expression the nature of their own feelings, needs, preferences and
views.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3821 (Number of characters: 189):
For those survivors whose self-expression was especially decimated by their caretakers,
self-focused verbal exploration typically needs to be the dominant activity for a great deal of
time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3822 (Number of characters: 90):
Without this, the unformed healthy ego has no room to grow and break free from the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3823 (Number of characters: 100):
The client’s healthy sense of self remains imprisoned beneath the hegemony of the outsized
superego.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3824 (Number of characters: 224):
This does not mean, however, that the client benefits when the therapist retreats into
extremely polarized listening. Most benefit, as early as the first session, from hearing something
real or “personal” from the therapist.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3825 (Number of characters: 121):
This helps overcome the shame-inducing potential that
arises in the “One-seen [client] / One-unseen [therapist]” dynamic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3826 (Number of characters: 101):
When one person is being
vulnerable and the other is not, shame has a huge universe in which to grow.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3827 (Number of characters: 175):
This also creates a
potential for the client to get stuck flashing back to childhood when the vulnerable child was
rejected over and over by the seemingly invulnerable parent.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3828 (Number of characters: 217):
Consequently, many of my colleagues see group therapy as especially powerful for healing
shame, because it rectifies this imbalance by creating a milieu where it is not just one person who
is risking being vulnerable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3829 (Number of characters: 120):
In this regard, it is interesting to note a large survey of California therapists that occurred
about fifteen years ago.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3830 (Number of characters: 198):
The survey was about their therapy preferences, and upwards of ninety
percent emphasized that they did not want a blank screen therapist, but rather one who
occasionally offered opinions and advice.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3831 (Number of characters: 292):
For twenty-five years, I have been routinely asking clients in the first session: “Based on
your previous experiences in therapy, what would you like to happen in our work together; and
what don’t you want to happen?” How frequently clients respond similarly to the therapists in

the survey!

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3832 (Number of characters: 108):
Moreover, the next most common response I receive is that I don’t want a therapist who
does all the talking.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3833 (Number of characters: 80):
More than a few have used the exact phrase: “I couldn’t get a word in
edgewise!”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3834 (Number of characters: 187):
How I wish there was a way that our qualification tests could spot and disqualify the
narcissists who do get licensed and then turn their already codependent clients into sounding
boards.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3835 (Number of characters: 68):
This is the shadowy flipside polarity of the blank screen therapist.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3836 (Number of characters: 172):
Psychoeducation As Part Of Dialogicality
Experience has taught me that clients who are childhood trauma survivors typically benefit from
psychoeducation about Complex PTSD.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3837 (Number of characters: 144):
When clients understand the whole picture of Cptsd
recovery, they become more motivated to participate in the self-help practices of recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3838 (Number of characters: 96):
This also increases their overall hopefulness and general engagement in the therapeutic process.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3839 (Number of characters: 142):
I
sometimes wonder whether the rise in the popularity of Coaching has been a reaction to the
various traditional forms of therapeutic neglect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3840 (Number of characters: 145):
One of the worst forms of therapeutic neglect occurs when the therapist fails to notice or
challenge a client’s incessant, self-hating diatribes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3841 (Number of characters: 94):
This, I believe, is akin to tacitly approving of
and silently colluding with the inner critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3842 (Number of characters: 130):
Perhaps therapeutic withholding and abstinence derives from the absent father syndrome
that afflicts so many Westernized families.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3843 (Number of characters: 208):
Perhaps traditional psychotherapy overemphasizes
the mothering principles of listening and unconditional love, and neglects the fathering principles
of encouragement and guidance that coaching specializes in.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3844 (Number of characters: 93):
Too much coaching is, of course, as counter-therapeutic and unbalanced as too much
listening.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3845 (Number of characters: 101):
It can interfere with the client’s process of self-exploration and self-discovery as
described above.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3846 (Number of characters: 118):
At its worst, it can lure the therapist into the narcissistic trap of falling in love
with the sound of his own voice.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3847 (Number of characters: 59):
At its best, coaching is an indispensable therapeutic tool.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3848 (Number of characters: 182):
Just as it takes fathering and
mothering to raise a balanced child, mothering and fathering principles are needed to meet the
developmental arrests of the attachment-deprived client.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3849 (Number of characters: 149):
The sophisticated therapist values both and intuitively oscillates between the two,
depending on the developmental needs of the client in the moment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3850 (Number of characters: 241):
Sometimes we guide with
psychoeducation, therapeutic self-disclosure and active positive noticing, and most times we
receptively nurture the client’s evolving practice of her own spontaneously arising self-
expression and verbal ventilation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3851 (Number of characters: 133):
Once again, I believe that in early therapy and many subsequent stages of therapy, the latter
process typically needs to predominate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3852 (Number of characters: 125):
In this vein, I would guess that over the course of most
therapies that I conduct, I listen about ninety percent of the time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3853 (Number of characters: 158):
Finally, I often notice that the last phase of therapy is often characterized by increasing
dialogicality – a more balanced fluidity of talking and listening.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3854 (Number of characters: 76):
This conversational reciprocity
is a key characteristic of healthy intimacy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3855 (Number of characters: 144):
Moreover, when therapy is successful, progress in
mutuality begins to serve the client in creating healthier relationships in the outside world.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3856 (Number of characters: 149):
Dialogicality And The 4F’s

Because of childhood abandonment and repetition compulsion in later relationships, many 4F
types are “dying” to be heard.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3857 (Number of characters: 95):
Different types however vary considerably in their dialogical
needs over the course of therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3858 (Number of characters: 202):
The Fawn/ Codependent type, who survived in childhood by becoming a parent’s sounding
board or shoulder to cry on, may use her listening defense to encourage the therapist to do too
much of the talking.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3859 (Number of characters: 112):
With her eliciting defense, she may even invoke the careless therapist into
narcissistically monologing himself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3860 (Number of characters: 183):
The Freeze/Dissociative type, who learned early to seek safety in the camouflage of silence,
often needs a great deal of encouragement to discover and talk about his inner experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3861 (Number of characters: 126):
Psychoeducation can help him understand how his healthy narcissistic need to express himself
was never nurtured in his family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3862 (Number of characters: 150):
Furthermore, freeze types can easily get lost in superficial and barely relevant free
associations as they struggle to learn to talk about themselves.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3863 (Number of characters: 202):
This of course needs to be
welcomed for some time, but eventually we must help him see that his flights of fantasy or
endless dream elaborations are primarily manifestations of his dissociative defense.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3864 (Number of characters: 171):
Freeze types need to learn that emotionally disconnected talking is an old childhood habit
that was developed to keep them buoyant above their undealt with emotional pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3865 (Number of characters: 133):
Because of
this, we must repeatedly guide them toward their feelings so that they can learn to express their
most important concerns.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3866 (Number of characters: 139):
The Fight/Narcissistic type, who often enters therapy habituated to holding court, typically
dodges real intimacy with her talking defense.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3867 (Number of characters: 155):
Therapy can actually be counterproductive for
these types as months or years of uninterrupted monologing in sessions exacerbate their sense of
entitlement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3868 (Number of characters: 149):
By providing a steady diet of uninterrupted listening, the therapist strengthens their
intimacy-destroying defense of over-controlling conversations.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3869 (Number of characters: 104):
Sooner or later, we must insert
ourselves into the relationship to work on helping them learn to listen.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3870 (Number of characters: 205):
As I write this, I remember Harry from my internship whose tiny capacity to listen to his
wife evaporated as my fifty minutes of uninterrupted listening became his new norm and
expectation in relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3871 (Number of characters: 141):
I felt guilty when I learned this from listening to a recorded message
from his wife about how therapy was making him even more insufferable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3872 (Number of characters: 147):
I was relieved,
however, a few years later when a different client told me that Harry’s wife eventually felt happy
about this “therapeutic” change.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3873 (Number of characters: 125):
Her husband’s increased self-centeredness was the last straw for
her and she finally, with great relief, shed herself of him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3874 (Number of characters: 203):
A therapist, who is a fawn type herself, may hide in a listening and eliciting defense to avoid the
scary work of gradually insinuating herself into the relationship and nudging it towards
dialogicality.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3875 (Number of characters: 71):
If we do not nudge the client to interact, there will be no recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3876 (Number of characters: 73):
For more on
how to approach this, please see the end of the next section.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3877 (Number of characters: 98):
The Flight/Obsessive-compulsive type sometimes presents as being more dialogical than
other types.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3878 (Number of characters: 122):
Like the freeze type, however, he can obsess about “safe” abstract concerns that are
quite removed from his deeper issues.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3879 (Number of characters: 151):
It is therefore up to the therapist to steer him into his
deeper, emotionally based concerns to help him learn a more intimacy-enhancing dialogicality.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3880 (Number of characters: 190):
Otherwise, the flight type can remain stuck and floundering in obsessive perseverations about

superficial worries that are little more than left-brain dissociations from his repressed pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3881 (Number of characters: 148):
It is important to note here that all 4F types use left- or right-brain dissociative processes to
avoid feeling and grieving their childhood losses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3882 (Number of characters: 144):
As dialogicality is established, it can then be
oriented toward helping them to uncover and verbally and emotionally vent their ungrieved
hurts.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3883 (Number of characters: 159):
4. COLLABORATIVE RAPPORT REPAIR
Collaborative rapport repair is the process by which relationships recover and grow closer from
successful conflict resolution.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3884 (Number of characters: 94):
Misattunements and periods of disaffection are existential to every
relationship of substance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3885 (Number of characters: 133):
We all need to learn a process for restoring intimacy when a
disagreement temporarily disrupts our feeling of being safely connected.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3886 (Number of characters: 159):
I believe most people, if they think about it, realize that their best friends are those with
whom they have had a conflict and found a way to work through it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3887 (Number of characters: 144):
Once a friendship survives a
hurtful misattunement, it generally means that it has moved through the fair-weather-friends
stage of relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3888 (Number of characters: 107):
Synchronistic with re-editing this last section, my son uncharacteristically got into a conflict
at school.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3889 (Number of characters: 151):
During third grade recess two of his good friends, also uncharacteristically, started
teasing him, and when they would not stop he pushed each of them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3890 (Number of characters: 54):
This earned them all a trip to
the principal’s office.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3891 (Number of characters: 64):
The principal is a strict but exceptionally wise and kind woman.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3892 (Number of characters: 225):
My son’s
offense, using physical force to resolve a conflict, was judged as the most serious violation of
school policy, but his friends’ were also held responsible for their part and given an enlightening
lecture on teasing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3893 (Number of characters: 66):
My son, not used to being in trouble, had a good cry about it all.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3894 (Number of characters: 115):
He then agreed that a one
day loss of recess plus writing letters of apology to his friends were fair consequences.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3895 (Number of characters: 86):
Two days
later, I asked him how things were going now between him and the two friends.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3896 (Number of characters: 75):
With a look of
surprise and delight, he told me: “It’s really funny, daddy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3897 (Number of characters: 66):
Now, it feels like we’re even better
friends than we were before.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3898 (Number of characters: 105):
Rapport repair is probably the most transformative, intimacy-building process that a therapist can
model.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3899 (Number of characters: 133):
I guide this process from a perspective that recognizes that there is usually a mutual
contribution to any misattunement or conflict.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3900 (Number of characters: 90):
Therefore, a mutually respectful dialogical process
is typically needed to repair rapport.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3901 (Number of characters: 96):
Exceptions to this include scapegoating and upsets that are
instigated by a bullying narcissist.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3902 (Number of characters: 46):
In those situations, they are solely at fault.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3903 (Number of characters: 131):
I have often been
saddened by codependent clients who apologize to their bullying parents as if they made their
parents abuse them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3904 (Number of characters: 101):
In more normal misattunements, I often initiate the repair process with two contiguous
interventions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3905 (Number of characters: 87):
Firstly, I identify the misattunement [e.g., “I think I might have misunderstood
you.”]

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3906 (Number of characters: 114):
And secondly, I then model vulnerability by describing what I think might be my
contribution to the disconnection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3907 (Number of characters: 155):
Abbreviated examples of this are: “I think I may have just been somewhat preachy…or
tired…or inattentive…or impatient…or triggered by my own transference.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3908 (Number of characters: 119):
Owning your part in

a conflict validates the normality of relational disappointment and the art of amiable resolution.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3909 (Number of characters: 155):
Taking responsibility for your role in a misunderstanding also helps to deconstruct the
client’s outer critic belief that relationships have to be perfect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3910 (Number of characters: 178):
At the same time, it models a
constructive approach to resolving conflicts, and over time leads most clients to become
interested in exploring their contribution to the conflict.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3911 (Number of characters: 91):
This becomes an invaluable skill which
they can then take into their outside relationships.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3912 (Number of characters: 133):
As one might expect, fight types are the least likely of the 4F’s to collaborate and own their
side of the street in a misattunement.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3913 (Number of characters: 167):
Extreme fight types such as those diagnosed with
Narcissistic Personality Disorder have long been considered untreatable in traditional
psychoanalysis for this reason.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3914 (Number of characters: 123):
With less extreme fight types, I sometimes succeed in psycho-educating them on how they
learned their controlling defenses.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3915 (Number of characters: 77):
From there I try to help them see how much they pay for being
so controlling.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3916 (Number of characters: 56):
At the top of the list of debits is intimacy-starvation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3917 (Number of characters: 101):
Consciously or not, they
hunger for human warmth and they do not get it from those whom they control.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3918 (Number of characters: 102):
Victims of fight
types are too afraid of them to relax enough to generate authentically warm feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3919 (Number of characters: 193):
Finally, I believe one of the most common reasons that clients terminate prematurely is the
gradual accumulation of dissatisfactions that they do not feel safe enough to bring up or talk
about.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3920 (Number of characters: 160):
How sad it is that all kinds of promising relationships wither and die from an individual or
couple’s inability to safely work through differences and conflict.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3921 (Number of characters: 103):
Please see Toolbox 4 in
chapter 13 for a list of many pragmatic tools to “Lovingly Resolving Conflict.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3922 (Number of characters: 142):
Moving Through Abandonment Into Intimacy: A Case Study
A sweet, freeze-fawn client of mine suffered severe emotional abandonment in childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3923 (Number of characters: 34):
Both
his parents were workaholics.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3924 (Number of characters: 50):
They were, by definition, exceedingly unavailable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3925 (Number of characters: 139):
As the
youngest of five children, Frank always finished last in the sibling competition for the paltry
caretaking his parents had to offer.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3926 (Number of characters: 96):
His adulthood was unfortunately a reenactment of the
relational impoverishment of his childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3927 (Number of characters: 66):
Childhood trauma left Frank hair-triggered to retreat and isolate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3928 (Number of characters: 50):
He had never experienced
an enduring relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3929 (Number of characters: 92):
As a result of our long-term work, however, he became more motivated
to seek a relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3930 (Number of characters: 54):
He successfully dated a healthy and available partner.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3931 (Number of characters: 116):
For the first six
months of their relationship, my coaching and her kind nature enabled him to show more of
himself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3932 (Number of characters: 89):
He was rewarded by increasing feelings of relaxation and comfort while relating with
her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3933 (Number of characters: 119):
When he accepted her request to move in together, however, it became harder to hide his
recurring emotional flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3934 (Number of characters: 129):
He was more convinced than ever that his feelings of fear, shame
and depression were the most despicable of his many fatal flaws.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3935 (Number of characters: 158):
As we worked with this belief in therapy, he remembered many times when even the
mildest dip in his mood triggered his mother to retreat into her home office.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3936 (Number of characters: 139):
He saw that the only
times his mother had a bit of time for him was on those rare occasions when he was buoyant
enough to lift her spirits.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3937 (Number of characters: 91):
He had a staunch conviction that social inclusion depended on him

generating cheerfulness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3938 (Number of characters: 67):
Gloomy and abashed, he confessed: “That’s pretty hard for me, Pete.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3939 (Number of characters: 31):
I’m not much fun to be around.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3940 (Number of characters: 99):
A codependent defense of being perpetually pleasant and agreeable had been deeply
instilled in him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3941 (Number of characters: 117):
He could not shake off the fear that if he was not upbeat enough, his new partner

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3942 (Number of characters: 54):
He reported that his flashbacks at home had increased.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3943 (Number of characters: 55):
Sometimes he felt a desperate need to isolate and hide.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3944 (Number of characters: 98):
His freeze response was so activated, that
he increasingly withdrew from his partner into silence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3945 (Number of characters: 134):
He knew that he was hiding too much in
computer activities, excessive sleeping, and marathon TV sports viewing, but he could not stop.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3946 (Number of characters: 132):
During his most intense flashbacks, his fear and self-disgust became so intense that he
invented any excuse to get out of the house.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3947 (Number of characters: 64):
He was besieged by thoughts and fantasies of being
single again.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3948 (Number of characters: 34):
His critic was winning the battle.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3949 (Number of characters: 80):
He was sure his partner was as disgusted with his
affect as his mother had been.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3950 (Number of characters: 49):
He was on the verge of a literal flight response.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3951 (Number of characters: 114):
He was about to
leave, as he had before when the brief infatuation stages of his few previous relationships ended.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3952 (Number of characters: 98):
We spent many subsequent sessions managing these emotional flashbacks to his original
abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3953 (Number of characters: 94):
He understood more deeply that his silent withdrawals were evidence that he was
flashing back.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3954 (Number of characters: 92):
He then committed to rereading and using the 13 steps of flashback management
at such times.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3955 (Number of characters: 112):
With my encouragement and gentle nudging, he grieved over his original abandonment
more deeply than ever before.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3956 (Number of characters: 84):
Over and over, he confronted the critic’s projection of his mother
onto his partner.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3957 (Number of characters: 76):
At the same time, I encouraged Frank to be more vulnerable with his partner.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3958 (Number of characters: 46):
He practiced
doing this in role-plays with me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3959 (Number of characters: 80):
Encouraged by all this work, he began talking to his girlfriend
about his Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3960 (Number of characters: 63):
A good-hearted person, she responded with sympathy and support.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3961 (Number of characters: 106):
This
eventually helped him to disclose that talking vulnerably made him feel even more afraid and
ashamed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3962 (Number of characters: 194):
To his great relief, she was not only empathic but grateful for his vulnerability. She
told him that his vulnerability made her feel safer to share an even deeper level of her own
vulnerability.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3963 (Number of characters: 56):
He cried poignant tears of gratitude as he told me this.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3964 (Number of characters: 60):
I commiserated with a
welling of sweet tears in my own eyes.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3965 (Number of characters: 155):
Frank’s crowning achievement came some months later when he finally felt brave enough
to tell her what he was experiencing while he was actually depressed.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3966 (Number of characters: 206):
This breakthrough further
enriched their intimacy. Their love expanded into those special depths of intimacy that are only
achieved when people feel safe enough to communicate about anything and everything.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3967 (Number of characters: 139):
As my client became more skilled at being vulnerable, he was rewarded with the
irreplaceable intimacy that comes from mutual commiseration.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3968 (Number of characters: 150):
Over the next year, he and his
future wife became such reliable sources of verbal ventilation for each other, that Frank no
longer needed my services.

chunk 3969 (Number of characters: 173):
Earned Secure Attachment
In therapy, clients get the most out of their session by learning to stay in interpersonal contact
while they communicate from their emotional pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3970 (Number of characters: 115):
This gradually shows them that they are
acceptable and worthwhile no matter what they are feeling and experiencing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3971 (Number of characters: 137):
As survivors realize more deeply that their flashbacks are normal responses to abnormal
childhood conditions, their shame begins to melt.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3972 (Number of characters: 55):
This then eases their fear of being seen as

defective.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3973 (Number of characters: 85):
In turn, their habits of isolating or pushing others away during flashbacks diminish.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3974 (Number of characters: 78):
Earned secure attachment is a newly recognized category of healthy attachment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3975 (Number of characters: 128):
Many
attachment therapists believe that effective treatment can help a survivor “earn” at least one truly
intimate relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3976 (Number of characters: 205):
Earned secure attachment is the good enough and intimacy-rich attachment
discussed throughout this book. I believe the principles outlined in this chapter are keys to achieving an earned secure
attachment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3977 (Number of characters: 68):
In this vein, good therapy can be an intimacy-modeling relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3978 (Number of characters: 66):
It fosters our
leaning and practicing of intimacy-making behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3979 (Number of characters: 178):
Your connection with your therapist can
become a transitional earned secure attachment. This in turn can lead to the attainment of an
earned secure attachment outside of therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3980 (Number of characters: 163):
I have repeatedly seen this result with my most
successful clients, and I am grateful to report that my last experience with my own therapy lead
me to this reward.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3981 (Number of characters: 99):
Rescuing The Survivor From The Critic
I will conclude this section with a final note to therapists.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3982 (Number of characters: 366):
The term rescuing and what it
represents has become taboo in many psychotherapy circles and in the 12-Step Movement (e.g.
AA, CODA and ACA). The word “rescuing” is often used in such an all-or-none way that any
type of active helping is pathologized. However, I believe that helping survivors out of the abyss
of emotional flashbacks is a necessary form of rescuing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3983 (Number of characters: 71):
A key place to practice healthy rescuing is in the realm of the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3984 (Number of characters: 137):
I believe there is an
unmet childhood need for rescue that I help meet when I “save” my client from the critic, the
proxy of her parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3985 (Number of characters: 28):
This is the need no one met.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3986 (Number of characters: 219):
The child was not rescued from her
traumatizing parent. This was terrible neglect on the part of the other parent, the relatives, the
neighbors or teachers who ignored the signs that she was withering from being abused.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3987 (Number of characters: 141):
Decades of trauma work have taken me to a place where my heart no longer allows me to
be silent when someone’s inner critic is on the attack.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3988 (Number of characters: 53):
Silence, in my mind, is equivalent to tacit
approval.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3989 (Number of characters: 117):
I can no longer sit quietly and not intervene when survivors abuse themselves with
their parents’ internalized voice.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3990 (Number of characters: 149):
I am additionally motivated to challenge the client’s toxic critic because of the failure of my
first long-term experience of psychoanalytic therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3991 (Number of characters: 106):
My “blank screen” therapist let me
flounder endlessly in attacking myself with self-hate and self-disgust.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3992 (Number of characters: 87):
Never once did she point
out that I could and should challenge this anti-self behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3993 (Number of characters: 110):
UCSF trauma expert Harvey Peskin
would call this a failure to bear witness to the traumatization of the child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3994 (Number of characters: 175):
I now vocally challenge the critic’s lies and slanders, and I try to give the survivor a hand to
climb out of the abyss of fear and shame into which the critic has pushed him.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3995 (Number of characters: 116):
It took me some time to break through the dysfunctional guilt that my early training
instilled in me about rescuing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3996 (Number of characters: 148):
Now, ironically, when I feel guilty, it is sometimes because I have
regressed and let the inner critic get away with abusing my friend or my client.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3997 (Number of characters: 54):
This guilt is
actually healthy emotional intelligence.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3998 (Number of characters: 72):
It comes from my empathy as a right action-call to
challenge the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 3999 (Number of characters: 147):
At such times, I feel derelict in my human and professional duty if I do not

bring attention to how he is hoisting himself on his parents’ petard.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4000 (Number of characters: 173):
Gratefully, I can no longer passively collude with the internalized critical parent by failing
to actively notice it like all those other adults did while he was growing up.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4001 (Number of characters: 135):
If an adult does not
protest when a child is being attacked with destructive criticism, she is in an unspoken alliance
with the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4002 (Number of characters: 64):
The child is forced to assume contempt is normal and acceptable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4003 (Number of characters: 125):
The witnessing
adult has forsaken her/his tribal responsibility to protect the child from parents who perpetrate
child abuse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4004 (Number of characters: 159):
When I label the traumatizing behavior of the client’s parents as contemptible, I begin the
awakening of his developmentally arrested need for self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4005 (Number of characters: 118):
I model to him that he
should have been protected, and that he can now resist mimicking their abuse in his own psyche.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4006 (Number of characters: 172):
With most of my clients, this eventually encourages disidentification from the aggressor and
weakens the internalization of the attacking parent as the locus of the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4007 (Number of characters: 164):
In my own case, I felt loved by my grandmother who lived with my family, but she failed to
help me see that my parents’ vitriolic rages were wrong and not my fault.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4008 (Number of characters: 93):
In retrospect, I believe
that her neglect crystallized my belief that I deserved their abuse.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4009 (Number of characters: 73):
The stage was then set for me
to morph their contempt into self-loathing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4010 (Number of characters: 52):
I did this chapter and verse for nearly two decades.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4011 (Number of characters: 155):
I have also noticed a significant difference in survivors who were helped in childhood to see that
it was not their fault that they were being traumatized.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4012 (Number of characters: 155):
When there was one witnessing adult who
sufficiently decried what was being done to them, most did not develop such a ferocious, self-
annihilating critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4013 (Number of characters: 110):
Typically this was the other parent, an enlightened older sibling, a relative, a
teacher or a kindly neighbor.

chunk 4014 (Number of characters: 188):
FINDING A THERAPIST
I have as yet to do any therapist trainings in my approach outside of the San Francisco Bay Area,
so I cannot make any recommendations for therapists outside this area.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4015 (Number of characters: 196):
However, because my
approach is compatible with that of John Bradshaw’s, I refer people to a website that lists
therapists around the U. S. and the World who report that they embrace his approach.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4016 (Number of characters: 56):
The link to
this is www.creativegrowth.com/referral.htm.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4017 (Number of characters: 141):
I and the Creative Growth Center are however unable to personally endorse these therapists
as we are not personally familiar with their work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4018 (Number of characters: 51):
Nonetheless, I think this is a good place to
start.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4019 (Number of characters: 725):
Please begin by first reading the following recommendations for interviewing a therapist. The purpose of the interview is to ascertain whether your potential therapist is able and
willing to work at the levels I describe above. I recommend interviewing and having a trial
appointment with at least three therapists, if possible, to determine if their approach is
compatible enough with the one I describe above. A suitable therapist will be happy to answer your question about their approach and
generally talk with you on the phone for at least five minutes before scheduling a meeting. Should the therapist respond to you in an aloof, critical or shaming way, I would immediately

cross them off your list and keep looking.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4020 (Number of characters: 232):
Finally, it is important to note that there are many untherapized therapists who are licensed
to practice psychotherapy, and my experience is that these types are rarely able to work at the
depth required for guiding Cptsd recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4021 (Number of characters: 94):
I believe it’s appropriate to ask a prospective therapist if they have done their own therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4022 (Number of characters: 94):
I would then at least expect from him/her a response that they have and have found it helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4023 (Number of characters: 109):
Ideally, the therapist would also be willing to disclose that they have done their own family of
origin work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4024 (Number of characters: 207):

right therapist.”

chances of finding a “good enough” therapist are good.

chunk 4041 (Number of characters: 334):
An important guideline for finding a safe enough online or in-person group: If you find that a
leader or member is over-dominating a group through narcissistic behaviors such as monologing,
monopolizing the time, pressuring anyone with unwanted advice or shaming anyone in anyway,
please allow yourself to leave and try another group.
