chunk 4042 (Number of characters: 473):
CO-COUNSELING
If you are not able to find or afford a “good enough” therapist, and/or if you want to supplement
your current therapy as my wife and I do regularly with each other, you can look for a safe
partner who is willing to work with you to mutually evolve a co-counseling relationship. There are many forms of co-counseling. {Google “co-counseling” to learn more.} My wife and I have a simple structure for establishing a safe and healing co-counseling
relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4043 (Number of characters: 78):
We have been using this model for many years and derive great benefit from it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4044 (Number of characters: 86):
I
have similarly benefitted from co-counseling with two wonderful friends in the past.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4045 (Number of characters: 91):
Please feel
free, of course to adapt the model to fit your own mutual needs and agreements.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4046 (Number of characters: 50):
Meet weekly and exchange 30 or 60 minute sessions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4047 (Number of characters: 163):
Begin with the counselee talking about all and any of his/her concerns and with the
counselor refraining from intervening other than to practice, Active Listening.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4048 (Number of characters: 76):
Active listening is based on an attitude of “unconditional positive regard”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4049 (Number of characters: 200):
It enhances the
counselee’s process of full verbal ventilation, and it uses non-directive, non-intrusive verbal
feedback to let the counselee know that you are attuned and paying attention to him/her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4050 (Number of characters: 108):
Active listening includes responses like “un hunh” and “mmm-hmmm” as well as a
technique known as mirroring.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4051 (Number of characters: 210):
Mirroring occurs when we repeat key words or phrases that the
other person says to let them know that we are paying attention to them. Advanced mirroring occurs when we paraphrase in our own words what we hear.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4052 (Number of characters: 84):
This is
only helpful however if we make an accurate translation of what’s been said.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4053 (Number of characters: 96):
Finally, the use of open-ended questions is perhaps the penultimate active listening
techniques.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4054 (Number of characters: 155):
Questions such as “Can you tell me more about that?”, “What else happened?”, and
“Do you have other thoughts and feelings about that?” can be very helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4055 (Number of characters: 122):
Opened ended questions stand in contrast to pointed questions which tend to limit or shape
the way the counselee responds.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4056 (Number of characters: 192):
“What do you think or feel about that?” allows the other person
greater internal exploration than “Did you feel upset about that?” which may be perceived as a
statement rather than a question.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4057 (Number of characters: 67):
It can sound like you are telling them what they should be
feeling.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4058 (Number of characters: 64):
People vary in the amount of active listening they find helpful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4059 (Number of characters: 98):
Please be open to giving and
receiving feedback about how much you or the other person would like.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4060 (Number of characters: 172):
In order to establish safety and build trust, begin with a commitment to refrain from advice

giving, criticism or any kind of unsolicited feedback except active listening.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4061 (Number of characters: 127):
If and when the
desire for feedback comes up, it is best to let the counselee determine when, what kind and how
much they want.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4062 (Number of characters: 118):
Feedback is best given from a take-it or leave-it perspective
Do not give any feedback unless it is clearly asked for.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4063 (Number of characters: 369):
The counselee often does well to be
specific about the type of feedback desired, or the desire to not have any feedback; e.g., “I’d like
to just verbally ventilate about my relationship, but don’t really want any feedback about it other
than active listening.” At another point the counselee might like to say: “This is something I
would actually like some feedback on.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4064 (Number of characters: 71):
I’d like to know whether it seems that I’m perceiving my
boss clearly.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4065 (Number of characters: 209):
With enough grace, luck, respect, practice and compassion, mutual trust may eventually
come so far that you both agree to change the structure to allow for spontaneous feedback at
certain times in the session.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4066 (Number of characters: 153):
Don’t rush to get there, and always reserve permission to invoke the
no-feedback guideline for any given issue, session or indefinite number of sessions.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4067 (Number of characters: 98):
In this vein, my wife or I might say to each other: “I think I’d just like active listening
today.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4068 (Number of characters: 128):
I’d like to just extensively free associate on and explore this anxious feeling in my chest
without getting any input about it.”

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4069 (Number of characters: 37):
Practice therapeutic confidentiality.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4070 (Number of characters: 50):
Let what is said in a session stay in the session.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4071 (Number of characters: 185):
I also recommend that both partners read Toolbox 4 in chapter 13, and the section above on
the four key qualities of relational healing prior to commencing a co-counseling relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4072 (Number of characters: 131):
FORGIVENESS: BEGIN WITH THE SELF
This chapter is a reworking of an article of mine that was published in Recovering, November
1991.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4073 (Number of characters: 106):
I wrote it because I was appalled at how much pressure my clients were getting to just
forgive and forget.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4074 (Number of characters: 115):
Consequently, many of them were diving right back into denial, and
minimizing all the trauma that they had endured.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4075 (Number of characters: 115):
Their recovery processes then, screeched to a
halt as their inner critics denigrated them for being so unforgiving.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4076 (Number of characters: 227):
Because this article was helpful to my clients and because I received so much positive
feedback from the recovery community, I was motivated to write my first book, The Tao of Fully
Feeling, Harvesting Forgiveness Out of Blame.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4077 (Number of characters: 87):
This book explores the complex subject of
forgiving past abusers in considerable depth.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4078 (Number of characters: 99):
In this vein, it asserts that some parents were so
destructive to us, that they are not forgivable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4079 (Number of characters: 152):
There is a lot of shaming, dangerous and inaccurate “guidance” put out about forgiveness in both
the recovery community and in many spiritual teachings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4080 (Number of characters: 455):
Many survivors of dysfunctional
families have been injured by the simplistic, black-and-white advice that they must embrace a
position of being totally and permanently forgiving in order to recover. Unfortunately, those who take the advice to forgive abuses that they have not fully grieved,
abuses that are still occurring, and/or abuses so heinous they should and could never be forgiven,
often find themselves getting nowhere in their recovery process.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4081 (Number of characters: 224):
In fact, the possibility of attaining real feelings of forgiveness is usually lost when there is a
premature, cognitive decision to forgive. This is because premature forgiveness mimics the
defenses of denial and repression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4082 (Number of characters: 88):
It keeps unprocessed feelings of anger and hurt about
childhood trauma out of awareness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4083 (Number of characters: 62):
Real forgiveness is quite distinct from premature forgiveness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4084 (Number of characters: 163):
It is almost always a byproduct of
effective grieving and no amount of thought, intention or belief can bring it into being without a
great deal of emotional work.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4085 (Number of characters: 674):
Conversely, belief systems that are not open to the possibility of forgiveness sometimes
block our access to forgiving feelings, even when such feelings are present. It might be that the healthiest cognitive position concerning forgiveness is an attitude that
allows for the possibility of its occurrence on the other side of extensive grieving. This attitude
works best if it includes the condition that feelings of forgiveness will not be forced or falsely
invoked to cover up any unresolved feelings of hurt or anger. In this vein, it is crucial to understand that certain types of abuse are so extreme and
damaging to the victim that forgiveness is simply not an option.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4086 (Number of characters: 107):
Examples of this include
sociopathy, conscious cruelty, and many forms of scapegoating and parental incest.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4087 (Number of characters: 256):
When forgiveness has substance, it is felt palpably in the heart, and is usually an expansion of
the emotion of compassion. Compassion is certainly not always the same thing as forgiveness,
but it is usually the experience within which forgiveness is born.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4088 (Number of characters: 251):
Often this happens via an
intermediate process, where having grieved our childhood losses substantially, we occasionally
find ourselves considering the extenuating circumstances that contributed to our parents raising
us in neglectful or abusive ways.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4089 (Number of characters: 72):
Most commonly these extenuating circumstances revolve around two issues.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4090 (Number of characters: 102):
First, our
parents often parented us in ways that blindly replicated the ways that they were parented.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4091 (Number of characters: 117):
And
second, they were often supported in their dysfunctional parenting by the social norms and
values of their times.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4092 (Number of characters: 229):
Nonetheless, it is once again vitally important that we do not jump into considering their
mitigating circumstances until we have significantly worked through the traumatic consequences
that their abuse and abandonment had on us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4093 (Number of characters: 207):
When considering our parents extenuating circumstances, we may sometimes “get” that our
parents were also quite victimized, and we may consequently find ourselves on occasion feeling
sorry (sorrow) for them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4094 (Number of characters: 155):
Sometimes this experience of feeling compassion for them becomes profound enough for us
to comprehend how similarly awful and unfair their childhoods were.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4095 (Number of characters: 92):
This feeling-based
realization may on occasion morph into feeling some forgiveness for them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4096 (Number of characters: 147):
However, unless this feeling of forgiveness for our parents is grounded in compassion for
ourselves, the above process is an empty mental exercise.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4097 (Number of characters: 100):
Even worse, it may become a great
hindrance to doing the fundamental angering work of real recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4098 (Number of characters: 154):
Premature forgiveness will prohibit us from showing the inner child that she had the right to
be angry about her parents’ cold-hearted abandonment of her.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4099 (Number of characters: 81):
It will stop us from helping her to
express and release those old angry feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4100 (Number of characters: 113):
Premature forgiveness will also inhibit the survivor from reconnecting with his instinctual

self-protectiveness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4101 (Number of characters: 95):
He may never learn that he can now use his anger, if necessary, to stop
present day unfairness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4102 (Number of characters: 88):
As real forgiveness is primarily a feeling, it is - like all other feelings - ephemeral.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4103 (Number of characters: 61):
It is
never complete, never permanent, and never a done deal.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4104 (Number of characters: 78):
Forgiveness is governed by the dynamic nature of all human feeling experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4105 (Number of characters: 103):
Our
emotional experience is a frequently changing, unchoosable and unpredictable process of the
psyche.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4106 (Number of characters: 71):
No emotional state can be induced to persist as a permanent experience.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4107 (Number of characters: 263):
As sad as this may
be, as much as we might like to deny it, as much as it continuingly frustrates us, and as much as
we are pressured to control and pick our emotions, they are still by definition of the human
condition, largely outside the province of our wills.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4108 (Number of characters: 210):
Forgiveness then, like love, remains a human feeling experience that is only temporarily ours. However, when we thoroughly vent our angry feelings about the past, feelings of forgiveness
become more accessible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4109 (Number of characters: 257):
When we learn how to grieve ourselves out of abandonment
flashbacks, we reemerge into a feeling of belonging to and loving the world. Moreover, when we learn to effectively grieve through present day hurts, we quite naturally
move back into loving feelings.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4110 (Number of characters: 142):
As our emotional flexibility matures, lost feelings of love and
forgiveness return so reliably that they can become consciously chosen values.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4111 (Number of characters: 274):
Thus, when I occasionally feel hurt by proven intimates, I may not be able to immediately
invoke loving or forgiving feelings towards them, but I know that with sufficient communication
and non-abusive venting, I will eventually return to an appreciative experience of them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4112 (Number of characters: 159):
As much as I can forgive myself, that much can I forgive others. What I often forgive in others is
an old pain of mine, released from the disgust of self-hate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4113 (Number of characters: 94):
It is an old vulnerability of mine that I
now love and welcome like a bird with a broken wing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4114 (Number of characters: 102):
Shame and self-hate did not start with me,
but with all my heart, I deign that they will stop with me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4115 (Number of characters: 56):
I will do unto myself as I would have
others do unto me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4116 (Number of characters: 104):
Carol Ruth Knox wrote a poem about loving feelings and the hide-and-seek game they seem to
play with us.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4117 (Number of characters: 30):
It comes and goes, doesn’t it?

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4118 (Number of characters: 226):
Sometimes related
to people and how they
treat us, and sometimes not
Sometimes related
to the moon

to personal finances
to the questions of life
to nothingness
to everything
to the seasons, the time
to the food we ate
to. . .

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4119 (Number of characters: 1):
.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4120 (Number of characters: 188):
It would appear as if the art of loving is not whether you love or not (we all do in our

BIBLIOTHERAPY AND THE COMMUNITY OF BOOKS
Bibliotherapy is a term that describes the very real process of being positively and
therapeutically influenced by what you read. As stated earlier, when it is at its most powerful,
bibliotherapy is also relationally healing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4129 (Number of characters: 83):
It can rescue you from the common Cptsd feeling of
abject isolation and alienation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4130 (Number of characters: 73):
Bibliotherapy can play an enormous role in enhancing recovery from Cptsd.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4131 (Number of characters: 164):
I usually find
that my clients who make the most progress are those who augment their therapy sessions with
reading homework [self-prescribed or recommended by me].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4132 (Number of characters: 152):
This is especially true of those who further augment their reading with journaling about
their cognitive and emotional responses to what they have read.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4133 (Number of characters: 169):
I believe that journaling helps
build the new physiological and neuronal brain circuitry that occurs as we effectively meet our
developmentally arrested childhood needs.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4134 (Number of characters: 99):
[For more on Journaltherapy, read the section on
verbal ventilating in chapter 5 of my first book].

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4135 (Number of characters: 179):
Bibliotherapy is especially helpful for people like me who grew up in dangerous social
environments replete with adults who offered little but criticism, intimidation and disgust.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4136 (Number of characters: 117):
It
equally serves those whose early lives were devoid of adults who could be looked to for safe
support and guidance.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4137 (Number of characters: 193):
It was not until later in life, after I had quite a few years of group and individual therapy,
that I realized that my journey of recovering had actually begun decades before my formal
therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4138 (Number of characters: 88):
It began with all the therapeutic reading and writing I had instinctively gravitated to.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4139 (Number of characters: 130):
I
unconsciously sought the help of others in the many spiritual and psychological self-help books
that I was intuitively drawn to.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4140 (Number of characters: 117):
Without really understanding it, I gained valuable insights about how to improve the way I
treated myself and others.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4141 (Number of characters: 200):
Just as importantly, I subliminally realized that there were a number of
good, safe, wise and helpful adults out there who could be trusted and who had a great deal of
wise and kind guidance to offer.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4142 (Number of characters: 83):
I remember my first deeply emotional experience of entering the community of books.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4143 (Number of characters: 130):
I was
in the library resentfully slogging through the poetry section trying to find a book for my
homework in high school English.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4144 (Number of characters: 161):
I was up to “W “and had found nothing that remotely interested me when I came to an
anthology with the picture of a very compelling looking old man on its cover.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4145 (Number of characters: 13):
Walt Whitman!

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4146 (Number of characters: 88):
His epic poems Song of Myself and Song of the Open Road thrilled me and changed my life.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4147 (Number of characters: 101):
He
became my hero and the first adult role model that had something useful and important to teach
me.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4148 (Number of characters: 114):
His ideas became my raison d’être and gave me a hopeful plan for what I would do when I
finally escaped my family.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4149 (Number of characters: 161):
Over time the authors in my community of books seemed like a small tribe of elders who I
imagined as people who would have empathy for me if I were to meet them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4150 (Number of characters: 138):
Eventually when I
achieved something of a critical mass of this awareness, I managed to take a frightening leap into
the water of therapy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4151 (Number of characters: 115):
I lucked out and got a good enough therapist to help me take steps in my
healing that I could not manage on my own.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4152 (Number of characters: 96):
So here are some authors [and their works] who have been especially helpful to me on my
journey.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4153 (Number of characters: 61):
These are the wise aunts and uncles I never biologically had.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4154 (Number of characters: 176):
ESPECIALLY RECOMMENDED READING
Alice Miller
The Drama of The Gifted Child {Great book for overcoming denial
and understanding the profound impact of growing up poorly parented.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4155 (Number of characters: 110):
Very relevant for fawn types.}
Gravitz & Bowden
Guide to Recovery {Great short, powerful overview of recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4156 (Number of characters: 103):
Oriented to recovering from having alcoholic parents, but very relevant
to having traumatizing parents.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4157 (Number of characters: 270):
Read this if you can only read one book.}
L. Davis & E. Bass
The Courage to Heal {Classic on recovering from sexual abuse.}
Jack Kornfield
A Path with Heart {Using meditation to increase self-compassion.}
Steven Levine
Who Dies {Mindfulness and radical self-acceptance.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4158 (Number of characters: 206):
Sue Johnson
Hold Me Tight {The book, and especially the DVD of the same name,
shows how she teaches real couples to use their emotional vulnerability
to develop real intimacy and a healthy attachment bond.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4159 (Number of characters: 565):
John Bradshaw
Healing The Shame That Binds {Brilliant book on recovering from
toxic shame and growing up in a dysfunctional family.}
Judith Herman
Trauma and Recovery {The book in which Herman coins the term
Complex PTSD. Last half of book more relevant to recovery.}
Susan Anderson
The Journey from Abandonment to Healing {Oriented toward
recovering from divorce, but remarkably relevant to Cptsd recovery.}
J. Middleton-Moz
Children of Trauma {Excellent overall book on recovery.}
Beverly Engel
Healing Your Emotional Self {Advocates angering-at-the-critic work.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4160 (Number of characters: 78):
Theodore Rubin
Compassion and Self-hate {Wonderful appeal to self-compassion.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4161 (Number of characters: 69):
Susan Forward
Betrayal of Innocence { Good overall book on recovery.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4162 (Number of characters: 113):
Byron Brown
Soul Without Shame {Inner critic shrinking with angering-at-the- critic
and Mindfulness perspective.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4163 (Number of characters: 155):
Susan Vaughan
The Talking Cure {How Therapy and Relational Healing works with
very accessible neuroscientific evidence and an enlightened view of
therapy.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4164 (Number of characters: 125):
Lewis & Amini
A General Theory Of Love {Accessible poetic and scientific argument
on the human need for love and attachment.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4165 (Number of characters: 115):
Pat Love
The Emotional Incest Syndrome {Great book to heal from
codependent entrapment with a narcissistic mother.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4166 (Number of characters: 70):
Robin Norwood
Women Who Love Too Much {Early classic on Codependence.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4167 (Number of characters: 133):
Gay Hendricks 
Lucia Capacchione  
Learning to Love Yourself Recovery of your Inner Child {Great book
on Journaltherapy.}
Cheri Huber

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4168 (Number of characters: 98):
There is Nothing Wrong with You {Great book for overcoming shame
and cultivating self-compassion.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4169 (Number of characters: 139):
Christine Lawson
Understanding The Borderline Mother {Healing from having a
borderline or narcissistic mother; explores 5 different types.}

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4170 (Number of characters: 259):
Elan Golomb
Trapped in The Mirror {Healing from having a narcissistic parent.}
John Gottman
The Seven Principles of Making Marriage Work

how helpful they have been to enhancing recovery. My friends and clients whose recovery progresses at the greatest rate are those who
supplement their therapy with self-help activities.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4175 (Number of characters: 169):

around or post them in a conspicuous place until they are deeply ingrained seem to take a
quantum leap in their recovery.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4176 (Number of characters: 141):

that I have seen so many others receive from them.

chunk 4190 (Number of characters: 97):
Conclusion
In conclusion, you progress in recovering from the multidimensional wounding of Cptsd:

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4191 (Number of characters: 71):
[1] as increasing mindfulness decreases your unconscious 4F acting out,

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4192 (Number of characters: 27):
[2] as your critic shrinks,

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4193 (Number of characters: 45):
[3] as your brain becomes more user-friendly,

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4194 (Number of characters: 135):
[4] as grieving your childhood losses builds your emotional intelligence,
[5] as your body relaxes and your mind becomes more peaceful,

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4195 (Number of characters: 135):
[5] as your healthy ego matures into a healthy sense of self,
[6] as your life narrative becomes self-compassionate and self-affirming,

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4196 (Number of characters: 81):
[7] as your emotional vulnerability creates authentic experiences of intimacy and

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4197 (Number of characters: 52):
[8] as a you attain “good enough” safe relationship.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4198 (Number of characters: 81):
And let me reemphasize once again that recovery is not an all-or-none phenomenon.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4199 (Number of characters: 157):
It is a
gradual process marked by ongoing growth in any of these arenas, and most especially in a
decreasing frequency, intensity and duration of flashbacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4200 (Number of characters: 132):
I hope and pray that much sooner than later you will experience an increasing access to the silver
linings I described in chapter 4.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4201 (Number of characters: 70):
I hope you sense the ongoing resolution of your developmental
arrests.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4202 (Number of characters: 111):
I hope you will notice an increasing kindness to yourself and a pride in the beautiful

uniqueness of yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4203 (Number of characters: 121):
I hope you become as fierce in your allegiance to yourself as you need to
be to feel that you safely belong to the world.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4204 (Number of characters: 207):
I further hope that the benefits of your improved
emotional intelligence will bring you at least one intimate relationship where you can ongoingly
discover the benefits of safe and multidimensional relating.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4292 (Number of characters: 138):
TOOLBOX 3
SUGGESTED INTERNAL
RESPONSES TO COMMON
CRITIC ATTACKS
The attacks of the critic often operate below the radar of self-awareness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4293 (Number of characters: 84):
Unless we can identify
them, we are at their mercy and helpless to deconstruct them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4294 (Number of characters: 166):
Once we learn to recognize inner
critic attacks, the simple techniques of Thought-Stopping and Thought-Substitution are powerful
tools in short-circuiting the critic.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4295 (Number of characters: 36):
There are two categories of attacks.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4296 (Number of characters: 93):
Perfectionism attacks, fueled by toxic shame, create
chronic self-hate and self-flagellation.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4297 (Number of characters: 80):
Endangerment attacks, fueled by fear, create chronic
hypervigilance and anxiety.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4298 (Number of characters: 166):
PERFECTIONISM ATTACKS
1. Perfectionism. My perfectionism arose as an attempt to gain safety and support in my
dangerous family. Perfection is a self-persecutory myth.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4299 (Number of characters: 63):
I do not have to be perfect to be safe or
loved in the present.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4300 (Number of characters: 57):
I am letting go of relationships that require perfection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4301 (Number of characters: 67):
I have a right to
make mistakes. Mistakes do not make me a mistake.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4302 (Number of characters: 106):
Every mistake or mishap is an opportunity
to practice loving myself in the places I have never been loved.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4303 (Number of characters: 42):
2. All-or-None & Black-and-White Thinking.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4304 (Number of characters: 75):
I reject extreme or over generalized descriptions,
judgments or criticisms.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4305 (Number of characters: 98):
Statements that describe me as “always” or “never” this or that, are
typically grossly inaccurate.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4306 (Number of characters: 41):
3. Self-Hate, Self-Disgust & Toxic Shame.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4307 (Number of characters: 19):
I commit to myself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4308 (Number of characters: 16):
I am on my side.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4309 (Number of characters: 26):
I am a good
enough person.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4310 (Number of characters: 25):
I refuse to trash myself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4311 (Number of characters: 243):
I turn shame back into blame and disgust and externalize
it to anyone who shames my normal feelings and foibles. As long as I am not hurting anyone, I
refuse to be shamed for normal emotional responses like anger, sadness, fear and depression.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4312 (Number of characters: 100):
I
especially refuse to attack myself for how hard it is to completely eliminate the self-hate habit.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4313 (Number of characters: 2):
4.

chunk 4384 (Number of characters: 180):
TOOLBOX 4
TOOLS FOR LOVINGLY
RESOLVING CONFLICT
This is a list of techniques and perspectives I’ve gathered over the years to help couples resolve
conflict as lovingly as possible.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4385 (Number of characters: 221):
When I give it to couples that I work with, I ask them to take
time at home to read it aloud together and to discuss each one as much as necessary to see if they
can agree to adopt it as a guideline for handling conflict.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4386 (Number of characters: 144):
When I first got together with my wife eleven years ago, we spent considerable time on a
weekend trip discussing these guidelines one at a time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4387 (Number of characters: 78):
We aired our concerns, enthusiasms,
caveats and reservations about using them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4388 (Number of characters: 175):
Over subsequent years, we refined our usage of them,
and have evolved a communication style around our conflicts that has helped to keep our
intimacy healthy and ever growing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4389 (Number of characters: 75):
1. Normalize the inevitability of conflict & establish a safe forum for it.

chunk 4434 (Number of characters: 135):
More on Timeouts, #16
Two of the most common reasons that relationships break up is irreconcilable differences and
irreparable damages.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4435 (Number of characters: 99):
The latter could have been prevented in many cases if couples knew how to
use timeouts judiciously.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4436 (Number of characters: 160):
This is especially true for fight-type trauma survivors, who when flashing back, can easily
lose control to the outer critic and say intimacy-destroying things.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4437 (Number of characters: 178):
Survivors benefit greatly from
learning to recognize the signs of being over-activated so that they can then take timeouts to stop
the bleeding caused by a critic on the rampage.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4438 (Number of characters: 133):
Things said in the heat of a flashback can wound deeply and engrave themselves in the
psyche of the other in ways that cripple trust.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4439 (Number of characters: 276):
So much of this needless intimacy-destruction will
be prevented if both members of the couple agree that either of them can call a timeout whenever
they feel too triggered to be lovingly confrontive, or are experiencing the other as flashing back
into being overly aggressive.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4440 (Number of characters: 304):
Timeouts can range from one minute to 24 hours depending on how long it takes either or
both partners to achieve good enough flashback management. Timeouts work best when the person calling them nominates a time to resume conflict
resolution, so that timeouts do not become techniques for dodging issues.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4441 (Number of characters: 78):
Timeouts can be used individually as a time to release any accumulated charge.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4442 (Number of characters: 122):
This can be
done by using the safe “angering out” techniques I describe in chapter 5 of my book, The Tao of
Fully Feeling.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4443 (Number of characters: 2):
2.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4444 (Number of characters: 31):
More on Transference, #19 & #20

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4445 (Number of characters: 155):
In using this list with couples, I notice that those who are most skilled in conflict resolution, have
achieved significant skill with steps 19 through 21.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4446 (Number of characters: 54):
These steps are about learning to handle
transference.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4447 (Number of characters: 166):
For trauma survivors, transference is often a type of flashback whereby we unconsciously
react to our significant others as though they were our childhood caretakers.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4448 (Number of characters: 97):
When this occurs,

we displace onto them a great deal of our unresolved childhood emotional pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4449 (Number of characters: 204):
One common example of this occurs when a partner’s fair and minor complaint triggers a
torrent of rage, fear and/or shame that is left over from decades of a parent’s overwhelming and
rejecting criticism.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4450 (Number of characters: 162):
Another instance of this occurs when her failure to say what he was hoping to hear stirs up
the pain of decades of his aloof, detached mother or father’s neglect.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4451 (Number of characters: 58):
All gender combinations
can of course fall into this trap.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4452 (Number of characters: 165):
The composition of most conflicts that I witness in my office eventually seems to be
approximately 90% re-experienced pain from the past and 10% actual current pain.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4453 (Number of characters: 176):
Harville
Hendrix’s
Getting The Love You Want, is a wonderful guide for working through this dynamic in a
way that heals childhood wounds and enhances intimacy at the same time.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4454 (Number of characters: 196):
In my experience, the vast majority of conflicts between consenting adults involve a
dynamic where both people play a part and have some responsibility for a disruption in their
loving connection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4455 (Number of characters: 154):
Truly healing resolutions to conflict typically occur when each partner owns their part and
expresses an apology about their contribution to the conflict.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4456 (Number of characters: 93):
For deep level resolution this
usually includes an apologetic reference to your transference.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4457 (Number of characters: 125):
A good apology sounds something
like this of this: “I’m sorry for the amount of charge I had in expressing my disappointment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4458 (Number of characters: 94):
While I believe I have a fair complaint, the intensity with which I expressed it was too much.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4459 (Number of characters: 77):
I’m
sorry I responded to you as if you were my constantly withholding mother.

--------------------------------------------------

TOOLBOX 6
I am ending this book with a reiteration of the most essential principles of Cptsd recovering.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4492 (Number of characters: 61):

chunk 4493 (Number of characters: 108):

you more significantly than when you first read them back in chapter 8.

chunk 4494 (Number of characters: 35):
13 STEPS FOR MANAGING FLASHBACKS
1.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4495 (Number of characters: 43):
Say to yourself: “I am having a flashback”.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4496 (Number of characters: 138):
Flashbacks take you into a timeless part
of the psyche that feels as helpless, hopeless and surrounded by danger as you were in
childhood.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4497 (Number of characters: 92):
The feelings and sensations you are experiencing are past memories that
cannot hurt you now.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4498 (Number of characters: 58):
2. Remind yourself: “I feel afraid but I am not in danger!

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4499 (Number of characters: 120):
I am safe now, here in the
present.” Remember you are now in the safety of the present, far from the danger of
the past.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4500 (Number of characters: 42):
3. Own your right/need to have boundaries.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4501 (Number of characters: 141):
Remind yourself that you do not have to
allow anyone to mistreat you; you are free to leave dangerous situations and protest
unfair behavior.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4502 (Number of characters: 41):
4. Speak reassuringly to the Inner Child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4503 (Number of characters: 148):
The child needs to know that you love
her/him unconditionally– that s/he can come to you for comfort and protection when
s/he feels lost and scared.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4504 (Number of characters: 2):
5.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4505 (Number of characters: 30):
Deconstruct eternity thinking.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4506 (Number of characters: 82):
In childhood, fear and abandonment felt endless – a
safer future was unimaginable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4507 (Number of characters: 58):
Remember this flashback will pass as it always has
before.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4508 (Number of characters: 128):
6. Remind yourself that you are in an adult body with allies, skills and resources to
protect you that you never had as a child.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4509 (Number of characters: 56):
[Feeling small and fragile is a sign of a
flashback.]
7.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4510 (Number of characters: 25):
Ease back into your body.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4511 (Number of characters: 68):
Fear launches you into “heady” worrying, or numbing and
spacing out.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4512 (Number of characters: 108):
[a] Gently ask your body to Relax: feel each of your major muscle groups and softly
encourage them to relax.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4513 (Number of characters: 60):
[Tightened muscles send false danger signals to your
brain.]

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4514 (Number of characters: 30):
[b] Breathe deeply and slowly.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4515 (Number of characters: 42):
[Holding your breath also signals danger.]

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4516 (Number of characters: 67):
[c] Slow down: rushing presses your brain’s flight response button.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4517 (Number of characters: 177):
[d] Find a safe place to unwind and soothe yourself: wrap yourself in a blanket, hold
a pillow or a stuffed animal, lie down on your bed or in a closet or in a bath;
take a nap.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4518 (Number of characters: 91):
[e] Feel the fear in your body without reacting to it. Fear is just an energy in your
body.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4519 (Number of characters: 45):
It cannot hurt you if you do not run from it.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4520 (Number of characters: 62):
8. Resist the Inner Critic’s Drasticizing and Catastrophizing.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4521 (Number of characters: 135):
[a] Use thought-stopping to halt the critic’s endless exaggerations of danger, and its
constant planning to control the uncontrollable.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4522 (Number of characters: 42):
Refuse to shame, hate or
abandon yourself.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4523 (Number of characters: 90):
Channel the anger of self- attack into saying “NO” to your
critic’s unfair self-criticism.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4524 (Number of characters: 142):
[b] Use Thought-substitution & Thought-correction to replace negative thinking
with your memorized list of your qualities and accomplishments.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4525 (Number of characters: 28):
9. Allow yourself to grieve.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4526 (Number of characters: 97):
Flashbacks are opportunities to release old, unexpressed
feelings of fear, hurt, and abandonment.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4527 (Number of characters: 82):
Validate and soothe your child’s past
experience of helplessness and hopelessness.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4528 (Number of characters: 94):
Healthy grieving can turn your tears into
self-compassion and your anger into self-protection.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4529 (Number of characters: 50):
10. Cultivate safe relationships and seek support.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4530 (Number of characters: 66):
Take time alone when you need it, but
don’t let shame isolate you.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4531 (Number of characters: 44):
Feeling shame doesn’t mean you are shameful.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4532 (Number of characters: 101):
Educate
your intimates about flashbacks and ask them to help you talk and feel your way
through them.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4533 (Number of characters: 3):
11.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4534 (Number of characters: 64):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4535 (Number of characters: 72):

chunk 4536 (Number of characters: 96):
Practice preventive maintenance
with these steps when triggering situations are unavoidable.
12.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4537 (Number of characters: 41):

chunk 4538 (Number of characters: 104):

chunk 4539 (Number of characters: 108):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4540 (Number of characters: 3):
13.

chunk 4541 (Number of characters: 40):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4542 (Number of characters: 166):

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4543 (Number of characters: 48):
Real recovery is a gradually progressive process

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4544 (Number of characters: 76):
[often two steps forward, one step back], not an attained salvation fantasy.

--------------------------------------------------

chunk 4545 (Number of characters: 46):
Don’t beat
yourself up for having a flashback.
